Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Transportation Code
====================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 1 - Department of Transportation Administration Act
********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-101(1): This title is known as the "Transportation Code."
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-101(2): This chapter is known as the "Department of Transportation Administration Act."


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this title:Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1): "Circulator alley" means a publicly owned passageway:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(a): with a right-of-way width of 20 feet or greater;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(b): located within a master planned community;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(c): established by the city having jurisdictional authority as part of the street network for traffic circulation that may also be used for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(c)(i): garbage collection;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(c)(ii): access to residential garages; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(c)(iii): access rear entrances to a commercial establishment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(1)(d): constructed with a bituminous or concrete pavement surface.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(2): 72-1-301 "Commission" means the Transportation Commission created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(3): "Construction" means the construction, reconstruction, replacement, and improvement of the highways, including the acquisition of rights-of-way and material sites.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(4): 72-1-201 "Department" means the Department of Transportation created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(5): 72-1-202 "Executive director" means the executive director of the department appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(6): 41-1a-102 "Farm tractor" has the meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(7): "Federal aid primary highway" means that portion of connected main highways located within this state officially designated by the department and approved by the United States Secretary of Transportation under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(8): 59-12-102 "Fixed guideway" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(9): 11-59-201
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(9)(a): "Fixed guideway capital development" means a project to construct or reconstruct a public transit fixed guideway facility that will add capacity to a fixed guideway public transit facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(9)(b): 11-59-201 "Fixed guideway capital development" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(9)(b)(i): a project to strategically double track commuter rail lines; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(9)(b)(ii): 11-59-201 a project to develop and construct public transit facilities and related infrastructure pertaining to the Point of the Mountain State Land Authority created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(10): 17C-1-102 "Greenfield" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(11): "Highway" means any public road, street, alley, lane, court, place, viaduct, tunnel, culvert, bridge, or structure laid out or erected for public use, or dedicated or abandoned to the public, or made  public in an action for the partition of real property, including the entire area within the right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(12): "Highway authority" means the department or the legislative, executive, or governing body of a county or municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(13): 63N-3-602 "Housing and transit reinvestment zone" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(14): 41-1a-102 "Implement of husbandry" has the meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(15): "Interstate system" means any highway officially designated by the department and included as part of the national interstate and defense highways, as provided in the Federal Aid Highway Act of 1956 and any supplemental acts or amendments.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(16): 17B-2a-802 "Large public transit district" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(17): "Limited-access facility" means a highway especially designated for through traffic, and over, from, or to which neither owners nor occupants of abutting lands nor other persons have any right or easement, or have only a limited right or easement of access, light, air, or view.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(18): "Master planned community" means a land use development:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(18)(a): designated by the city as a master planned community; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(18)(b): comprised of a single development agreement for a development larger than 500 acres.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(19): 41-1a-102 "Motor vehicle" has the same meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(20): 10-1-104 "Municipality" has the same meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(21): "National highway systems highways" means that portion of connected main highways located within this state officially designated by the department and approved by the United States Secretary of Transportation under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(22): 72-9-501
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(22)(a): 72-9-501 "Port-of-entry" means a fixed or temporary facility constructed, operated, and maintained by the department where drivers, vehicles, and vehicle loads are checked or inspected for compliance with state and federal laws as specified in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(22)(b): "Port-of-entry" includes inspection and checking stations and weigh stations.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(23): 72-9-501 "Port-of-entry agent" means a person employed at a port-of-entry to perform the duties specified in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(24): 17B-2a-802 "Public transit" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(25): "Public transit facility" means a fixed guideway, transit vehicle, transit station, depot, passenger loading or unloading zone, parking lot, or other facility:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(25)(a): leased by or operated by or on behalf of a public transit district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(25)(b): related to the public transit services provided by the district, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(25)(b)(i): railway or other right-of-way;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(25)(b)(ii): railway line; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(25)(b)(iii): a reasonable area immediately adjacent to a designated stop on a route traveled by a transit vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(26): "Right-of-way" means real property or an interest in real property, usually in a strip, acquired for or devoted to state transportation purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(27): "Sealed" does not preclude acceptance of electronically sealed and submitted bids or proposals in addition to bids or proposals manually sealed and submitted.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(28): 41-1a-102 "Semitrailer" has the meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(29): "SR" means state route and has the same meaning as state highway as defined in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(30): Title 72, Chapter 4, Designation of State Highways Act "State highway" means those highways designated as state highways in
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(31): 72-5-102 "State transportation purposes" has the meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(32): "State transportation systems" means all streets, alleys, roads, highways, pathways, and thoroughfares of any kind, including connected structures, airports, aerial corridor infrastructure, spaceports, public transit facilities, and all other modes and forms of conveyance used by the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(33): 41-1a-102 "Trailer" has the meaning set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(34): 11-13-227 "Transportation reinvestment zone" means a transportation reinvestment zone created pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-102(35): 41-1a-102 "Truck tractor" has the meaning set forth in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201 Creation of Department of Transportation -- Functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; 63G-22-102; Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements; 53-8-103 There is created the Department of Transportation which shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(a): have the general responsibility for planning, research, design, construction, maintenance, security, and safety of state transportation systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(b): provide administration for state transportation systems and programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(c): implement the transportation policies of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(d): plan, develop, construct, and maintain state transportation systems that are safe, reliable, environmentally sensitive, and serve the needs of the traveling public, commerce, and industry;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(e): establish standards and procedures regarding the technical details of administration of the state transportation systems as established by statute and administrative rule;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(f): advise the governor and the Legislature about state transportation systems needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(g): coordinate with utility companies for the reasonable, efficient, and cost-effective installation, maintenance, operation, relocation, and upgrade of utilities within state highway rights-of-way;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(h): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(i): jointly with the commission annually report to the Transportation Interim Committee, by November 30 of each year, as to the operation, maintenance, condition, mobility, safety needs, and wildlife and livestock mitigation for state transportation systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(j): 63G-22-102; Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements ensure that any training or certification required of a public official or public employee, as those terms are defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(j)(i): under this title;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(j)(ii): by the department; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(j)(iii): by an agency or division within the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(k): study and make recommendations to the Legislature on potential managed lane use and implementation on selected transportation systems within the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(l): 53-8-103 before July 1 of each year, coordinate with the Utah Highway Patrol Division created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(l)(i): future highway projects that will add additional capacity to the state transportation system;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(l)(ii): potential changes in law enforcement responsibilities due to future highway projects; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(1)(l)(iii): incident management services on state highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(2)(a): The department shall exercise reasonable care in designing, constructing, and maintaining a state highway in a reasonably safe condition for travel.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(2)(b): (2)(a) Nothing in this section shall be construed as:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(2)(b)(i): creating a private right of action; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-201(2)(b)(ii): (2)(a) expanding or changing the department's common law duty as described in Subsection

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(1)(a): The governor, with the advice and consent of the Senate, shall appoint an executive director to be the chief executive officer of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(1)(b): The executive director shall be a registered professional engineer and qualified executive with technical and administrative experience and training appropriate for the position.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(1)(c): The executive director shall remain in office until a successor is appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(1)(d): The executive director may be removed by the governor.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(2)(a): have responsibility for the administrative supervision of the state transportation systems and the various operations of the department;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(2)(h): have responsibility for administrative supervision of the Comptroller Division, the Internal Audit Division, and the Communications Division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(2)(i): appoint assistants, to serve at the discretion of the executive director, to administer the divisions of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-202(3): The executive director may employ other assistants and advisers as the executive director finds necessary and fix salaries in accordance with the salary standards adopted by the Division of Human Resource Management.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204 Divisions enumerated -- Duties.
--------------------------------------------------------------
In addition to divisions created by the department necessary to administer the areas of responsibility of the deputy directors as described in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(1): the Comptroller Division responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(1)(a): all financial aspects of the department, including budgeting, accounting, and contracting;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(1)(b): providing all material data and documentation necessary for effective fiscal planning and programming; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(1)(c): procuring administrative supplies;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(2): the Internal Audit Division responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(2)(a): conducting and verifying all internal audits and reviews within the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(2)(b): performing financial and compliance audits to determine the allowability and reasonableness of proposals, accounting records, and final costs of consultants, contractors, utility companies, and other entities used by the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(2)(c): implementing audit procedures that meet or exceed generally accepted auditing standards relating to revenues, expenditures, and funding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(3): the Communications Division responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(3)(a): developing, managing, and implementing the department's public hearing processes and programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(3)(b): responding to public complaints, requests, and input;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(3)(c): assisting the divisions and regions in the department's public involvement programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(3)(d): developing and managing internal department communications; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-204(3)(e): managing and overseeing department media relations.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205 Region offices -- Region directors -- Qualifications -- Responsibilities.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205(1): The department shall maintain region offices throughout the state as the executive director finds reasonable and necessary for the efficient carrying out of the duties of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205(2)(a): The executive director shall appoint a region director for each region.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205(2)(b): Each region director shall be a qualified executive with technical and administrative experience and training.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205(3): The executive director shall establish the responsibilities of each region director.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-205(4): The executive director may also establish district offices within a region to implement maintenance, encroachment, safety, community involvement, and loss management functions of the region.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207 Department may sue and be sued -- Legal adviser of department -- Partial waiver of Eleventh Amendment immunity.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(1): The department may sue, and it may be sued only on written contracts made by it or under its authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(2): The department may sue in the name of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(3): In all matters requiring legal advice in the performance of its duties and in the prosecution or defense of any action growing out of the performance of its duties, the attorney general is the legal adviser of the commission, and the department, and shall perform any and all legal services required by the commission and the department without other compensation than his salary.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(4): Chapter 9, Motor Carrier Safety Act Upon request of the department, the attorney general shall aid in any investigation, hearing, or trial under the provisions of
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5): (5); (5)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5)(a): The state waives its immunity under the 11th Amendment of the United States Constitution and consents to suit in a federal court for lawsuits arising out of the department's compliance, discharge, or enforcement of responsibilities assumed pursuant to 23 U.S.C. Secs. 326 and 327.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5)(b): (5); (5)(b)(i) The waiver of immunity under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5)(b)(i): the executive director or the executive director's designee executes a memorandum of understanding with the United States Department of Transportation accepting the jurisdiction of the federal courts as required by 23 U.S.C. Secs. 326(c) and 327(c);
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5)(b)(ii): (5)(b)(i) before execution of the memorandum of understanding under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5)(b)(iii): the act or omission that is the subject of the lawsuit arises out of or relates to compliance, discharge, or enforcement of responsibilities assumed by the department pursuant to 23 U.S.C. Secs. 326 and 327; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-207(5)(b)(iv): the memorandum of understanding is in effect when the act or omission that is the subject of the federal lawsuit occurred.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208 Cooperation with counties, cities, towns, the federal government, and all state departments -- Inspection of work done by a public transit district.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208(1): The department shall cooperate with the counties, cities, towns, and community reinvestment agencies in the construction, maintenance, and use of the highways and in all related matters, and may provide services to the counties, cities, towns, and community reinvestment agencies on terms mutually agreed upon.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208(2): The department, with the approval of the governor, shall cooperate with the federal government in all federal-aid projects and with all state departments in all matters in connection with the use of the highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208(3): Title 17B, Chapter 2a, Part 8, Public Transit District Act The department:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208(3)(a): Title 17B, Chapter 2a, Part 8, Public Transit District Act shall inspect all work done by a public transit district under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208(3)(b): may make further additions or changes necessary for the purpose of safety to employees and the general public.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5 Definition -- Cooperation with metropolitan planning organizations -- Cooperation in plans and programs required.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(1): As used in this section, "metropolitan planning organization" means an organization established under 23 U.S.C. Sec. 134.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(2): The department shall cooperate with a metropolitan planning organization in the metropolitan planning organization's responsibility to carry out a continuing, cooperative, and comprehensive process for transportation planning and project programming.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(3): If a metropolitan planning organization has a contiguous boundary with another metropolitan planning organization, the department shall cooperate with those organizations if the metropolitan planning organizations have:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(3)(a): coordinated project priorities, transportation plans, and transportation improvement programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(3)(b): submitted joint priorities, plans, and programs to the department as comprehensive, integrated transportation plans.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(4): (3) Subject to the provisions of 23 U.S.C. Sec. 134, if the governor and the affected local units of government jointly determine that metropolitan planning organizations have failed to meet the guidelines under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5): 35A-4-312(5)(e); (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5)(a): 35A-4-312(5)(e) A metropolitan planning organization is a governmental agency that is eligible to receive employment information from the Unemployment Insurance Division in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5)(b): (5)(a) Information obtained under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5)(b)(i): name;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5)(b)(ii): worksite address;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5)(b)(iii): industrial classification; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-208.5(5)(b)(iv): number of employees.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-209 Department to cooperate in programs relating to scenic centers.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall cooperate in planning and promoting road-building programs into the scenic centers of the state and in providing camping grounds and facilities in scenic centers for tourists with:Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-209(1): the Governor's Office of Economic Opportunity;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-209(2): other states;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-209(3): all national, state, and local planning and zoning agencies and boards;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-209(4): municipal and county officials; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-209(5): other agencies.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-210 Department to be assisted by faculties and personnel of universities.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The engineering machinery and apparatus and the force of mechanics and instructors in the University of Utah and Utah State University are at the disposal of the department, and any faculty member of the institutions shall furnish any information or assistance desired upon request of the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1 Road usage charge program.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1): 41-1a-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(a): "Account manager" means an entity under contract with the department to administer and manage the road usage charge program.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b): 41-1a-102 "Alternative fuel vehicle" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b)(i): 41-1a-102 an electric motor vehicle as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b)(ii): a motor vehicle powered exclusively by a fuel other than:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b)(ii)(A): motor fuel;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b)(ii)(B): diesel fuel;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b)(ii)(C): natural gas; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(b)(ii)(D): propane.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(c): "Payment period" means the interval during which an owner is required to report mileage and pay the appropriate road usage charge according to the terms of the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(d): "Program" means the road usage charge program established and described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(e): "Road usage charge cap" means the maximum fee charged to a participant in the program for a registration period.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(1)(f): "Road usage charge rate" means the per-mile usage fee charged to a participant in the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(2): There is established a road usage charge program as described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(3)(a): The department shall implement and oversee the administration of the program, which shall begin on January 1, 2020.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(3)(b): To implement and administer the program, the department may contract with an account manager.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(4): 41-1a-1206(1)(h); (2)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(4)(a): The owner or lessee of an alternative fuel vehicle may apply for enrollment of the alternative fuel vehicle in the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-213.1(4)(b): 41-1a-1206(1)(h); (2)(b) If an application for enrollment into the program is approved by the department, the owner or lessee of an alternative fuel vehicle may participate in the program in lieu of paying the fee described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214 Department designated as state safety oversight agency for rail fixed guideway public transportation safety -- Powers and duties -- Rulemaking.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(1): (1)(b); 59-12-102
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(1)(a): (1)(b); 59-12-102 Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(1)(b): For purposes of this section, "fixed guideway" does not include a rail system subject to regulation by the Federal Railroad Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(2): The department is designated as the state safety oversight agency for rail fixed guideway public transportation safety in accordance with 49 U.S.C. Sec. 5329(e)(4).
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3): As the state safety oversight agency, the department may, to the extent necessary to fulfill the department's obligations under federal law:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(a): enter into and inspect the property of a fixed guideway rail system receiving federal funds without prior notice to the operator;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(b): audit an operator of a fixed guideway rail system receiving federal funds for compliance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(b)(i): federal and state laws regarding the safety of the fixed guideway rail system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(b)(ii): a public transportation agency safety plan adopted by a specific operator in accordance with 49 U.S.C. Sec. 5329(d);
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(c): direct the operator of a fixed guideway rail system to correct a safety hazard by a specified date and time;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(d): prevent the operation of all or part of a fixed guideway rail system that the department has determined to be unsafe;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(e): audit, review, approve, and oversee an operator of a fixed guideway rail system receiving federal funds for compliance with a plan adopted by the operator in compliance with 49 U.S.C. Sec. 5329(d); and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(3)(f): enforce statutes, rules, regulations, and executive orders relating to the operation of a fixed guideway rail public transportation system in Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(4): The department shall, at least annually, provide a status report on the safety of the rail fixed guideway public transportation systems the department oversees to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(4)(a): the Federal Transit Administration;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(4)(b): the governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(4)(c): members of the board of any rail fixed guideway public transportation system that the department oversees in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-214(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (5)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-215 Affordable housing study.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-215(1): As used in this section, "moderate income housing unit" means a housing unit that has an appraised value that would allow, as estimated by the department, a household whose income is no more than 80% of the area median income to occupy the housing unit paying no more than 30% of the household's income for gross housing costs, including utilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-215(2): 35A-8-2201 On or before September 15, the department shall provide a written report to the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee and to the Commission on Housing Affordability created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-215(2)(a): the total number of housing units that were permanently vacated or destroyed as a result of department action in the previous fiscal year, including separate subtotals describing the total number of housing units with one bedroom, two bedrooms, three bedrooms, and four or more bedrooms, which were permanently vacated or destroyed as a result of department action in the previous fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-215(2)(b): the total number of moderate income housing units that were permanently vacated or destroyed as a result of department action in the previous fiscal year, including separate subtotals describing the total number of moderate income housing units with one bedroom, two bedrooms, three bedrooms, and four or more bedrooms, which were permanently vacated or destroyed as a result of department action in the previous fiscal year.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216 Statewide electric vehicle charging network plan -- Report.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1): 19-1-104; 63A-5b-301; 79-6-401; 79-2-201
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1)(a): The department, in consultation with relevant entities in the private sector, shall develop a statewide electric vehicle charging network plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1)(b): 19-1-104; 63A-5b-301; 79-6-401; 79-2-201 To develop the statewide electric vehicle charging network plan, the department shall consult with political subdivisions and other relevant state agencies, divisions, and entities, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1)(b)(i): 19-1-104 the Department of Environmental Quality created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1)(b)(ii): 63A-5b-301 the Division of Facilities Construction and Management created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1)(b)(iii): 79-6-401 the Office of Energy Development created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(1)(b)(iv): 79-2-201 the Department of Natural Resources created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(2): The statewide electric vehicle charging network plan shall provide implementation strategies to ensure that electric vehicle charging stations are available:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(2)(a): at strategic locations as determined by the department by June 30, 2021;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(2)(b): at incremental distances no greater than every 50 miles along the state's interstate highway system by December 31, 2025; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(2)(c): along other major highways within the state as the department finds appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-1-216(3): The department shall provide a report before November 30, 2020, to the Transportation Interim Committee to outline the statewide electric vehicle charging network plan.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 2 - Transportation Finances Act
************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Transportation Finances Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-102 Transportation Fund.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-102(1): There is created a fund entitled the "Transportation Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-102(2): Transportation Fund money shall be used exclusively for highway purposes as provided in this title.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103 Limitations on Transportation Fund appropriations to agencies not a part of the Department of Transportation -- Exceptions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(1): (2) Except as provided under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(1)(a): the Department of Public Safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(1)(b): the State Tax Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(1)(c): the Division of Finance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(1)(d): any other state agency that is not a part of the Department of Transportation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(2): (1); 53-3-106; 41-1a-1218; 41-1a-1219; 53-3-905 The following amounts are exempt from the appropriation and transfer limitations of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(2)(a): 53-3-106 amounts deposited in the Department of Public Safety Restricted Account created under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-103(2)(d): 53-3-905 revenue generated by the Motorcycle Rider Education Program under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-104 Budget.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-104(1): The department shall prepare and submit to the governor, to be included in his budget to be submitted to the Legislature, a budget of the requirements for the operation of the department for the fiscal year following the convening of the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-104(2): This budget shall be so separated, in relation to the various functions of the department, so as to allow the separate determination of funds for deposit into the Transportation Fund and into any other special funds which are required by law to be utilized for specific purposes and which are separately maintained by the department for those purposes.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-105 Budgetary accounts within Transportation Fund -- Disposition of unexpended balances.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-105(1): The amount designated by the Legislature, out of which the items budgeted shall be paid, shall be established in appropriation and allotment accounts within the Transportation Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-105(2): At the close of the biennium all unexpended balances remaining in the accounts so budgeted shall be closed to the fund balance account of the Transportation Fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-106 Appropriation and transfers from Transportation Fund.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-106(1): On and after July 1, 1981, there is appropriated from the Transportation Fund to the use of the department an amount equal to two-elevenths of the taxes collected from the motor fuel tax and the special fuel tax, exclusive of the formula amount appropriated for class B and class C roads, to be used for highway rehabilitation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-106(2): 72-2-124 For a fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2016, the Division of Finance shall annually transfer an amount equal to the amount of revenue generated by a tax imposed on motor and special fuel that is sold, used, or received for sale or used in this state at a rate of 1.8 cents per gallon to the Transportation Investment Fund of 2005 created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-106(3): 72-2-124 For a fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2019, the Division of Finance shall annually transfer to the Transportation Investment Fund of 2005 created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-106(4): 59-12-103(7)(c); (2); (3) For purposes of the calculation described in Subsection

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-107(1)(f): any other amounts appropriated or transferred for any other state agencies not a part of the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-107(3): Each quarter of every year the department shall make the necessary accounting entries to transfer the money appropriated under this section for class B and class C roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-107(4): The funds appropriated for class B and class C roads shall be expended under the direction of the department as the Legislature shall provide.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-108(1)(d)(i): the width of the road; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-108(1)(d)(ii): the number of lanes into which the road is divided.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-109 Rules for uniform accounting -- Apportionment and use of class B and class C road funds -- Compliance with federal-aid provisions -- Duties of department.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-109(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-109(2): The department shall cooperate with the county governing bodies and the governing officials of the cities and towns in the apportionment and use of class B and C road funds.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-110 Funds allocated to class B and class C roads -- Matching federal funds -- R.S. 2477 rights.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A county or municipality may:Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-110(1): use funds which are allocated to class B and class C roads for matching federal funds for the construction of secondary roads now available or which may later become available in accordance with the provisions of law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-110(2): use up to 30% of the class B and class C road funds allocated to the county or municipality to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-110(2)(a): pay the costs of asserting, defending, or litigating local government rights under R.S. 2477 on class B, class C, or class D roads; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-110(2)(b): maintain class D roads.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111 Assent to federal acts on federal aid for highway purposes -- Department to represent state -- Pledge of funds -- Rulemaking authority -- Contracts for energy conservation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(a): The Legislature assents to all the provisions of Title 23, Highways, U.S.C., relating to federal aid for highway purposes, and all amendatory acts.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(b): The department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(b)(i): enter into a contract or agreement with the United States government relating to the survey, construction, and maintenance of highways under a federal act;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(b)(ii): submit a scheme or program of construction and maintenance required by a federal agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(b)(iii): do any other thing necessary to fully carry out the cooperation contemplated and provided for by a federal act.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(c): The good faith of the state is pledged to make available sufficient funds to match the sums apportioned to the state by the United States government:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(c)(i): for the construction of federal-aid highways; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(1)(c)(ii): to provide adequate maintenance for federal-aid highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-111(3): The department may contract with individuals, associations, or corporations to accomplish energy conservation and encouragement of car and van pooling.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112 Transportation department authorized to participate in federal program -- Prohibition against spending certain transportation funds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(1): Notwithstanding any law to the contrary, the department is empowered to participate in the deferred payment program authorized by Congress in Public Law 94-30.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(2): Any indebtedness incurred by the department under this section shall be paid from state transportation funds as appropriated.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(3): (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(3)(a): (3) As used in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(3)(a)(i): "Apportioned" means divided or assigned among the states based on a prescribed formula established in 23 U.S.C.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(3)(a)(ii): "Authorization act" means an act of Congress enacted after July 1, 2009 that authorizes transportation programs from the Highway Trust Fund established in 26 U.S.C. Sec. 9503.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-112(3)(b): The state, including any agency, department, or division of the state, may not spend project-specific funds that are allocated through an authorization act for a transportation-related project that is eligible for funds apportioned to the state in support of the statewide transportation improvement program unless the specified project is included on the statewide transportation improvement program.

-----------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-115 Transportation Fund balance -- Income -- Allocation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
All interest and earnings and other income derived from the Transportation Fund balance shall be credited to the Transportation Fund, including the collector road and B and C road accounts in proportion to the various fund account balances on an average monthly balance basis.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-116 Gifts, bequests, and donations part of Transportation Fund -- Expenditure.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-116(1): Gifts, bequests, and donations by individuals, corporations, or societies to the state for road building purposes shall become part of the Transportation Fund, and shall be expended for state highway purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-116(2): Gifts, bequests, or donations made to any county shall be expended under the direction of the county legislative body.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118 Centennial Highway Fund.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(1): 72-2-124 There is created a capital projects fund entitled the Centennial Highway Fund within the Transportation Investment Fund of 2005 created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(2): The account consists of money generated from the following revenue sources:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(2)(a): any voluntary contributions received for the construction, reconstruction, or renovation of state or federal highways; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(2)(b): appropriations made to the fund by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(3)(a): The fund shall earn interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(3)(b): All interest earned on fund money shall be deposited into the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(4): The executive director may use fund money, as prioritized by the Transportation Commission, only to pay the costs of construction, reconstruction, or renovation to state and federal highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(5): (6)(c); 72-2-124 When the highway general obligation bonds have been paid off and the highway projects completed that are intended to be paid from revenues deposited in the account as determined by the Executive Appropriations Committee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(6)(a): The Division of Finance shall monitor the highway general obligation bonds that are being paid from revenues deposited in the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(6)(b): The department shall monitor the highway construction, reconstruction, or renovation projects that are being paid from revenues deposited in the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(6)(c): The department shall notify the State Tax Commission and the Division of Finance when:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(6)(c)(i): all highway general obligation bonds that are intended to be paid from revenues deposited in the fund have been paid off; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-118(6)(c)(ii): all highway projects that are intended to be paid from revenues deposited in the account have been completed.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120 Tollway Special Revenue Fund -- Revenue.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(1): There is created a special revenue fund within the Transportation Fund known as the "Tollway Special Revenue Fund."
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2): 72-6-118; 72-6-203 The fund shall be funded from the following sources:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2)(a): 72-6-118 tolls collected by the department under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2)(b): 72-6-203 funds received by the department through a tollway development agreement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2)(c): appropriations made to the fund by the Legislature;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2)(d): contributions from other public and private sources for deposit into the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2)(e): interest earnings on cash balances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(2)(f): money collected for repayments and interest on fund money.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(3): 72-6-118 The Division of Finance may create a subaccount for each tollway as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-120(4): The commission may authorize the money deposited into the fund to be spent by the department to establish and operate tollways and related facilities and state transportation systems, including design, construction, reconstruction, operation, maintenance, enforcement, impacts from tollways, and the acquisition of right-of-way.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-123(2): (1) The guidelines described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-123(2)(a): the consideration of factors relevant to a decision to make a program adjustment including the potential to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-123(2)(a)(i): extend department resources to other needed projects;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-123(2)(a)(ii): alleviate significant existing or future congestion or hazards to the traveling public; and

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-132 State Aircraft Restricted Account.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-132(2)(a): fees the department receives for use of state owned aircraft;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-132(2)(c): contributions from other public or private sources for deposit into the account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-132(2)(d): interest earned on money in the account.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-132(3): Upon appropriation by the Legislature, the department may use money in the account for the operation and maintenance of state owned aircraft.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-133(1)(f): 72-2-108 "Road mile" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-133(1)(g): 72-2-108 "Weighted mileage" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-133(3): 41-1a-1201(10) The Rural Transportation Infrastructure Fund shall be funded by:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-133(3)(c): other deposits into the fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-133(5)(a): 50% in the ratio that the class B roads weighted mileage within each county and class C roads weighted mileage within each municipality bear to the total class B and class C roads weighted mileage within the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-133(5)(b): 50% in the ratio that the population of a county or municipality bears to the total population of the state as of the last official federal census or the United States Census Bureau estimate, whichever is most recent, except that if population estimates are not available from the United States Census Bureau, population figures shall be derived from the estimate from the Utah Population Committee.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(1): 72-2-202 "Fund" means the State Infrastructure Bank Fund created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(2): "Infrastructure assistance" means any use of fund money, except an infrastructure loan, to provide financial assistance for transportation projects or publicly owned infrastructure projects, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(2)(a): capital reserves and other security for bond or debt instrument financing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(2)(b): any letters of credit, lines of credit, bond insurance, or loan guarantees obtained by a public entity to finance transportation projects.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(3): "Infrastructure loan" means a loan of fund money to finance a transportation project or publicly owned infrastructure project.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(4): 63H-1-201 "Public entity" means a state agency, county, municipality,  special district, special service district, an intergovernmental entity organized under state law, or the military installation development authority created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(5): "Publicly owned infrastructure project" means a project to improve sewer or water infrastructure that is owned by a public entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6): 11-13-227; Title 63N, Chapter 3, Part 6, Housing and Transit Reinvestment Zone Act "Transportation project":
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(a): 11-13-227; Title 63N, Chapter 3, Part 6, Housing and Transit Reinvestment Zone Act means a project:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(a)(i): to improve a state or local highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(a)(ii): to improve a public transportation facility or nonmotorized transportation facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(a)(iii): to construct or improve parking facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(a)(iv): 11-13-227 that is subject to a transportation reinvestment zone agreement pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(a)(v): Title 63N, Chapter 3, Part 6, Housing and Transit Reinvestment Zone Act that is part of a housing and transit reinvestment zone created pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(b): includes the costs of acquisition, construction, reconstruction, rehabilitation, equipping, and fixturing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(c): may only include a project if the project is part of:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(c)(i): the statewide long range plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(c)(ii): a regional transportation plan of the area metropolitan planning organization if a metropolitan planning organization exists for the area; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-201(6)(c)(iii): a local government general plan or economic development initiative.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202 State Infrastructure Bank Fund -- Creation -- Use of money.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(1): There is created a revolving loan fund entitled the State Infrastructure Bank Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2): (2)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a): (2)(b) The fund consists of money generated from the following revenue sources:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a)(i): appropriations made to the fund by the Legislature;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a)(ii): federal money and grants that are deposited into the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a)(iii): money transferred to the fund by the commission from other money available to the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a)(iv): state grants that are deposited into the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a)(v): contributions or grants from any other private or public sources for deposit into the fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(a)(vi): (2)(b) subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(2)(b): When a loan from the fund is repaid, the department may request and the Legislature may transfer from the fund to the source from which the money originated an amount equal to the repaid loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(3)(a): The fund shall earn interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(3)(b): All interest earned on fund money shall be deposited into the fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(4): Money in the fund shall be used by the department, as prioritized by the commission, only to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(4)(a): provide infrastructure loans or infrastructure assistance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-202(4)(b): pay the department for the costs of administering the fund, providing infrastructure loans or infrastructure assistance, monitoring transportation projects and publicly owned infrastructure projects, and obtaining repayments of infrastructure loans or infrastructure assistance.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203 Loans and assistance -- Authority -- Rulemaking.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(1): Money in the fund may be used by the department, as prioritized by the commission or as directed by the Legislature, to make infrastructure loans or to provide infrastructure assistance to any public entity for any purpose consistent with any applicable constitutional limitation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3): The prioritization process, procedures, and standards for making an infrastructure loan or providing infrastructure assistance may include consideration of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(a): availability of money in the fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(b): credit worthiness of the project;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(c): demonstration that the project will encourage, enhance, or create economic benefits to the state or political subdivision;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(d): likelihood that assistance would enable the project to proceed at an earlier date than would otherwise be possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(e): the extent to which assistance would foster innovative public-private partnerships and attract private debt or equity investment;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(f): demonstration that the project provides a benefit to the state highway system, including safety or mobility improvements;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(g): the amount of proposed assistance as a percentage of the overall project costs with emphasis on local and private participation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(h): demonstration that the project provides intermodal connectivity with public transportation, pedestrian, or nonmotorized transportation facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-203(3)(i): other provisions the commission considers appropriate.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204 Loan program procedures -- Repayment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(1): A public entity may obtain an infrastructure loan from the department, upon approval by the commission, by entering into a loan contract with the department secured by legally issued bonds, notes, or other evidence of indebtedness validly issued under state law, including pledging all or any portion of a revenue source controlled by the public entity to the repayment of the loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(2): A loan or assistance from the fund shall bear interest at a rate not to exceed .5% above bond market interest rates available to the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(3): A loan shall be repaid no later than 15 years from the date the department issues the loan to the borrower, with repayment commencing no later than:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(3)(a): when the project is completed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(3)(b): in the case of a highway project, when the facility has opened to traffic.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(4): (7) The public entity shall repay the infrastructure loan in accordance with the loan contract from any of the following sources:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(4)(a): transportation project or publicly owned infrastructure project revenues, including special assessment revenues;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(4)(b): general funds of the public entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(4)(c): (7) money withheld under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(4)(d): any other legally available revenues.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(5): An infrastructure loan contract with a public entity may provide that a portion of the proceeds of the loan may be applied to fund a reserve fund to secure the repayment of the loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(6): 11-14-316 Before obtaining an infrastructure loan, a county or municipality shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(6)(a): 11-14-316 publish its intention to obtain an infrastructure loan at least once in accordance with the publication of notice requirements under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(6)(b): adopt an ordinance or resolution authorizing the infrastructure loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(7): (7)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(7)(a): If a public entity fails to comply with the terms of its infrastructure loan contract, the department may seek any legal or equitable remedy to obtain compliance or payment of damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(7)(b): If a public entity fails to make infrastructure loan payments when due, the state shall, at the request of the department, withhold an amount of money due to the public entity and deposit the withheld money in the fund to pay the amounts due under the contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(7)(c): (7) The department may elect when to request the withholding of money under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-204(8): 63B-1b-202 All loan contracts, bonds, notes, or other evidence of indebtedness securing the loan contracts shall be held, collected, and accounted for in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-205 Loan contracts of state agencies.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-205(1): 53B-21-113; 63A-1-112
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-205(1)(a): 53B-21-113; 63A-1-112 Notwithstanding Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-205(1)(b): A state agency may contract to repay an infrastructure loan from the money which is appropriated to the agency and may pledge all or any portion of the money to repay the loan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-205(1)(c): A state agency's infrastructure loan may not constitute a debt of the state or lending the credit of the state within the meaning of any constitutional or statutory limitation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-205(2): The terms of an infrastructure loan contract shall bind the state and a state agency, and the state agency shall unconditionally repay the loan from the money the agency has pledged under the terms of the loan contract.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-206 Department authority to contract.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The department may, upon approval of the commission:Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-206(1): make all contracts, execute all instruments, and do all things necessary or convenient to provide financial assistance for transportation projects or publicly owned infrastructure projects in accordance with this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-2-206(2): enter into and perform the contracts and agreements with entities concerning the planning, construction, lease, or other acquisition, installation, or financing of transportation projects or publicly owned infrastructure projects.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 3 - Highway Jurisdiction and Classification Act
****************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Highway Jurisdiction and Classification Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-102 State highways -- Class A state roads.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-102(1): Chapter 4, Designation of State Highways Act State highways comprise highways, roads, and streets designated under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-102(2): State highways are class A state roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-102(3): The state has title to all rights-of-way for all state highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-102(4): The department has jurisdiction and control over all state highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-102(5): The department shall construct and maintain each state highway using funds made available for that purpose.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103 County roads -- Class B roads -- Construction and maintenance by counties.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(1): County roads comprise all public highways, roads, and streets within the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(1)(a): are situated outside of incorporated municipalities and not designated as state highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(1)(b): have been designated as county roads; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(1)(c): are located on property under the control of a federal agency and constructed or maintained by the county under agreement with the appropriate federal agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(2): County roads are class B roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(3): The state and county have joint undivided interest in the title to all rights-of-way for all county roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(4): The county governing body exercises sole jurisdiction and control of county roads within the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(5): The county shall construct and maintain each county road using funds made available for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(6): The county legislative body may expend funds allocated to each county from the Transportation Fund under rules made by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(7): A county legislative body may use any portion of the class B road funds provided by this chapter for the construction and maintenance of class A state roads by cooperative agreement with the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-103(8): A county may enter into agreements with the appropriate federal agency for the use of federal funds, county road funds, and donations to county road funds to construct, improve, or maintain county roads within or partly within national forests.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104 City streets -- Class C roads -- Construction and maintenance.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(1): City streets comprise:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(1)(a): highways, roads, circulator alleys, and streets within the corporate limits of the municipalities that are not designated as class A state roads or as class B roads; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(1)(b): those highways, roads, and streets located within a national forest and constructed or maintained by the municipality under agreement with the appropriate federal agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(2): City streets are class C roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(3): 17-50-501 Except for city streets within counties of the first and second class as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(4): The municipal governing body exercises sole jurisdiction and control of the city streets within the municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(5): The department shall cooperate with the municipal legislative body in the construction and maintenance of the class C roads within each municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(6): The municipal legislative body shall expend or cause to be expended upon the class C roads the funds allocated to each municipality from the Transportation Fund under rules made by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(7): Any town or city in the third, fourth, or fifth class may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(7)(a): contract with the county or the department for the construction and maintenance of class C roads within its corporate limits; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(7)(b): transfer, with the consent of the county, its:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(7)(b)(i): class C roads to the class B road system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(7)(b)(ii): funds allocated from the Transportation Fund to the municipality to the county legislative body for use upon the transferred class C roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-104(8): A municipal legislative body of any city of the third, fourth, or fifth class may use any portion of the class C road funds allocated to the municipality for the construction of sidewalks, curbs, and gutters on class A state roads within the municipal limits by cooperative agreement with the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105 Class D roads -- Maps to be prepared by county -- Indication of roads.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(1): As used in this section, "class D road" means any road, way, or other land surface route that has been or is established by use or constructed and has been maintained to provide for usage by the public for vehicles with four or more wheels that is not a class A, class B, or class C road under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(2): Each class D road is part of the highway and road system within the state with the same force and effect as if the class D road had been included within this system upon its being first established or constructed.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(3): The state and county have joint undivided interest in the title to all rights-of-way for class D roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(4): The county governing body exercises sole jurisdiction and control of class D roads within the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(5): Each county shall prepare maps showing to the best of its ability the class D roads within its boundaries which were in existence as of October 21, 1976. Preparation of these maps may be done by the county itself or through any multi-county planning district in which the county participates.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(6): (5) Any class D road which is established or constructed after October 21, 1976, shall be reflected on maps prepared as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(7): (5); (6) The county shall provide a copy of any map under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-105(8): The department shall scribe each road shown on its own county map series.  The department is not responsible for the validity of any class D road and is not responsible for its being inventoried. The department shall also keep on file an historical map record of the roads as provided by the counties.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-106 Actions to determine priority of use of public roads.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-106(1): The county attorney under the direction of the county legislative body shall determine a priority of public use of all county roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-106(2): This action may be instigated by the written request of 10 taxpayers of the county to the county legislative body.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-106(3): The county legislative body shall request the county attorney to instigate action within a reasonable length of time.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-107 County executive to keep plats of roads and highways.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-107(1): The county  executive of each county shall determine all county roads existing in the county and prepare and keep current plats and specific descriptions of the county roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-107(2): 72-3-108
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-107(2)(a): The plats and specific descriptions shall be kept on file in the office of the county clerk or recorder.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-107(2)(b): 72-3-108 A county clerk or recorder may not remove a platted road from the records unless the legislative body has vacated the road after a public hearing in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108 County roads -- Vacation and narrowing -- Notice requirements.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108(1): A county may, by ordinance, vacate, narrow, or change the name of a county road without petition or after petition by a property owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108(2): 63G-30-102 A county may not vacate a county road unless notice of the hearing is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108(2)(a): 63G-30-102 published for the county, as a class A notice under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108(2)(b): mailed to the department and all owners of property abutting the county road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108(3): The right-of-way and easements, if any, of a property owner and the franchise rights of any public utility may not be impaired by vacating or narrowing a county road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-108(4): 72-5-305 Except as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-109(2)(b): The department may delegate the administration of the rules to the highway authorities of a municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-109(2)(c): 72-7-104 In accordance with this section and Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-109(3): The department has jurisdiction and control over the entire right-of-way of interstate highways within municipalities and is responsible for the construction, maintenance, and regulation of the interstate highways within municipalities.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-110 Proposal to bypass or provide alternate route through city or town -- Notice and hearing required.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-110(1): Whenever the department proposes to construct a highway bypassing any city or town, or to provide an alternate route through or outside any city or town, the commission shall notify the governing officials of the city or town and hold a public hearing, on a date set, for the purpose of advising the citizens of the city or town of the reason or reasons for the highway proposed to be constructed.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-110(2): The hearing shall be held within the city or town to be bypassed, except that if the highway proposed will bypass or provide an alternate route through or outside of several cities or towns located within close proximity to each other, the commission may combine the hearings and hold them in one city or town centrally and conveniently located to the others at which time each city and town shall be given ample opportunity to be heard.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-110(3): Subsequent to the hearing, the commission shall notify in writing the officials of the city or town, or of each of the cities or towns if the hearings are combined, of the decision reached as a result of the hearing within 10 days from the time the decision is reached.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-111 Roads and parking spaces in connection with state institutions and areas for recreational activities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to SectionUtah Code Annotated § 72-3-111(1): leading to roads and parking spaces on the grounds of state institutions to which roads have not been designated by the Legislature; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-111(2): roads and parking spaces to serve areas in immediate proximity to a designated highway used for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-111(2)(a): salt flat races;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-111(2)(b): ski meets; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-111(2)(c): activities which are promoted for the general welfare.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112 Authority to designate, maintain, and build livestock highways.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(1): A highway authority may designate, survey, construct, protect, enter into agreements for, purchase rights-of-way for, and maintain livestock highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(2): If state highways with heavy traffic are regularly used for the movement of livestock, the department, county legislative bodies, and municipal legislative bodies shall construct and maintain livestock roads or trails for livestock travel.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(3): A livestock highway or trail is for the purpose of transferring livestock and may not be used for pasturing purposes, except during regular transfer operations.  The public may use livestock highways or trails but shall give preference to livestock when livestock is present.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(4): A person may not drive livestock upon the public highways when a livestock highway is available and can be used without undue inconvenience.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(5): (4) A person who violates the provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(5)(a): fine of not more than $100;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(5)(b): jail sentence of not more than 30 days; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-112(5)(c): fine and imprisonment.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201 Jurisdiction over highways leading to and within state parks.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(1): As used in this part, "state park access highways" means the highways specified under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(2): The department, a county, or a municipality has jurisdiction over and responsibility for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(2)(a): primary access highways to state parks;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(2)(b): highways to the main attraction within each state park; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(2)(c): highways through state parks providing access to land uses beyond state park boundaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(3): (2)(a); (b); 72-3-202; 72-3-206; (2)(c); 72-3-102; 72-3-103; 72-3-104
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(3)(a): (2)(a); (b); 72-3-202; 72-3-206 The appropriate entities with jurisdiction over and responsibility for the highways referred to in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-201(3)(b): (2)(c); 72-3-102; 72-3-103; 72-3-104 Jurisdiction over and responsibility for highways under Subsection
