Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207 State Park Access Highways Improvement Program -- Distribution -- Rulemaking.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(1): There is created the State Park Access Highways Improvement Program within the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(2): The program shall be funded from the following revenue sources:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(2)(a): any voluntary contributions received for improvements to state park access highways; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(2)(b): appropriations made to the program by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(3): (4) The department may use the program money as matching grants to a county or municipality for the improvement of class B or class C roads specified as state park access highways under this part subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(3)(a): money available in the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(3)(b): prioritization of the program money by the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(3)(c): a county or municipality providing at least 50% of the cost of each improvement project in matching funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(3)(d): (4) rules made under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The department shall make rules in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-207(5): The department shall commit funds for state park access highway projects for the amount of funding currently programmed in a funded year in the 2007 Statewide Transportation Improvement Program.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-301 Statewide public safety interest highway defined -- Designations -- Control -- Maintenance -- Improvement restrictions -- Formula funding provisions.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-301(1): As used in this part, "statewide public safety interest highway" means a designated state highway that serves a compelling statewide public safety interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-301(2): Statewide public safety interest highways include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-301(2)(a): SR-900.  From near the east bound on and off ramps of the I-80 Delle Interchange on the I-80 south frontage road, traversing northwesterly, westerly, and northeasterly, including on portions of a county road and a Bureau of Land Management road for a distance of 9.24 miles. Then beginning again at the I-80 south frontage road traversing southwesterly and northwesterly on a county road for a distance of 4.33 miles. Then beginning again at the I-80 south frontage road traversing southwesterly, northerly, northwesterly, westerly, and northeasterly on a county road and a Bureau of Land Management road to near the east bound on and off ramps of I-80 Low/Lakeside Interchange for a distance of 2.61 miles. The entire length of SR-900 is a total distance of 16.18 miles.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-3-301(2)(b): SR-901.  From SR-196 traversing westerly and northwesterly on a county road to a junction with a Bureau of Land Management road described as part of SR-901, then northwesterly to a junction with a county road for a distance of 8.70 miles. Then beginning again at a junction with SR-901 traversing northwesterly on a Bureau of Land Management road to a junction with a county road for a distance of 6.52 miles. Then beginning again at a junction with SR-901 traversing southwesterly on a Bureau of Land Management road to a junction with a county road for a distance of 5.44 miles. Then beginning again from a junction with SR-901 traversing southwesterly on a county road to a junction with a county road a distance of 11.52 miles. Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 4 - Designation of State Highways Act
******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Designation of State Highways Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102 Additions to or deletions from state highway system -- Designation of highways as state highways between sessions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1): (1)(b); 72-4-102.5; (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(a): The Legislature may add to or delete highways or sections of highways from the state highway system.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(b): The department shall annually submit to the Legislature a list of highways or sections of highways the commission recommends for addition to or deletion from the state highway system.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(c): (1)(b); 72-4-102.5; (3) All recommendations under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(c)(i): 72-4-102.5 the criteria for state highways under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(c)(ii): (3) funding and operational considerations identified under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(c)(iii): efficiency of highway operations and maintenance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(1)(c)(iv): other factors the commission determines are appropriate, in consultation with the department and the highway authorities involved in the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(2): 72-4-102.5; (3) Between general sessions of the Legislature, highways may be designated as state highways or deleted from the state highway system if:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102(2)(a): 72-4-102.5; (3) approved by the commission in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5 Definitions -- Rulemaking -- Criteria for state highways.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(a): "Arterial highway" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(b): "Collector highway," "collector road," or "collector street" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(c): "Local street" or "local road" means a highway that is not an arterial highway or a collector highway and that is under the jurisdiction of a county or municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(d): "Major collector highway," "major collector road," or "major collector street" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(e): "Minor collector road" or "minor collector street" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(f): "Minor arterial highway" or "minor arterial street" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(g): "Principal arterial highway" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(h): "Rural area" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(i): "Tourist area" means an area of the state frequented by tourists for the purpose of visiting national parks, national recreation areas, national monuments, or state parks.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(1)(j): "Urban area" has the same meaning as provided under the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(2): Title 72, Chapter 3, Highway Jurisdiction and Classification Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(2)(a): Title 72, Chapter 3, Highway Jurisdiction and Classification Act Subject to the provisions of
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(2)(b): The highway authorities of this state or their representatives shall cooperate to match the criteria provided under this section with the state highways designated under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(2)(c): The primary function of state highways is to provide for the safe and efficient movement of traffic, while providing access to property is a secondary function.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(2)(d): The primary function of county and municipal highways is to provide access to property.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(2)(e): For purposes of this section, if a highway is within 10 miles of a location identified under this section, the location is considered to be served by that highway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3): A state highway shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(a): serve a statewide purpose by accommodating interstate movement of traffic or interregion movement of traffic within the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(b): primarily move higher traffic volumes over longer distances than highways under local jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(c): connect major population centers;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(d): be spaced so that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(d)(i): all developed areas in the state are within a reasonable distance of a state highway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(d)(ii): duplicative state routes are avoided;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(e): provide state highway system continuity and efficiency of state highway system operation and maintenance activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(f): include all interstate routes, all expressways, and all highways on the National Highway System as designated by the Federal Highway Administration under 23 C.F.R. Section 470, Subpart A, as of January 1, 2005; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(3)(g): exclude parking lots, driving ranges, and campus roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4): (3) Consistent with the provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(a): include all minor arterial highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b): include a major collector highway that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b)(i): serves a county seat;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b)(ii): serves a municipality with a population of 1,000 or more;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b)(iii): serves a major industrial, commercial, or recreation areas that generate traffic volumes equivalent to a population of 1,000 or more;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b)(iv): provides continuity for the state highway system by providing major connections between other state highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b)(v): provides service between two or more counties; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(b)(vi): serves a compelling statewide public safety interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(4)(c): exclude all minor collector streets and local roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5): (3) Consistent with the provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5)(a): include all principal arterial highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5)(b): include a minor arterial highway that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5)(b)(i): provides continuity for the state highway system by providing major connections between other state highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5)(b)(ii): is a route that is expected to be a principal arterial highway within 10 years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5)(b)(iii): is needed to provide access to state highways; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(5)(c): exclude all collector highways and local roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6): (3); (4) In addition to the provisions of Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6)(a): shall include a highway that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6)(a)(i): serves a national park or a national recreational area; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6)(a)(ii): serves a national monument with visitation greater than 100,000 per year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6)(b): may include a highway that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6)(b)(i): serves a state park with visitation greater than 100,000 per year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(6)(b)(ii): serves a recreation site with visitation greater than 100,000 per year.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (7)(a); (7)(a); (7)(c)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(a)(i): establishing and defining a functional classification of highways for the purpose of implementing this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(a)(ii): defining and designating regionally significant arterial highways; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(a)(iii): establishing an access management policy consistent with the functional classification of roadways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(b): (7)(a) The definitions under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(c): (7)(a); (7)(c)(i) The rules under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(c)(i): shall conform as nearly as practical to the Federal Highway Administration Functional Classification Guidelines; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-102.5(7)(c)(ii): (7)(c)(i) may incorporate by reference, in whole or in part, the federal guidelines under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-103 Deletion of highway from state highway system -- Return to county or municipality or abandonment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
When a state highway or portion of a state highway is deleted from the state highway system by the Legislature or the commission, the department shall:Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-103(1): return or relinquish the state highway or portion of the state highway to the county or municipality in which it is situated; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-103(2): abandon the state highway or portion of the state highway if it no longer serves the purpose of a highway.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-104 Disposition of portion of highways realigned.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-104(1): The department may make changes in the alignment of state highways to provide for greater highway safety or more economical highway operation and maintenance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-104(2): 72-5-111 When a state highway is realigned, the former portion of it may be:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-104(2)(a): returned or relinquished to the county or municipality in which it is situated to be maintained as a highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-104(2)(b): abandoned by the department if it no longer serves the purpose of a highway; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-104(2)(c): 72-5-111 disposed of in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-105 Designation of state highways in municipalities.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If the route of a state highway extends into or through a municipality and the Legislature has not specifically designated the location of the highway within the municipality, the commission, in cooperation with the municipality, shall designate the streets of the municipality over which the state highway shall be routed.   The designated streets shall be part of the state highway system without compensation to the municipality.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-105.1 Future designations of state highways.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-105.1(2): 72-4-115
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-105.1(2)(a): The department shall perform an environmental analysis related to the proposed extension of the western terminus of SR-92 with funds appropriated to the department for that purpose.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(1): 72-4-302 "Committee" means the Utah State Scenic Byway Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(2): "Corridor management plan" means a written document:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(2)(a): required to be submitted for a highway to be nominated as a National Scenic Byway or All-American Road that specifies the actions, procedures, controls, operational practices, and administrative strategies to maintain the scenic, historic, recreational, cultural, archeological, and natural qualities of a scenic byway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(2)(b): adopted by each municipality or county affected by the corridor management plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(3): 72-4-303(1)(b); 72-4-303(1)(b) "Non-scenic area" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(3)(a): 72-4-303(1)(b) any property that is unzoned or zoned for commercial or industrial use adjoining a highway that does not contain at least one of the intrinsic qualities described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(3)(b): 72-4-303(1)(b) any property that is unzoned or zoned for commercial or industrial use that contains an intrinsic quality described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(4): "Segmentation" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(4)(a): removing the scenic byway designation from a portion of an existing scenic byway that adjoins a non-scenic area; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301(4)(b): excluding a portion of a highway from a scenic byway designation where the highway adjoins a non-scenic area.

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(1): 72-4-304 Except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(2): (1); (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(2)(a): (1) In accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(2)(a)(i): approve the corridor management plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(2)(a)(ii): approve the corridor management plan with conditions specified by the Legislature; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(2)(a)(iii): deny the corridor management plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-301.5(2)(b): (2)(a) Upon a decision by the Legislature under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303 Powers and duties of the Utah State Scenic Byway Committee -- Requirements for designation -- Segmentation -- Rulemaking authority -- Designation on state maps -- Outdoor advertising.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1): (1)(b) The committee shall have the responsibility to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(a): (1)(b) administer a coordinated scenic byway program within the state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(a)(i): (1)(b) preserves and protects the intrinsic qualities described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(a)(ii): enhances recreation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(a)(iii): promotes economic development through tourism and education;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b): ensure that a highway nominated for a scenic byway designation possesses at least one of the following six intrinsic qualities:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b)(i): scenic quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b)(ii): natural quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b)(iii): historic quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b)(iv): cultural quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b)(v): archaeological quality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(b)(vi): recreational quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(c): designate highways as state scenic byways from nominated highways within the state if the committee determines that the highway possesses the criteria for a state scenic byway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(1)(d): remove the designation of a highway as a scenic byway if the committee determines that the highway no longer meets the criteria under which it was designated.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(2)(a): A highway located within a county, city, or town within this state may not be included as part of a designation or nomination as a state scenic byway, National Scenic Byway, or All-American Road unless the nomination or designation is sanctioned in writing by an official action of the legislative body of each county, city, or town through which the proposed state scenic byway, National Scenic Byway, or All-American Road passes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(2)(b): (2)(a) If a county, city, or town does not give approval as required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3): (3)(d); (3)(a)(i); (3)(a)(i); (3)(a)(i); (3)(c)(i); (3)(c)(ii); (3)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(a): (3)(d); (3)(a)(i) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(a)(i): (3)(a)(i) by the legislative body of the county, city, or town where the segmentation is to occur if:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(a)(i)(A): a person or another entity, with the consent of any landowners affected by the segmentation, has requested the segmentation of a portion of a road or highway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(a)(i)(B): (3)(a)(i) the legislative body of the county, city, or town reviews the segmentation proposed under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(a)(ii): by the committee at the written request of the owner of real property that is a non-scenic area adjacent to a state scenic byway, National Scenic Byway, or All-American Road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(b): (3)(a)(i) The legislative body of a county, city, or town shall render a decision on a segmentation request under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(c): (3)(a)(i); (3)(c)(i); (3)(c)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(c)(i): (3)(a)(i) If the legislative body of a county, city, or town denies the request to segment the state scenic byway, National Scenic Byway, or All-American Road under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(c)(ii): (3)(c)(i) The committee shall hear and answer an appeal of the denial of a segmentation request within 60 days of a request submitted in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-4-303(3)(c)(iii): (3)(c)(ii) If the committee does not render a decision on an appeal in accordance with Subsection

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 5 - Rights-Of-Way Act
**************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Rights-of-way Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part, "state transportation purposes" includes:Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(1): highway, public transit facility, and transportation rights-of-way, including those necessary within cities and towns;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(2): the construction, reconstruction, relocation, improvement, maintenance, and mitigation from the effects of these activities on state highways and other transportation facilities, including parking facilities, under the control of the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(3): limited access facilities, including rights of access, air, light, and view and frontage and service roads to highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(4): adequate drainage in connection with any highway, cut, fill, or channel change and the maintenance of any highway, cut, fill, or channel change;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(5): weighing stations, shops, offices, storage buildings and yards, and road maintenance or construction sites;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(6): road material sites, sites for the manufacture of road materials, and access roads to the sites;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(7): the maintenance of an unobstructed view of any portion of a highway to promote the safety of the traveling public;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(8): the placement of traffic signals, directional signs, and other signs, fences, curbs, barriers, and obstructions for the convenience of the traveling public;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(9): the construction and maintenance of storm sewers, sidewalks, and highway illumination;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(10): the construction and maintenance of livestock highways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(11): the construction and maintenance of roadside rest areas adjacent to or near any highway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-102(12): the mitigation of impacts from transportation projects.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103 Acquisition of rights-of-way and other real property -- Title to property acquired.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(1): The department may acquire any real property or interests in real property necessary for temporary, present, or reasonable future state transportation purposes by gift, agreement, exchange, purchase, condemnation, or otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(2): 72-3-104(3); Title 72, Chapter 5, Part 3, Rights-Of-Way Across Federal Lands Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(2)(a)(i): Title to real property acquired by the  department or the counties, cities, and towns by gift, agreement, exchange, purchase, condemnation, or otherwise for highway rights-of-way or other transportation purposes may be in fee simple or any lesser estate or interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(2)(a)(ii): Title to real property acquired by the department for a public transit project shall be transferred to the public transit district responsible for the project.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(2)(a)(iii): A public transit district shall cover all costs associated with any condemnation on its behalf.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(2)(b): 72-3-104(3); Title 72, Chapter 5, Part 3, Rights-Of-Way Across Federal Lands Act If the highway is a county road, city street under joint title as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-103(3): A transfer of land bounded by a highway on a right-of-way for which the public has only an easement passes the title of the person whose estate is transferred to the middle of the highway.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-106 Expiration of franchise of toll bridge or road.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If the franchise of any toll bridge or road expires by limitation, forfeiture, or nonuser it is a free public highway, and no claim shall be valid against the public for right-of-way or for land or material comprising the bridge or road.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107 United States patents -- Patentee and county to assert claims to roads crossing land.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(1)(a): If any person acquires title from the United States to any land in this state over which any public highway extends that has not been duly platted, and that has not been continuously used as a public highway for a period of 10 years, the person shall within three months after receipt of the person's patent assert the person's claim for damages in writing to the county executive of the county in which the land is situated.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(1)(b): The county legislative body shall have an additional period of three months in which to begin proceedings to condemn the land according to law.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(2): (1); (1)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(2)(a): (1) The highway shall continue open as a public highway during the periods described under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(2)(b): (1)(b) If no action is begun by the county executive within the period described under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-107(3): In case of a failure by the person so acquiring title to public lands to assert his claim for damage during the three months from the time the person received a patent to the lands, the person shall thereafter be barred from asserting or recovering any damages by reason of the public highway, and the public highway shall remain open.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-108 Width of rights-of-way for public highways.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
The width of rights-of-way for public highways shall be set as the highway authorities of the state, counties, or municipalities may determine for the highways under their respective jurisdiction.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-109 Contributions of property by counties and municipalities.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Counties and municipalities may contribute real or personal property to the department for state transportation purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-112 Acquisition of real property from county, city, or other political subdivision -- Exchange.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department may purchase or otherwise acquire from any county, city, or other political subdivision of the state real property or interests in real property which may be exchanged for or used in the purchase of other real property or interests in real property to be used in connection with the construction, maintenance, or operation of state highways.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-113 Acquisition of entire lot, block, or tract -- Sale or exchange of remainder.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a part of an entire lot, block, tract of land, or interest or improvement in real property is to be acquired by the department and the remainder is to be left in a shape or condition of little value to its owner or to give rise to claims or litigation concerning damages, the department may acquire the whole of the property and may sell the remainder or may exchange it for other property needed for highway purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114 Property acquired in advance of construction -- Lease or rental.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114(1)(a): The department may acquire real property or interests or improvements in real property in advance of the actual construction, reconstruction, or improvement of highways or public transit facilities in order to save on acquisition costs or avoid the payment of excessive damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114(1)(b): The real property or interests or improvements in real property may be leased or rented by the department in a manner, for a period of time, and for a sum determined by the department to be in the best interest of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114(2)(a): The department may employ private agencies to manage rental properties when it is more economical and in the best interests of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-114(2)(b): All money received for leases and rentals, after deducting any portion to which the federal government may be entitled, shall be deposited with the state treasurer and credited to the  Transportation Fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-115 Acquisition of property devoted to or held for other public use.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-115(1): If property devoted to or held for some other public use for which the power of eminent domain might be exercised is to be taken for state transportation purposes, the department may, with the consent of the person or agency in charge of the other public use, condemn real property to be exchanged with the person or agency for the real property to be taken for state transportation purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-115(2): This section does not limit the department's authorization to acquire, other than by condemnation, property for exchange purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-118 Unlawful road closures.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-118(1): 72-1-212; 72-5-105; 72-6-114; 72-7-103 Except as provided in Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-201 Purpose statement.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-201(1)(a): The Legislature recognizes that highways provide tangible benefits to private and public lands of the state by providing access, allowing development, and facilitating production of income.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-201(1)(b): Many of those highways traverse state lands, including lands held by the state in trust for the school children and public institutions of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-201(1)(c): Many of the existing highways have been previously established without an official grant of an easement or right of entry from this state, yet these highways often are the only access to private and public lands of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-201(2): The Legislature intends to establish a means for ensuring continued access to the private and public lands of the state for the good of the people, while fulfilling its fiduciary responsibilities toward the schoolchildren by protecting their trust holdings against loss.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-202 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-202(1): "Responsible authority" means a private party, the state of Utah, or a political subdivision of the state claiming rights to a highway right-of-way, easement, or right of entry across state lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-202(2): 65A-1-1 "Sovereign lands" has the same meaning as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-202(3): "State lands" means sovereign and trust lands, as well as all other lands held by or on behalf of the departments, divisions, or institutions of the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1): 72-5-104 "Acceptance," "acceptance of a right-of-way for the construction of a highway over public lands, not reserved for public uses," or "accepted" so as to vest the R.S. 2477 dominant estate in the right-of-way in the state and any applicable political subdivision of the state, means one or more of the following acts prior to October 21, 1976:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a): by the state or any political subdivision of the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(i): construction or maintenance of a highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(ii): inclusion of the highway in a state, county, or municipal road system;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(iii): expenditure of any public funds on the highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(iv): execution of a memorandum of understanding or other agreement with any other public or private entity or an agency of the federal government that recognizes the right or obligation of the state or a political subdivision of the state to construct or maintain the highway or a portion of the highway; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(v): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(v)(A): the acceptance at statehood of the school or institutional trust lands accessed or traversed by the right-of-way; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(a)(v)(B): the selection and receipt by the state of a clear list, indemnity list, or other document conveying title to the state of school, institutional trust lands, or other state lands accessed or traversed by the highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(b): 72-5-104 use by the public for a period in excess of 10 years in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(1)(c): any other act consistent with state or federal law indicating acceptance of a right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(a): "Construction" means any physical act of readying a highway for use by the public according to the available or intended mode of transportation, including, foot, horse, vehicle, pipeline, or other mode.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b): "Construction" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b)(i): removing vegetation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b)(ii): moving obstructions, including rocks, boulders, and outcroppings;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b)(iii): filling low spots;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b)(iv): maintenance over several years;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b)(v): creation of an identifiable route by use over time; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(2)(b)(vi): other similar activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(3): "Cut-off date" means the earlier of the date the underlying land was reserved for public use or October 21, 1976.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(a): "Highway" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(a)(i): any road, street, trail, or other access or way that is open to the public to come and go or transport water at will, without regard to how or by whom the way was constructed or maintained; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(a)(ii): appurtenant land and structures including road drainage ditches, back and front slopes, turnouts, rest areas, and other areas that facilitate use of the highway by the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(b): "Highway" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(b)(i): pedestrian trails, horse paths, livestock trails, wagon roads, jeep trails, logging roads, homestead roads, mine-to-market roads, alleys, tunnels, bridges, and all other ways and their attendant access for maintenance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(b)(ii): irrigation canals, waterways, viaducts, ditches, pipelines, or other means of water transmission and their attendant access for maintenance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(4)(c): To be a "highway" a right-of-way need not have destinations or termini that are some kind of landmarks distinguishable from other points along the right-of-way, as long as the right-of-way accommodates travelers from one point along the right-of-way to another point as often as convenient or necessary.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5): "Maintenance" means any physical act of upkeep of a highway or repair of wear or damage whether from natural or other causes, including the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(a): vertical and horizontal alignment alterations to meet applicable safety standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(b): widening an existing road or flattening of shoulders or side slopes to meet applicable safety standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(c): grooming and grading of the previously constructed road surface;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(d): establishing and maintaining the road crown with materials gathered along the road;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(e): filling ruts;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(f): spot filling with the same materials of the road, or improved materials;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(g): leveling or smoothing washboards;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(h): clearing the roadway of obstructing debris;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(i): cleaning culverts, including head basins and outlets;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(j): resurfacing with the same or improved materials;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(k): installing, maintaining, repairing and replacing rip rap;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(l): maintaining drainage;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(m): maintaining and repairing washes and gullies;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(n): installing, maintaining, repairing, and replacing culverts as necessary to protect the existing surface from erosion;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(o): repairing washouts;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(p): installing, maintaining, repairing and replacing marker posts;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(q): installing, maintaining, and repairing water crossings;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(r): installing, maintaining, and repairing and replacing cattle guards;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(s): installing, maintaining, and repairing and replacing road signs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(t): installing, maintaining, and repairing and replacing road striping;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(u): repair, stabilization and improvement of cut and fill slopes;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(v): application of seal coats; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(5)(w): snow removal.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(6): "Public lands not reserved for public uses" means the surface of federal lands open to entry and location and includes the surface of lands that are subject to subsurface coal withdrawals or mining claims.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-301(7): "R.S.  2477 right-of-way" means a right-of-way for a highway constructed in this state on public lands not reserved for public uses in accordance with Revised Statute 2477, codified as 43 U.S.C.  Section 932, and accepted by the state or a political subdivision of the state prior to October 21, 1976.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302 Rights-of-way across federal lands -- Title -- Presumption -- Scope.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(1): This part applies to all R.S. 2477 rights-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(2): 72-3-102; 72-3-103; 72-3-104; 72-3-105; 72-5-103 The state and its political subdivisions have title to the R.S. 2477 rights-of-ways in accordance with Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(3)(a): Acceptance of a right-of-way for the construction of a highway over public lands, not reserved for public uses, is presumed if the state or a political subdivision of the state makes a finding that the highway was constructed and the right-of-way was accepted prior to October 21, 1976.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(3)(b): The existence of a highway in a condition suitable for public use establishes a presumption that the highway has continued in use in its present location since the land over which it is built was public land not reserved for public use.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4): 72-5-301; 72-5-301
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4)(a): 72-5-301; 72-5-301 Unless specifically determined prior to the cut-off date provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4)(a)(i): highway drainage facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4)(a)(ii): shoulders adjacent to the right-of-way; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4)(a)(iii): 72-5-301 maintenance activities defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4)(b): Unless specifically determined by the state or political subdivision of the state with the authority over the R.S. 2477 right-of-way, an R.S. 2477 right-of-way is presumed to be at least 66 feet wide if that is the usual width of highway rights-of-way in the area.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(4)(c): The scope of the R.S. 2477 right-of-way includes the right to widen the highway as necessary to accommodate the increased travel associated with those uses, up to, where applicable, improving a highway to two lanes so travelers can safely pass each other.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-302(5): 72-6-102 The safety standards established by the Department of Transportation in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-303 Maintenance -- Impact on adjacent land owners.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-303(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-303(1)(a): The state and its political subdivisions are not required to maintain highways within R.S. 2477 rights-of-way for vehicular travel unless the R.S. 2477 right-of-way encompasses a highway included on a highway system for vehicular travel.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-303(1)(b): A decision to improve or not improve an R.S. 2477 right-of-way is a purely discretionary function.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-303(2): The holder of an R.S. 2477 right-of-way and the owner of the servient estate shall exercise their rights without unreasonably interfering with one another.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-303(3): The holder of the R.S. 2477 right-of-way shall design and conduct construction and maintenance activities so as to minimize impacts on adjacent federal public lands, consistent with applicable safety standards.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304 Mapping and survey requirements.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304(1): The Department of Transportation, counties, and cities are not required to possess centerline surveys for R.S. 2477 rights-of-ways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304(2): 72-3-105; 72-3-107; 63A-16-506; (3) To be accepted, highways within R.S. 2477 rights-of-way do not need to be included in the plats, descriptions, and maps of county roads required by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304(3): 63A-16-505
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304(3)(a): 63A-16-505 The Utah Geospatial Resource Center, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304(3)(b): The record of R.S. 2477 rights-of-way shall be based on information maintained by the Department of Transportation and cartographic, topographic, photographic, historical, and other data available to or maintained by the Utah Geospatial Resource Center.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-304(3)(c): Agencies and political subdivisions of the state may provide additional information regarding R.S. 2477 rights-of-way when information is available.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305 Term of grant -- Abandonment.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305(1): In accordance with the terms of the R.S. 2477 right-of-way grant, once accepted, an R.S. 2477 right-of-way is established for a perpetual term.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305(2): Part 1, Public Highways
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305(2)(a): Part 1, Public Highways Abandonment of any R.S. 2477 right-of-way shall only take place in accordance with the procedures in
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305(2)(b): If any R.S. 2477 right-of-way is abandoned by a political subdivision of the state, the right-of-way shall revert to the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305(3): The passage of time or the frequency of use of an R.S. 2477 right-of-way is not evidence of waiver or abandonment of the R.S. 2477 right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-305(4): An R.S. 2477 right-of-way continues even if the servient estate is transferred out of the public domain.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306 Assumption of risk -- Immunity -- Public safety.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(1): 72-3-102; 72-3-103; 72-3-104 An R.S. 2477 right-of-way not designated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(2): Title 63G, Chapter 7, Governmental Immunity Act of Utah The state and its political subdivisions do not waive immunity under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(3): The state and its political subdivisions assume no liability for injury or damage resulting from a failure to maintain any:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(3)(a): R.S. 2477 right-of-way for vehicular travel; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(3)(b): highway sign on an R.S. 2477 right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(4): If the state or any political subdivision of the state chooses to maintain an R.S. 2477 right-of-way, the basic governmental objective involved in providing the improvements is the consistent promotion of public safety.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(5)(a): The state recognizes that there are limited funds available to upgrade all R.S. 2477 rights-of-way to applicable safety standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(5)(b): A decision by the state or a political subdivision of the state to allocate funds for maintaining an R.S. 2477 right-of-way is the result of evaluation and assigning of priorities for the promotion of public safety.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(5)(c): The state or a political subdivision of the state must use its judgment and expertise to evaluate which safety feature improvements should be made first.  In making this policy determination the state or a political subdivision of the state may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(5)(c)(i): perform on-site inspections and weigh all factors relating to safety, including the physical characteristics and configuration of the R.S. 2477 right-of-way and the volume and type of traffic on the R.S. 2477 right-of-way; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-306(5)(c)(ii): consult with transportation experts who have expertise to make an evaluation of the relative dangerousness of R.S. 2477 rights-of-way within their jurisdiction.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-307(2)(a): the county does not object to the proposed agreement; or

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-307(5): (1) If a political subdivision fails to provide notice of a proposed agreement to a county as required by Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-308 Provisions govern determinations -- Determinations effective dates.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The provisions of this part pertaining to substantive standards for acceptance of the R.S. 2477 grant shall govern the R.S. 2477 assessments of the governor or the governor's designee and the decisions of the courts to the extent that the provisions are consistent with state law, including common law, applicable as of the cut-off date.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310 Notice of acknowledgment -- Court determination -- Presumption of acceptance.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(1): The governor or the governor's designee shall provide a copy of the notice of acknowledgement by certified mail and return receipt requested to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(1)(a): the last known owner of the servient estate in land over which the right-of-way or rights-of-way subject to the notice runs; and

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(2)(b): Venue for the court action shall be the district court for Salt Lake County.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(2)(c): The petition shall be filed no later than 60 days after the date on which the petitioner received a copy of the notice of acknowledgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(2)(d): The state, through the governor or the governor's designee, shall be named as a respondent and served with a copy of the petition in accordance with the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(2)(e): No one other than a person with a servient estate ownership claim in land over which the right-of-way or rights-of-way subject to the notice runs or a competing dominant estate claim may challenge the correctness of a notice of acknowledgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(3): The petition for a court decision of the correctness of the notice of acknowledgment shall be a complaint governed by the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure and shall contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(3)(a): the petitioner's name and mailing address;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(3)(b): a copy of the notice of acknowledgment the petitioner asserts is incorrect;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(3)(c): a request for relief specifying the type and extent of relief requested; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(3)(d): a statement of the reasons why the petitioner is entitled to relief.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(4): Part 3, Rights-Of-Way Across Federal Lands Act Except as provided under this
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-310(5): The court shall make its decision without deference to the notice of acknowledgment.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(1): "Corridor" means the path or proposed path of a transportation facility, including a public transit facility, that exists or that may exist in the future, and may include the land occupied or to be occupied by a transportation facility, and any other land that may be needed for expanding a transportation facility or for controlling access to it.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(2): "Corridor preservation" means planning or acquisition processes intended to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(2)(a): protect or enhance the capacity of existing corridors; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(2)(b): protect the availability of proposed corridors in advance of the need for and the actual commencement of the transportation facility construction.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(3): "Development" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(3)(a): the subdividing of land;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(3)(b): the construction of improvements, expansions, or additions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(3)(c): any other action that will appreciably increase the value of and the future acquisition cost of land.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(4): Title 17, Chapter 27a, Part 4, General Plan; Title 10, Chapter 9a, Part 4, General Plan "Official map" means a map, drawn by government authorities and recorded in county recording offices that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(4)(a): shows actual and proposed rights-of-way, centerline alignments, and setbacks for highways and other transportation facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(4)(b): provides a basis for restricting development in designated rights-of-way or between designated setbacks to allow the government authorities time to purchase or otherwise reserve the land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(4)(c): Title 17, Chapter 27a, Part 4, General Plan; Title 10, Chapter 9a, Part 4, General Plan for counties and municipalities may be adopted as an element of the general plan, pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-401(5): "Taking" means an act or regulation, either by exercise of eminent domain or other police power, whereby government puts private property to public use or restrains use of private property for public purposes, and that requires compensation to be paid to private property owners.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-402 Public purpose.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-402(1): The Legislature finds and declares that the planning and preservation of transportation corridors is a public purpose, that the acquisition of public rights in private property for possible use as a transportation corridor years in advance is a public purpose, and that acquisition of public rights in private property for possible use as alternative transportation corridors is a public purpose, even if one or more of the transportation corridors is eventually not used for a public purpose, so long as reasonable evidence exists at the time of acquisition that the transportation facility will be developed within the time period established under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-402(2): The Legislature finds and declares that the acquisition of private property rights for the preservation of transportation corridors should be done on a voluntary basis and not by the use of eminent domain powers.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403 Transportation corridor preservation powers.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(1): 72-2-117 The department, counties, and municipalities may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(1)(a): 72-2-117 act in cooperation with one another and other government entities to promote planning for and enhance the preservation of transportation corridors and to more effectively use the money available in the Marda Dillree Corridor Preservation Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(1)(b): undertake transportation corridor planning, review, and preservation processes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(1)(c): acquire fee simple rights and other rights of less than fee simple, including easement and development rights, or the rights to limit development, including rights in alternative transportation corridors, and to make these acquisitions up to a projected 40 years in advance of using those rights in actual transportation facility construction.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(2): (1) In addition to the powers described under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(2)(a): limit development for transportation corridor preservation by land use regulation and by official maps; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(2)(b): by ordinance prescribe procedures for approving limited development in transportation corridors until the time transportation facility construction begins.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(3): 10-9a-206; 17-27a-206

Utah Code Annotated § 72-5-403(3)(b): The department shall notify a county or municipality if the county or municipality has land within its boundaries that is located within the boundaries of a high priority transportation corridor.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 6 - Construction, Maintenance, and Operations Act
******************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Construction, Maintenance, and Operations Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-102 Uniform plans and specifications for construction and maintenance.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall:Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-102(1): prepare and adopt uniform standard plans and specifications for the construction and maintenance of state highways; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-102(2): issue a manual containing plans and specifications for the information and guidance of officials having supervision of the construction and maintenance of state highways.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-103 Plans, specifications, and estimates for culverts, bridges, and road construction.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall furnish plans, specifications, and estimates for culverts, bridges, road construction, and other related information desired by local highway authorities for use on county roads and city streets on terms mutually agreed upon.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-104 Highways to conform to grade and direction in municipalities.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Except for the highways part of the interstate system, a highway that extends through a municipality shall conform to the direction and grade of other streets in the municipality unless permission is obtained from the highway authorities of the municipality for a variance in the direction and grade.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-105 Contracts for construction and maintenance -- Agreements with county or municipality.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department may enter into written agreements on behalf of the state with any county or municipality for rights-of-way and the construction or maintenance of any part of a state highway:Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-105(1): at the expense of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-105(2): at the expense of any county or municipality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-105(3): at the joint expense of the state and any county and any municipality.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-106 Use of recycled asphalt.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-106(1): In making plans, specifications, and estimates, and in advertising for bids under this chapter, the department shall allow up to 25% but may allow up to 60% reclaimed asphalt pavement to be incorporated into hot asphaltic concrete used for road construction and maintenance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-106(2): The department shall ensure that hot asphaltic concrete incorporating reclaimed asphalt pavement meets or exceeds the department quality standards for roads constructed or maintained with hot asphaltic concrete not containing reclaimed asphalt pavement.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-106(3): If the department rejects any hot asphaltic concrete containing reclaimed asphalt pavement, the department shall give a written statement to the provider indicating the specific reasons the hot asphaltic concrete was rejected.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-106(4): This section does not authorize the state to directly or indirectly subsidize the production of hot asphaltic concrete containing reclaimed asphalt pavement.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109 Class B and C roads -- Construction and maintenance -- Definitions -- Estimates lower than bids -- Accountability.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1): 72-6-108; 41-6a-302; (2) As used in this section and Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(a): "Bid limit" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(a)(i): for the year 2003, $125,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(a)(ii): for each year after 2003, the amount of the bid limit for the previous year, plus an amount calculated by multiplying the amount of the bid limit for the previous year by the lesser of 3% or the actual percent change in the Consumer Price Index during the previous calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(b): "Consumer Price Index" means the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers as published by the Bureau of Labor Statistics of the United States Department of Labor.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(c): 41-6a-302
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(c)(i): "Construction" means the work that would apply to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(c)(i)(A): any new roadbed either by addition to existing systems or relocation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(c)(i)(B): resurfacing of existing roadways with more than two inches of bituminous pavement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(c)(i)(C): new structures or replacement of existing structures, except the replacement of drainage culverts.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(c)(ii): 41-6a-302 "Construction" does not include maintenance, emergency repairs, or the installation of traffic control devices as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(d): (2) "Improvement project" means construction and maintenance as defined in this section except for that maintenance excluded under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(e): "Maintenance" means the keeping of a road facility in a safe and usable condition to which it was constructed or improved, and includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(e)(i): the reworking of an existing surface by the application of up to and including two inches of bituminous pavement;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(e)(ii): the installation or replacement of guardrails, seal coats, and culverts;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(e)(iii): the grading or widening of an existing unpaved road or flattening of shoulders or side slopes to meet current width and safety standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(e)(iv): horizontal or vertical alignment changes necessary to bring an existing road in compliance with current safety standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(1)(f): "Project" means the performance of a clearly identifiable group of associated road construction activities or the same type of maintenance process, where the construction or maintenance is performed on any one class B or C road, within a half-mile proximity and occurs within the same calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(2): The following types of maintenance work are not subject to the contract or bid limit requirements of  this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(2)(a): the repair of less than the entire surface by crack sealing or patching; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(2)(b): road repairs incidental to the installation, replacement, or repair of water mains, sewers, drainage pipes, culverts, or curbs and gutters.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3): 72-6-108
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(a): 72-6-108
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(a)(i): 72-6-108 If the estimates of a qualified engineer referred to in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(a)(ii): In no event shall "substantially lower" mean estimates that are less than 10% below the lowest responsible bid.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(b): If a county or municipality performs an improvement project by force account, it shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(b)(i): provide an accounting of the costs and expenditures of the improvement including material, labor, and direct equipment costs to be calculated using the Cost Reference Guide for Construction Equipment by Dataquest Inc. or the Federal Emergency Management Agency schedule of equipment rates;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(b)(ii): disclose the costs and expenditures to any person upon request and allow the person to make a copy and pay for the actual cost of the copy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-109(3)(b)(iii): perform the work using the same specifications and standards that would apply to a private contractor.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111 Construction and maintenance of appurtenances -- Noise abatement measures.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(1): The department is authorized to construct and maintain  appurtenances along the state highway system necessary for public safety, welfare, and information.  Appurtenances include highway illumination, sidewalks, curbs, gutters, steps, driveways, retaining walls, fire hydrants, guard rails, noise abatement measures, storm sewers, and rest areas.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(2): A noise abatement measure may only be constructed by the department along a highway when:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(2)(a): the department is constructing a new state highway or performing major reconstruction on an existing state highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(2)(b): the Legislature provides an appropriation or the federal government provides funding for construction of retrofit noise abatement along an existing state highway; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(2)(c): the cost for the noise abatement measure is provided by citizens, adjacent property owners,  developers, or local governments.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(3): (2) In addition to the requirements under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(3)(a): a study to be conducted to determine the noise levels along new development adjacent to an existing state highway or a dedicated right-of-way; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(3)(b): the construction of noise abatement measures at the expense of the developer if required to be constructed under standards established by a rule of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (2)(b); (2)(b) In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4)(a): when noise abatement measures are required to be constructed, including standards for decibel levels of traffic noise;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4)(b): (2)(b) the decibel level of traffic noise which identifies the projects to be programmed by the commission for the earliest construction of retrofit noise abatement measures funded under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4)(c): (2)(b) a priority system for the construction of other retrofit noise abatement measures that meet or exceed the standards established under this section and are funded under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4)(c)(i): the number of residential dwellings adversely affected by the traffic noise;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4)(c)(ii): the cost effectiveness of mitigating the traffic noise; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-111(4)(c)(iii): the length of time the decibel level of traffic noise has met or exceeded the standards established under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112 Traffic Noise Abatement Program -- Uses.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112(1): There is created the Traffic Noise Abatement Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112(2): The program consists of money generated from the following revenue sources:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112(2)(a): any voluntary contributions received for traffic noise abatement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112(2)(b): appropriations made to the program by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112(3): The department shall use program money as prioritized by the commission and as provided by law for the study, design, construction, and maintenance of noise abatement measures.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112(4): All funding for the Traffic Noise Abatement Program shall be nonlapsing.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5 Definitions -- Nighttime highway construction noise -- Exemptions -- Permits.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1): 63N-3-602; 78B-6-1101 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(a): 63N-3-602 "Commuter rail" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(b)(i): "Front row receptor" means a noise-sensitive residential receptor that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(b)(i)(A): immediately adjacent to a transportation facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(b)(i)(B): within 800 feet of a transportation facility that is within a commercial or industrialized area.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(b)(ii): "Front row receptor" includes a residence that is contiguous to a property immediately adjacent to a transportation facility in a residential area.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(c): "Nighttime construction" means highway or public transit facility construction occurring between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(d): 78B-6-1101 "Nuisance" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(i): "Permitted activities" means activities occurring between the hours of 7:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. that are related to and necessary for nighttime construction, whether occurring at the construction site or at a gravel pit or other site for production of raw materials, and includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(i)(A): loading and unloading of trucks;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(i)(B): asphalt mixing and hauling; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(i)(C): concrete mixing and hauling.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(ii): "Permitted activities" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(ii)(A): blasting; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(1)(e)(ii)(B): crushing.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(2): The following projects are exempt from any noise ordinance, regulation, or standard of a local jurisdictional authority:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(2)(a): a state highway construction project conducted on a road where the normal posted speed limit is 55 miles per hour or greater; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(2)(b): a commuter rail construction project.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3): (2) Except for a project described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(a): provides reasonable written notice at least 48 hours in advance of any required nighttime construction to each residential dwelling located within front row receptors of the activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b): determines a net community, including traveler community, benefit exists to conduct nighttime highway construction after considering the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(i): public health;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(ii): project completion time;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(iii): air quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(iv): traffic;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(v): economics;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(vi): safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(b)(vii): local jurisdiction concerns; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(c): institutes best management noise reduction practices, as determined by the department, for front row receptors, in consultation with local government or the local jurisdictional authority for all nighttime construction, which may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(c)(i): equipment maintenance;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(c)(ii): noise shielding;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(c)(iii): scheduling the most noise intrusive activities during the day; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(3)(c)(iv): other noise mitigation methods.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(4): (2); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(4)(a): (2); (3) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(4)(b): To the extent practical, the department shall coordinate with the local jurisdictional authority during the pre-construction phase of a project to address noise exemption conditions.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(5): (4) A local jurisdictional authority shall issue a nighttime construction permit limited to permitted activities if:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(5)(a): (4) the applicant provides evidence that the permitted activities are directly related to and necessary for a nighttime construction project for which the department has obtained a noise permit from a local jurisdictional authority pursuant to Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-112.5(7)(b): (7)(a) If adjustments are requested as described in Subsection
