Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113 Acquisition and improvement of land for preservation of scenic beauty -- Authority of department.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113(1): The department is authorized to acquire and improve strips of land necessary for the restoration, preservation, and enhancement of scenic beauty within and adjacent to a federal-aid highway of this state, including acquisition of publicly owned and controlled rest and recreation areas, sanitary, and other facilities within or adjacent to the highway right-of-way reasonably necessary to accommodate the traveling public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113(2): Acquisition may be by gift, purchase, or exchange but may not be by condemnation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113(3): The interest in any land authorized to be acquired and maintained under this section may be fee simple or any lesser interest, as determined by the department to be reasonably necessary to accomplish the purposes of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113(4)(a): Real property, or any interest in real property, acquired under this section is part of the adjacent or nearest highway and is under the jurisdiction of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-113(4)(b): The department may enter into an agreement with any state agency for maintenance of land acquired in accordance with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-114 Restricting use of or closing highway -- Penalty for failure to observe barricade, warning light, etc.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-114(1): A highway authority may close or restrict travel on a highway under their jurisdiction due to construction, maintenance work, or emergency.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-114(2): 41-6a-301 If a highway or portion of a highway is closed or restricted to travel, a highway authority shall cause suitable barriers and notices to be posted and maintained in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-114(3): A person who willfully fails to observe any temporary or permanent barricade, warning light, sign, cone, or other object used in accordance with this section, or to obey a flagman, is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115 Traffic Management Systems.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(a): The Department of Transportation shall implement and administer traffic management systems to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(a)(i): facilitate the efficient flow of motor vehicle traffic on state highways to improve regional mobility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(a)(ii): reduce motor vehicle emissions where those improvements are cost effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(b): A traffic management system shall be designed to allow safe, efficient, and effective:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(b)(i): integration of existing traffic management systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(b)(ii): additions of highways and intersections under county and city administrative jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(b)(iii): incorporation of other traffic management systems; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(1)(b)(iv): adaptation to future traffic needs.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(2): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(2)(a): The cost of implementing and administering a traffic management system shall be shared pro rata by the department and the counties and municipalities using it.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(2)(b): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act The department shall enter into an agreement or contract under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(3): (2)(a); (2)(b) Additional highways and intersections under the administrative jurisdiction of a county or municipality may be added to a traffic management system upon application of the county or municipality after:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(3)(a): approval by the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(3)(b): (2)(a) determination of the appropriate cost share of the addition under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-115(3)(c): (2)(b) an agreement under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116 Regulation of utilities -- Relocation of utilities.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1): 54-2-1 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(a): "Cost of relocation" includes the entire amount paid by the utility company properly attributable to the relocation of the utility after deducting any increase in the value of the new utility and any salvage value derived from the old utility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(b): 54-2-1 "Exempt water supplier" means an entity that directly or indirectly supplies at least a portion of the entity's water for culinary purposes to the public for municipal, domestic, or industrial use, and is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(b)(i): 54-2-1 a water corporation, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(b)(ii): a community water system:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(b)(ii)(A): that either supplies water to at least 100 service connections used by year-round residents, or regularly serves at least 200 year-round residents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(b)(ii)(B): whose voting members own a share in the community water system, receive water from the community water system in proportion to the member's share in the community water system, and pay the rate set by the community water system based on the water the member receives.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(c): "Utility" includes telecommunication, crude oil, petroleum products, gas, electricity, cable television, water, sewer, data, and video transmission lines, drainage and irrigation facilities, and other similar utilities whether public, private, or cooperatively owned.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(1)(d): "Utility company" means a privately, cooperatively, or publicly owned utility, including utilities owned by political subdivisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(2)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-116(2)(b): If the department determines under the rules established in this section that it is necessary that any utilities should be relocated, the utility company owning or operating the utilities shall relocate the utilities in accordance with this section and the order of the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117 Limited-access facilities and service roads -- Access -- Right-of-way acquisition -- Grade separation -- Written permission required.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(1): A highway authority, acting alone or in cooperation with the federal government, another highway authority, or another state may plan, designate, establish, regulate, vacate, alter, improve, maintain, and provide a limited-access facility including a service road to the limited-access facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(2): A highway authority may regulate, restrict, or prohibit the use of a limited-access facility by pedestrians, animals, or by the various classes of vehicles or traffic.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(3): A highway authority may divide and separate any limited-access facility into separate roadways by the construction of raised curbing, central dividing sections, or other physical separations, or by designating separate roadways by signs, markers, stripes, and other appropriate devices.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(4): A person may not enter, exit, or cross a limited-access facility, except at designated points at which access is permitted by the highway authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(5): A highway authority may acquire, by gift, devise, purchase, or condemnation, private or public property and property rights for a limited-access facility and service road, including rights of access, air, view, and light.  All property rights acquired under this section may be in fee simple or in any lesser estate or interest.  A highway authority may acquire an entire lot, block, or tract of land, if needed, even though the entire lot, block, or tract is not immediately needed for the right-of-way of the limited-access facility or service road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(6): A highway authority may designate and establish limited-access highways as new facilities or may designate and establish an existing highway as part of a limited-access facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(7)(a): A highway authority may provide for the elimination of at grade intersections of a limited-access facility and an existing highway by grade separation, service road, or by closing the intersecting highway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(7)(b): A highway authority may not connect or intersect a limited-access facility without the written consent and previous approval of the highway authority having jurisdiction over the limited-access facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-117(8): Highway authorities may enter into agreements with each other, or with the federal government, on the financing, planning, establishment, improvement, maintenance, use, regulation, or vacation of limited-access facilities or other public ways in their respective jurisdiction, to facilitate the purposes of this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203 Authority to enter into public-private partnership agreements for tollways.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1): 72-6-118 Subject to the provisions of this part, the department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(a): enter into a tollway development agreement with one or more public or private entities to permit the entity or entities to, independently or jointly with the department, study, perform predevelopment activities, design, finance, acquire, construct, reconstruct, maintain, repair, operate, extend, or expand a tollway facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(b): enter into an agreement with other public agencies or private entities to independently or jointly provide services, or to study the feasibility of a tollway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c): negotiate the terms of private participation in a tollway, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(i): methods to determine the applicable cost, profit, and revenue distribution between the private participants and the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(ii): a reasonable method to determine toll rates or user fees, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(ii)(A): identification of vehicle or user classifications, or both, for toll rates;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(ii)(B): the original proposed toll rate or user fee for the tollway facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(ii)(C): proposed toll rate or user fee increases; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(ii)(D): a maximum toll rate or user fee for the tollway facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(iii): acceptable safety and policing standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(c)(iv): other applicable professional, consulting, design, engineering, construction, operation and maintenance standards, requirements, expenses, and costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(d): 72-6-118 grant to a private entity through a tollway development agreement the right to impose and collect tolls or user fees under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(1)(e): provide to the private entity, on mutually agreed terms, services in support of the tollway development, operation, and maintenance including planning, environmental review, design, right-of-way acquisition, oversight, inspection and monitoring, maintenance, and policing.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(2): The department shall engage outside consultants and counsel to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(2)(a): provide the state with professional services, including legal and financial guidance, to develop rules and guidelines for public-private partnerships;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(2)(b): assist the department in evaluating the risks and benefits of a proposed public-private partnership; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(2)(c): assist in the selection and terms of a tollway development agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(3): A tollway development agreement entered into under this section shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(3)(a): a provision for the application of tolls and other operating revenues to the payment of operating and maintenance costs, indebtedness by the private entity for the tollway, reserves for reconstruction, rehabilitation, resurfacing and restoration, return on equity or investment, and sums owing the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(3)(b): a provision authorizing the department to purchase, under terms agreed to by the parties, the interest of a private participant in a tollway development agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(3)(c): a provision requiring that, at the termination of the tollway development agreement, the tollway project shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(3)(c)(i): be in a state of proper maintenance as outlined in the agreement and determined by the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(3)(c)(ii): be returned to the department in satisfactory condition at no further cost to the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4): A tollway development agreement entered into under this section may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(a): allocations of liability, risk, and responsibility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(b): combinations of public and private funding and financing;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(c): compensation to the department for the grant of the tollway development agreement or the right to impose and collect tolls;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(d): participation by the department in tollway revenue, proceeds of refinancings and proceeds of sale of the tollway or interests in the private entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(e): extensions of time for, and exceptions to, performance by the private entity and compensation from the department to the private entity, due to stated events or circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(f): requirements for performance security, including payment and performance bonds, letters of credit, security deposits, guarantees, and similar protections;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(g): rights and obligations to expand the tollway, extend the tollway, add capacity improvements, add intelligent transportation systems, and otherwise upgrade the tollway during the term of the tollway development agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(h): alternative dispute resolution procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(i): limitations on liability and waivers of consequential damages;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(j): lender rights and protections; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(4)(k): other terms necessary or desirable to attract private investment and protect the department's interests.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(a): A tollway that is the subject of a tollway development agreement with a private entity, including the facilities acquired or constructed on the tollway, is public property and title to the tollway and facilities is vested in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(b): A tollway that is the subject of a tollway development agreement is part of the state highway system for purposes of identification, maintenance, enforcement of traffic laws, and other purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(c): The department may enter into one or more agreements that provide for:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(c)(i): the lease of rights-of-way, improvements, and all or any portion of the appurtenances over and under the tollway facility to the private entity for a term ending not later than 99 years after commencement of revenue operations, provided that the agreement provides upon termination for reversion of the leased property, together with the right to impose and collect tolls, to the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(c)(ii): the granting of easements;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(c)(iii): the issuance of franchises, licenses, or permits; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-203(5)(c)(iv): any other lawful uses to enable a private entity to construct, operate, maintain, or finance a tollway.

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(2): As part of an application to lease sovereign land, a private entity seeking to obtain a lease over sovereign lakebed lands shall submit an application to the commission for approval from the commission to construct a highway facility over sovereign lakebed lands.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(3)(j): a statement whether or how the highway facility can safely accommodate recreational fishing or other recreational activities on the highway facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(4): The commission is not required to review an application submitted under this section if it determines that the proposal does not meet the guidelines established under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(5): The commission shall review an application submitted under this section and approve the application if the commission determines, based upon recommendations by the department, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(5)(a): construction, operation, and maintenance of the highway facility is feasible as proposed by the private entity in the application;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(5)(b): the proposed highway facility is contained anywhere within the long-range highway plan prepared by the department or by a metropolitan planning organization, including the visionary long-range highway plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(5)(c): the construction plan for the proposed highway facility meets the engineering and design standards specified by the commission in rules made under this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(5)(d): the proposed plan for the construction, operation, and maintenance of the highway facility is financially viable, including a determination that sufficient bonding or other financial assurances are in place to cover construction, operation, and maintenance of the facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(5)(e): the private entity has entered an agreement with the department authorizing the department to assure the safety of the design, construction, operation, and maintenance of the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-303(6): 65A-7-5 Approval by the commission under this section does not constitute approval of the lease application by the Division of Forestry, Fire, and State Lands under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-402(2)(a): the highway-related service or product; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-6-402(2)(b): a monetary contribution to pay for a portion of the highway-related service or product.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103 Limitation on access authority.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1): 72-4-106; 72-4-112; 72-4-114; 72-4-121; 72-4-126 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(a): 72-4-106; 72-4-112; 72-4-114; 72-4-121; 72-4-126 "Highway facility" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(a)(i): 72-4-106 SR-7 as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(a)(ii): 72-4-112 SR-67 as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(a)(iii): 72-4-114 SR-85 as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(a)(iv): 72-4-121 SR-154 as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(a)(v): 72-4-126 SR-201 as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(b): "Legal point of access" means an access established in accordance with applicable law:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(b)(i): before July 1, 2003;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(b)(ii): by permit issued by the highway authority; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(1)(b)(iii): by a deed or court order.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(2): A highway authority may not deny reasonable ingress and egress to property adjoining a public highway except where:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(2)(a): the highway authority acquires right of ingress and egress by gift, agreement, purchase, eminent domain, or otherwise; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(2)(b): no right of ingress or egress exists between the right-of-way and the adjoining property.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(3): For a property adjoining a public highway that is not an interstate system or a highway facility, a highway authority may not close a legal point of access to the public highway, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(3)(a): the property has reasonably equivalent access to the public highway after the legal access is closed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-103(3)(b): the highway authority acquires the legal point of access by gift, agreement, purchase, or eminent domain.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104 Installations constructed in violation of rules -- Rights of highway authorities to remove or require removal.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(1): If any person, firm, or corporation installs, places, constructs, alters, repairs, or maintains any approach road, driveway, pole, pipeline, conduit, sewer, ditch, culvert, outdoor advertising sign, or any other structure or object of any kind or character within the right-of-way of any  highway without complying with this title, the highway authority having jurisdiction over the right-of-way may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(1)(a): remove the installation from the right-of-way or require the person, firm, or corporation to remove the installation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(1)(b): give written notice to the person, firm, or corporation to remove the installation from the right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(2): (1)(b) Notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(2)(a): personal service; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(2)(b)(i): mailing the notice to the person, firm, or corporation by certified mail; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(2)(b)(ii): posting a copy on the installation for 10 days.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(3): If the installation is not removed within 10 days after the notice is complete, the highway authority may remove the installation at the expense of the person, firm, or corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(4): A highway authority may recover:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-104(5)(a): If the person, firm, or corporation disputes or denies the existence, placement, construction, or maintenance of the installation, or refuses to remove or permit its removal, the highway authority may bring an action to abate the installation as a public nuisance.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108 Longitudinal telecommunication access in the interstate highway system -- Definitions -- Agreements -- Compensation -- Restrictions -- Rulemaking.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(1)(a): "Longitudinal access" means access to or use of any part of a right-of-way of a highway on the interstate system that extends generally parallel to the right-of-way for a total of 30 or more linear meters.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(1)(b): "Statewide telecommunications purposes" means the further development of the statewide network that meets the telecommunications needs of state agencies and enhances the learning purposes of higher and public education.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(1)(c): "Telecommunication facility" means any telecommunication cable, line, fiber, wire, conduit, innerduct, access manhole, handhole, tower, hut, pedestal, pole, box, transmitting equipment, receiving equipment, power equipment, or other equipment, system, and device used to transmit, receive, produce, or distribute via wireless, wireline, electronic, or optical signal for communication purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(2)(a): (4) Except as provided in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(2)(b)(ii)(C): be nonexclusive; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-108(2)(b)(ii)(D): be limited to a maximum term of 30 years.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-201 Purpose.
---------------------------------------
The regulation of junkyards in areas adjacent to any state highway included in the national system of interstate and primary highways is a statewide public purpose and necessary to promote the public safety, health, welfare, convenience, and enjoyment of public travel, to protect the public investment in public highways, and to preserve and enhance the scenic beauty of lands bordering on the highways.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-202 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-202(1): "Automobile graveyard" means any establishment or place of business which is maintained, used, or operated for storing, keeping, buying, or selling wrecked, scrapped, ruined, or dismantled motor vehicles or motor vehicle parts.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-202(2): "Junk" means old or scrap copper, brass, rope, rags, batteries, plastic, paper, trash, rubber, waste, junked, dismantled, or wrecked automobiles or their parts, and iron, steel, and other old or scrap ferrous or nonferrous material.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-202(3): "Junkyard" means any place, establishment, or business maintained, used, or operated for storing, keeping, buying, or selling junk, or for the maintenance or operation of an automobile graveyard.  Junkyard includes a salvage yard, war surplus yard, garbage dump, recycling facility, garbage processing facility, and sanitary land fill.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-203 License required.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-203(1): A person may not establish, operate, or maintain a junkyard, any portion of which is within 1,000 feet of the nearest edge of the right-of-way of any interstate or federal-aid primary highway, without obtaining a license from the department under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-203(2): A municipality may adopt ordinances, not in conflict with this part, to regulate the creation or maintenance of junkyards of any type within 660 feet of the right-of-way of designated state and federal highways within the jurisdictional limits of the adopting municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-203(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-204(2): All licenses issued under this section expire on the first day of January following the date of issue.  Licenses may be renewed from year to year upon payment of the requisite fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-204(3): Proceeds from the license fee shall be deposited with the state treasurer and credited to the Transportation Fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-206 Screening of existing junkyards.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-206(1): The department shall screen any junkyard lawfully in existence on May 9, 1967, which is located within 1,000 feet of the nearest edge of the right-of-way and visible from the main-traveled-way of any highway on the interstate or primary system.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-206(2): The screening shall be at locations on the right-of-way or in areas outside the right-of-way acquired for that purpose and may not be visible from the main-traveled-way of the interstate or federal-aid primary systems.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207 Junkyards not adaptable to screening -- Authority of department to acquire land -- Compensation.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207(1): If the department determines that the topography of the land adjoining the interstate and primary systems will not permit adequate screening of junkyards or that screening would not be economically feasible, the department may acquire by gift, purchase, exchange, or eminent domain the interests in lands necessary to secure the relocation, removal, or disposal of the junkyards.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207(2): If the department determines that it is in the best interests of the state, it may acquire lands, or interests in lands, necessary to provide adequate screening of junkyards.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207(3): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act The acquisitions provided for in this section may not be undertaken unless:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207(3)(b): Title 63J, Chapter 5, Federal Funds Procedures Act the department has received approval to seek federal grants, loans, or participation in federal programs under
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207(4): Damages resulting from any taking of property in eminent domain shall be ascertained in the manner provided by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-207(5): Just compensation shall be paid the owner for the relocation, removal, or disposal of a junkyard lawfully established under the laws of this state and which must be relocated, removed, or disposed of under this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-210 Present ordinances or regulations may be stricter.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this part affects the provisions of any lawful ordinance or regulation which is more restrictive than the provisions of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-302 Damage to signs, warnings, or barriers -- Penalty.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-302(1): A person is guilty of a class B misdemeanor who willfully and unlawfully removes, defaces, or interferes with any highway sign, signal, notice, warning, or barrier.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-302(2): (1) A person who commits an offense under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-303 Escaping water and other obstructions -- Injuring or obstructing highway -- Penalty for violations.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-303(1): A person may not willfully or carelessly:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-303(1)(a): obstruct or damage any public highway by causing or permitting flow or seepage of water;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-303(1)(b): permit water under the person's control to escape in any manner that results in damage to a public highway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-303(1)(c): place or leave, or cause to be placed or left, anything upon a public highway in a way that obstructs travel or that endangers property or persons passing on the highway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-303(2): A person who violates this section is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-304 Injury to trees on highways -- Penalty for violations.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-304(1): A person may not dig up, cut down, or otherwise willfully damage or destroy any shade, ornamental, or other tree, planted and standing on any public highway in conformity to law.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-304(2): A person who violates this section is guilty of a class B misdemeanor and is liable to the owner of the tree for treble the amount of damages sustained.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-305 Driving animals over highways -- Liability for damages.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-305(1): Except for a livestock highway, a person who drives a herd of domestic animals over a public highway is liable for any damage done by the animals in destroying the banks or rolling rocks into or upon the highway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-305(2): The damage may be recovered in a civil action brought by a highway authority having jurisdiction over the highway.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-306 Limited highways -- Penalty for driving animals over.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-306(1): A highway authority may declare a public highway that is laid out through improved lands that are not protected by fences along the lines of the highway passing through it, to be limited highways. A notice to that effect shall be posted at each end of a limited highway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-306(2): A person who willfully drives any band or herd of domestic animals over a limited highway except during the time that the abutting lands are thrown open to the public by the owners for grazing purposes, is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402 Limitations as to vehicle width, height, length, and load extensions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(1)(a): Except as provided by statute, all state or federally approved safety devices and any other lawful appurtenant devices, including refrigeration units, hitches, air line connections, and load securing devices related to the safe operation of a vehicle are excluded for purposes of measuring the width and length of a vehicle under the provisions of this part, if the devices are not designed or used for carrying cargo.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(1)(b): Load-induced tire bulge is excluded for purposes of measuring the width of vehicles under the provisions of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(1)(c): Appurtenances attached to the sides or rear of a recreational vehicle that is not a commercial motor vehicle are excluded for purposes of measuring the width and length of the recreational vehicle if the additional width or length of the appurtenances does not exceed six inches.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(2): A vehicle unladen or with a load may not exceed a width of 8-1/2 feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(3): A vehicle unladen or with a load may not exceed a height of 14 feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4): 72-7-406
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(a)(i): A single-unit vehicle, unladen or with a load, may not exceed a length of 45 feet including front and rear bumpers.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(a)(ii): In this section, a truck tractor coupled to one or more semitrailers or trailers is not considered a single-unit vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(b)(i): A semitrailer, unladen or with a load, may not exceed a length of 53 feet excluding refrigeration units, hitches, air line connections, and safety appurtenances.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(b)(ii): There is no overall length limitation on a truck tractor and semitrailer combination when the semitrailer length is 53 feet or less.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(c)(i): Two trailers coupled together, unladen or with a load, may not exceed an overall length of 61 feet, measured from the front of the first trailer to the rear of the second trailer.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(c)(ii): There is no overall length limitation on a truck tractor and double trailer combination when the trailers coupled together measure 61 feet or less.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(4)(d): 72-7-406 All other combinations of vehicles, unladen or with a load, when coupled together, may not exceed a total length of 65 feet, except the length limitations do not apply to combinations of vehicles operated at night by a public utility when required for emergency repair of public service facilities or properties, or when operated under a permit under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(5): (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(5)(a): (4) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(5)(b): A passenger vehicle may not carry any load extending beyond the line of the fenders on the left side of the vehicle nor extending more than six inches beyond the line of the fenders on the right side of the vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(6): 72-7-406 Any exception to this section must be authorized by a permit as provided under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-402(7): Any person who violates this section is guilty of a class C misdemeanor.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-403(1)(a): 41-6a-102; 72-7-406 The draw-bar or other connection between any two vehicles, one of which is towing or drawing the other on a highway, may not exceed 15 feet in length from one vehicle to the other except:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-403(1)(a)(i): 41-6a-102 in the case of a connection between any two vehicles transporting poles, pipe, machinery, or structural material that cannot be dismembered when transported upon a pole trailer as defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-403(2): A person may not operate a combination of vehicles when any trailer, semitrailer, or other vehicle being towed:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-403(2)(a): whips or swerves from side to side dangerously or unreasonably; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-403(2)(b): fails to follow substantially in the path of the towing vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-403(3): A person who violates this section is guilty of an infraction.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404 Maximum gross weight limitation for vehicles -- Bridge formula for weight limitations -- Minimum mandatory fines.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(1)(a): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(1)(a)(i): "Axle load" means the total load on all wheels whose centers may be included between two parallel transverse vertical planes 40 inches apart.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(1)(a)(ii): "Tandem axle" means two or more axles spaced not less than 40 inches nor more than 96 inches apart and having at least one common point of weight suspension.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(1)(b): The tire load rating shall appear on the tire sidewall.  A tire, wheel, or axle may not carry a greater weight than the manufacturer's rating.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(2)(a)(iii): a tandem axle load in excess of 34,000 pounds.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(3)(a)(i): W = overall gross weight on any group of two or more consecutive axles to the nearest 500 pounds.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(3)(a)(ii): L = distance in feet between the extreme of any group of two or more consecutive axles.  When the distance in feet includes a fraction of a foot of one inch or more the next larger number of feet shall be used.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(3)(a)(iii): N = number of axles in the group under consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-404(3)(b): Two consecutive sets of tandem axles may carry a gross weight of 34,000 pounds each if the overall distance between the first and last axles of the consecutive sets of tandem axles is 36 feet or more.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405 Measuring vehicles for size and weight compliance -- Summary powers of peace officers -- Penalty for violations.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405(1): Any peace officer having reason to believe that the height, width, length, or weight of a vehicle and load is unlawful may require the operator to stop the vehicle and submit to a measurement or weighing of the vehicle and load.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405(2): A peace officer may require that the vehicle be driven to the nearest scales or port-of-entry if the scales or port-of-entry is within three miles.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405(3)(a): A peace officer, special function officer, or port-of-entry agent may measure or weigh a vehicle and vehicle load for compliance with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405(3)(b): If, upon measuring or weighing a vehicle and load, it is determined that the height, width, length, or weight is unlawful, the measuring or weighing peace officer, special function officer, or port-of-entry agent may require the operator to park the vehicle in a suitable place.  The vehicle shall remain parked until the vehicle or its load is adjusted or a portion of the load is removed to conform to legal limits.  All materials unloaded shall be cared for by the owner or operator of the vehicle at his risk.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-405(4): An operator who fails or refuses to stop and submit the vehicle and load to a measurement or weighing, or who fails or refuses when directed by a peace officer, special function officer, or port-of-entry agent to comply with this section is guilty of an infraction.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-408(2): The highway authority imposing restrictions under this section shall erect signs citing the provisions of the rule or ordinance at each end of that portion of any highway affected.  The restriction is effective only when the signs are erected and maintained.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-408(3): Any person who violates any restriction imposed under the authority of this section is guilty of an infraction.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409 Loads on vehicles -- Limitations -- Confining, securing, and fastening load required -- Penalty.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(1): 41-1a-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(1)(a): "Agricultural product" means any raw product which is derived from agriculture, including silage, hay, straw, grain, manure, and other similar product.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(1)(b)(i): "Unsecured load" means the contents of a vehicle, operated on a highway, not sufficiently covered, confined, fastened, or otherwise secured in a way to prevent the contents from escaping the vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(1)(b)(ii): "Unsecured load" includes materials such as dirt, sand, gravel, rock fragments, pebbles, crushed base, aggregate, any other similar material, or scrap metal or other loose material on any portion of the vehicle not designed to carry the material.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(1)(c): 41-1a-102 "Vehicle" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(2): (3); (5) Except as provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(2)(a): operate a vehicle with an unsecured load on any highway; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(2)(b): operate a vehicle carrying trash or garbage without a covering over the entire load.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3): (3)(a); (3)(a); (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(a): A vehicle carrying dirt, sand, gravel, rock fragments, pebbles, crushed base, aggregate, any other similar material, or scrap metal shall have a covering over the entire load unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(a)(i): the highest point of the load does not extend above the top of any exterior wall or sideboard of the cargo compartment of the vehicle; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(a)(ii): the outer edges of the load are at least six inches below the top inside edges of the exterior walls or sideboards of the cargo compartment of the vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(b): (3)(a); (3)(a) The following material is exempt from the provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(b)(i): hot mix asphalt;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(b)(ii): construction debris or scrap metal if the debris or scrap metal is a size and in a form not susceptible to being blown out of the vehicle;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(b)(iii): material being transported across a highway between two parcels of property that would be contiguous but for the highway that is being crossed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(b)(iv): (3)(a) material listed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(3)(c): (3)(a) A chemical substance capable of coating or bonding a load so that the load is confined on a vehicle, may be considered a covering for purposes of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(4): (2) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(4)(a): being transported in a manner which is not a hazard or a potential hazard to the safe operation of the vehicle or to other highway users; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(4)(b): loaded in a manner that only allows minimal spillage.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(5)(a): An authorized vehicle performing snow removal services on a highway is exempt from the requirements of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(5)(b): This section does not prohibit the necessary spreading of any substance connected with highway maintenance, construction, securing traction, or snow removal.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6): 72-9-102
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(a): Any person suspected of operating a vehicle with an unsecured load on a highway may be issued a warning.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(b): Any person who violates this section is guilty of:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(b)(i): an infraction, if the violation creates a hazard but does not lead to a motor vehicle accident;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(b)(ii): a class B misdemeanor, if the violation creates a hazard that leads to a motor vehicle accident; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(b)(iii): a class A misdemeanor, if the violation creates a hazard that leads to a motor vehicle accident that results in the serious bodily injury or death of a person.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(c): A person who violates a provision of this section shall be fined not less than:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(c)(i): $200 for a violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(c)(ii): $500 for a second or subsequent violation within six years of a previous violation of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(d): 72-9-102 A person who violates a provision of this section while operating a commercial vehicle as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(d)(i): not less than $500 for a violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(6)(d)(ii): $1,000 for a second or subsequent violation within six years of a previous violation of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-409(7): As resources and opportunities allow, the department shall implement programs or activities that increase public awareness on the importance of properly securing loads.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-501 Purpose of part -- Utah-Federal Agreements ratified.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-501(1): The purpose of this part is to provide the statutory basis for the regulation of outdoor advertising consistent with zoning principles and standards and the public policy of this state in providing public safety, health, welfare, convenience and enjoyment of public travel, to protect the public investment in highways, to preserve the natural scenic beauty of lands bordering on highways, and to ensure that outdoor advertising shall be continued as a standardized medium of communication throughout the state so that it is preserved and can continue to provide general information in the specific interest of the traveling public safely and effectively.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-501(2): It is the purpose of this part to provide a statutory basis for the reasonable regulation of outdoor advertising consistent with the customary use, zoning principles and standards, the protection of private property rights, and the public policy relating to areas adjacent to the interstate, federal aid primary highway existing as of June 1, 1991, and the national highway systems highways.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-501(3): The agreement entered into between the governor of the state of Utah and the Secretary of Transportation of the United States dated January 18, 1968, regarding the size, lighting, and spacing of outdoor advertising which may be erected and maintained within areas adjacent to the interstate, federal aid primary highway existing as of June 1, 1991, and national highway systems highways which are zoned commercial or industrial or in other unzoned commercial or industrial areas as defined pursuant to the terms of the agreement is hereby ratified and approved, subject to subsequent amendments.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(1): "Clearly visible" means capable of being read without obstruction by an occupant of a vehicle traveling on the main traveled way of a street or highway within the visibility area.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(2): "Commercial or industrial activities" means those activities generally recognized as commercial or industrial by zoning authorities in this state, except that none of the following are commercial or industrial activities:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(2)(a): agricultural, forestry, grazing, farming, and related activities, including wayside fresh produce stands;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(2)(b): transient or temporary activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(2)(c): activities not visible from the main-traveled way;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(2)(d): activities conducted in a building principally used as a residence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(2)(e): railroad tracks and minor sidings.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a): "Commercial or industrial zone" means only:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a)(i): those areas within the boundaries of cities or towns that are used or reserved for business, commerce, or trade, or zoned as a highway service zone, under enabling state legislation or comprehensive local zoning ordinances or regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a)(ii): those areas within the boundaries of urbanized counties that are used or reserved for business, commerce, or trade, or zoned as a highway service zone, under enabling state legislation or comprehensive local zoning ordinances or regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a)(iii): those areas outside the boundaries of urbanized counties and outside the boundaries of cities and towns that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a)(iii)(A): are used or reserved for business, commerce, or trade, or zoned as a highway service zone, under comprehensive local zoning ordinances or regulations or enabling state legislation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a)(iii)(B): are within 8420 feet of an interstate highway exit, off-ramp, or turnoff as measured from the nearest point of the beginning or ending of the pavement widening at the exit from or entrance to the main-traveled way; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(a)(iv): those areas outside the boundaries of urbanized counties and outside the boundaries of cities and towns and not within 8420 feet of an interstate highway exit, off-ramp, or turnoff as measured from the nearest point of the beginning or ending of the pavement widening at the exit from or entrance to the main-traveled way that are reserved for business, commerce, or trade under enabling state legislation or comprehensive local zoning ordinances or regulations, and are actually used for commercial or industrial purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(3)(b): "Commercial or industrial zone" does not mean areas zoned for the sole purpose of allowing outdoor advertising.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(4): 10-9a-401; 10-9a-501; 17-27a-401; 17-27a-501 "Comprehensive local zoning ordinances or regulations" means a municipality's comprehensive plan required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(5): "Contiguous" means that a portion of one parcel of land is situated immediately adjacent to, and shares a common boundary with, a portion of another parcel of land.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(6): 72-7-501 "Controlled route" means any route where outdoor advertising control is mandated by state or federal law, including under this part and under the Utah-Federal Agreements described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(7): "Directional signs" means signs containing information about public places owned or operated by federal, state, or local governments or their agencies, publicly or privately owned natural phenomena, historic, cultural, scientific, educational, or religious sites, and areas of natural scenic beauty or naturally suited for outdoor recreation, that the department considers to be in the interest of the traveling public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(8): (8)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(8)(a): "Erect" means to construct, build, raise, assemble, place, affix, attach, create, paint, draw, or in any other way bring into being.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(8)(b): (8)(a) "Erect" does not include any activities defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(9): "Highway service zone" means a highway service area where the primary use of the land is used or reserved for commercial and roadside services other than outdoor advertising to serve the traveling public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(10): "Information center" means an area or site established and maintained at rest areas for the purpose of informing the public of:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(10)(a): places of interest within the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(10)(b): any other information that the department considers desirable.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(11): "Interchange or intersection" means those areas and their approaches where traffic is channeled off or onto an interstate route, excluding the deceleration lanes, acceleration lanes, or feeder systems, from or to another federal, state, county, city, or other route.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(12): "Maintain" means to allow to exist, subject to the provisions of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(13): "Maintenance" means to repair, refurbish, repaint, or otherwise keep an existing sign structure safe and in a state suitable for use, including signs destroyed by vandalism or an act of God.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(14): "Main-traveled way" means the through traffic lanes, including auxiliary lanes, acceleration lanes, deceleration lanes, and feeder systems, exclusive of frontage roads and ramps.  For a divided highway, there is a separate main-traveled way for the traffic in each direction.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(15): "Major sponsor" means a sponsor of a public assembly facility or of a team or event held at the facility where the amount paid by the sponsor to the owner of the facility, to the team, or for the event is at least $100,000 per year.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(16): "Official signs and notices" means signs and notices erected and maintained by public agencies within their territorial or zoning jurisdictions for the purpose of carrying out official duties or responsibilities in accordance with direction or authorization contained in federal, state, or local law.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(17): "Off-premise sign" means a sign located in an area zoned industrial, commercial, or H-1 and in an area determined by the department to be unzoned industrial or commercial that advertises an activity, service, event, person, or product located on premises other than the premises on which the sign is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(18): "On-premise sign" means a sign used to advertise the sale or lease of, or activities conducted on, the property on which the sign is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(19): "Outdoor advertising" means any outdoor advertising structure or outdoor structure used in combination with an outdoor advertising sign or outdoor sign within the outdoor advertising corridor which is visible from a place on the main-traveled way of a controlled route.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(20): "Outdoor advertising corridor" means a strip of land 660 feet wide, measured perpendicular from the edge of a controlled highway right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(21): "Outdoor advertising structure" or "outdoor structure" means any sign structure, including any necessary devices, supports, appurtenances, and lighting that is part of or supports an outdoor sign.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(22): "Point of widening" means the point of the gore or the point where the intersecting lane begins to parallel the other lanes of traffic, but the point of widening may never be greater than 2,640 feet from the center line of the intersecting highway of the interchange or intersection at grade.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(23): 59-12-602 "Public assembly facility" means a convention facility as defined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(23)(a): includes all contiguous interests in land, improvements, and utilities acquired, constructed, and used in connection with the operation of the public assembly facility, whether the interests are owned or held in fee title or a lease or easement for a term of at least 40 years, and regardless of whether the interests are owned or operated by separate governmental authorities or districts;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(23)(b): is wholly or partially funded by public money;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(23)(c): requires a person attending an event at the public assembly facility to purchase a ticket or that otherwise charges for the use of the public assembly facility as part of its regular operation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(23)(d): has a minimum and permanent seating capacity of at least 10,000 people.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(24): "Public assembly facility sign" means a sign located on a public assembly facility that only advertises the public assembly facility, major sponsors, events, the sponsors of events held or teams playing at the facility, and products sold or services conducted at the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(25): "Relocation" includes the removal of a sign from one situs together with the erection of a new sign upon another situs in a commercial or industrial zoned area as a substitute.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(26): "Relocation and replacement" means allowing all outdoor advertising signs or permits the right to maintain outdoor advertising along the interstate, federal aid primary highway existing as of June 1, 1991, and national highway system highways to be maintained in a commercial or industrial zoned area to accommodate the displacement, remodeling, or widening of the highway systems.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(27): "Remodel" means the upgrading, changing, alteration, refurbishment, modification, or complete substitution of a new outdoor advertising structure for one permitted pursuant to this part and that is located in a commercial or industrial area.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(28): "Rest area" means an area or site established and maintained within or adjacent to the right-of-way by or under public supervision or control for the convenience of the traveling public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(29): "Scenic or natural area" means an area determined by the department to have aesthetic value.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(30): "Traveled way" means that portion of the roadway used for the movement of vehicles, exclusive of shoulders and auxiliary lanes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31)(a): "Unzoned commercial or industrial area" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31)(a)(i): those areas not zoned by state law or local law, regulation, or ordinance that are occupied by one or more industrial or commercial activities other than outdoor advertising signs;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31)(a)(ii): the lands along the highway for a distance of 600 feet immediately adjacent to those activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31)(a)(iii): lands covering the same dimensions that are directly opposite those activities on the other side of the highway, if the department determines that those lands on the opposite side of the highway do not have scenic or aesthetic value.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31)(b): In measuring the scope of the unzoned commercial or industrial area, all measurements shall be made from the outer edge of the regularly used buildings, parking lots, storage, or processing areas of the activities and shall be along or parallel to the edge of pavement of the highway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(31)(c): All signs located within an unzoned commercial or industrial area become nonconforming if the commercial or industrial activity used in defining the area ceases for a continuous period of 12 months.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(32): "Urbanized county" means a county with a population of at least 125,000 persons.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(33): "Visibility area" means the area on a street or highway that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(33)(a): defined at one end by a line extending from the base of the billboard across all lanes of traffic of the street or highway in a plane that is perpendicular to the street or highway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(33)(b): defined on the other end by a line extending across all lanes of traffic of the street or highway in a plane that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(33)(b)(i): perpendicular to the street or highway; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-502(33)(b)(ii): 500 feet from the base of the billboard.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-503 Advertising -- Permit required -- Penalty for violation.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-503(1): It is unlawful for any person to place any form of advertising upon any part of the public domain, or within 660 feet of a public highway, except within the corporate limits of a city or town, and except upon land in private ownership situated along the highway, without first receiving a permit from the department, if a state highway, or from the county executive, if a county road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-503(2): Any person who violates this section is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5 Public assembly facility signs -- Restrictions.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(1): Signs on the premises of a public assembly facility that do not bring rental income to the owner of the public assembly facility may advertise:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(1)(a): the name of the facility, including identifiable venues or stores within the facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(1)(b): principal or accessory products or services offered on the property and activities conducted on the property as permitted by 23 C.F.R. Section 750.709, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(1)(b)(i): events being conducted in the facility or upon the premises, including the sponsor of the current event; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(1)(b)(ii): products or services sold at the facility and activities conducted on the property that produce significant income to the operation of the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(2): (1) An advertising structure described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(2)(a): shall be located on a public assembly facility or on a parcel contiguous to the public assembly facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(2)(b): shall be under the same ownership as the public assembly facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(2)(c): may not be separated from the public assembly facility by a public road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(3): (1) An advertising structure described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(4): (1) An advertising structure described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.5(5): A public assembly facility is exempt from the requirement under this part to have a state outdoor advertising permit.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6 Unified commercial development.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1): 72-7-502; (1)(d) As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(a): "Common areas" means sidewalks, roadways, landscaping, parking, storage, and service areas that are identified on the approved map provided to the department describing the unified commercial development as required by this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(b): 72-7-502
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(b)(i): 72-7-502 "Contiguous" includes parcels that are otherwise contiguous, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(b)(i)(A): a road, other than a controlled route, that provides access to the development;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(b)(i)(B): a railway right-of-way; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(b)(i)(C): land that is undevelopable.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(b)(ii): "Contiguous" does not include a parcel of land that is only physically connected to another parcel of land by a long, narrow strip.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(c): "Permit waiver" means written approval by the department, issued to the owner of a unified commercial development, to maintain a unified commercial development sign within the outdoor corridor that is within the boundaries of a unified commercial development per this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(d): (1)(d)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(d)(i): "Property," for purposes of the definition of " unified commercial development sign," includes all property within a unified commercial development upon which all owners in the development have irrevocable shared ownership and use rights and irrevocable shared obligations to the common areas, and specifically excludes any parcels of land within a unified commercial development that allow residential use.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(d)(ii): "Property" does not include development that involves merely reciprocal easements or use agreements among individual properties.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(d)(iii): (1)(d) If the owners in an approved unified commercial development subdivide the unified commercial development into individual parcels that do not meet the criteria in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e): "Unified commercial development" means a development that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e)(i): is used primarily for commercial or industrial activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e)(ii): is developed by a single developer, including successors, under a common development plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e)(iii): may include phased development;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e)(iv): consists solely of land that is contiguous;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e)(v): holds itself out to the public as a common development through signs and other marketing efforts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(e)(vi): received planning approval from the local land use authority and is recorded in the county in which the development was approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(f): "Unified commercial development sign" means a sign:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(f)(i): erected within an approved unified commercial development;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(f)(ii): erected within the outdoor advertising corridor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(1)(f)(iii): that advertises only the brands, logos, or trade names of businesses, products, services, and events that are available to the public at facilities on parcels within the boundaries of the unified commercial development.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(2)(a): The department shall issue a revocable permit waiver to the owner of a unified commercial development, approved by the local land use authority, for the erection and maintenance of a unified commercial development sign within the outdoor advertising corridor after receiving the development map that:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(2)(a)(ii)(C): included parcels, owners, and businesses within the development that would qualify to advertise on the unified commercial development sign in compliance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(2)(b): The entity holding a permit waiver under this section shall provide an updated list of all businesses located within the unified commercial development every 12 months from the date of issue of the unified commercial development permit waiver.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-504.6(2)(c): In the event that a parcel within the boundaries of the approved unified commercial development allows a residential use, is removed from the development, or does not include irrevocable ownership and use rights and obligations, that parcel shall be excluded from the unified commercial development for purposes of determining a legal site for the sign, and any business, product, service, or event occurring on that parcel shall be excluded from display upon the unified commercial development sign.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505 Sign size -- Sign spacing -- Location in outdoor advertising corridor -- Limit on implementation.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1): (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(a): (2) Except as provided in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(a)(ii): maximum length - 60 feet; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(a)(iii): maximum height - 25 feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(b): No more than two facings visible and readable from the same direction on the main-traveled way may be erected on any one sign structure.  Whenever two facings are so positioned, neither shall exceed the maximum allowed square footage.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(c): Two or more advertising messages on a sign face and double-faced, back-to-back, stacked, side-by-side, and V-type signs are permitted as a single sign or structure if both faces enjoy common ownership.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(d): A changeable message sign is permitted if the interval between message changes is not more frequent than at least eight seconds and the actual message rotation process is accomplished in three seconds or less.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(1)(e): An illumination standard adopted by any jurisdiction shall be uniformly applied to all signs, public or private, on or off premise.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(2)(a): An outdoor sign structure located inside the unincorporated area of a nonurbanized county may have the maximum height allowed by the county for outdoor advertising structures in the commercial or industrial zone in which the sign is located.  If no maximum height is provided for the location, the maximum sign height may be 65 feet above the ground or 25 feet above the grade of the main traveled way, whichever is greater.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-505(2)(b): An outdoor sign structure located inside an incorporated municipality or urbanized county may have the maximum height allowed by the municipality or urbanized county for outdoor advertising structures in the commercial or industrial zone in which the sign is located.  If no maximum height is provided for the location, the maximum sign height may be 65 feet above the ground or 25 feet above the grade of the main traveled way, whichever is greater.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(1)(a): control the erection and maintenance of outdoor advertising along the interstate and primary highway systems;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(1)(c): establish the form, content, and submittal of applications to erect outdoor advertising; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(1)(d): establish administrative procedures.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(2): In addition to all other statutory notice requirements:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(2)(a): the department shall give reasonably timely written notice to all outdoor advertising permit holders of any changes or proposed changes in administrative rules made under authority of this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-506(2)(b): any county, municipality, or governmental entity shall, upon written request, give reasonably timely written notice to all outdoor advertising permit holders within its jurisdiction of any change or proposed change to the outdoor or off-premise advertising provisions of its zoning provisions, codes, or ordinances.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508 Unlawful outdoor advertising -- Adjudicative proceedings -- Judicial review -- Costs of removal -- Civil and criminal liability for damaging regulated signs -- Immunity for Department of Transportation.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(1): Outdoor advertising is unlawful when:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(1)(a): erected after May 9, 1967, contrary to the provisions of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(1)(b): a permit is not obtained as required by this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(1)(c): a false or misleading statement has been made in the application for a permit that was material to obtaining the permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(1)(d): the sign for which a permit was issued is not in a reasonable state of repair, is unsafe, or is otherwise in violation of this part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(1)(e): a sign in the outdoor advertising corridor is permitted by the local zoning authority as an on-premise sign and the sign, from time to time or continuously, advertises an activity, service, event, person, or product located on property other than the property on which the sign is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(2): The establishment, operation, repair, maintenance, or alteration of any sign contrary to this chapter is also a public nuisance.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7): The following criteria shall be used for determining whether an existing sign within an interstate outdoor advertising corridor has as its purpose unlawful off-premise outdoor advertising:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(a): whether the sign complies with this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(b): whether the premise includes an area:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(b)(i): from which the general public is serviced according to normal industry practices for organizations of that type; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(b)(ii): that is directly connected to or is involved in carrying out the activities and normal industry practices of the advertised activities, services, events, persons, or products;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(c): whether the sign generates revenue:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(c)(i): arising from the advertisement of activities, services, events, or products not available on the premise according to normal industry practices for organizations of that type;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(c)(iii)(B): securities;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(c)(iii)(F): promise of future payment or compensation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(c)(iii)(G): forbearance of debt;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(d)(i): carries on hours of operation on the premise comparable to the normal industry practice for a business, service, or operation of that type, or posts the hours of operation on the premise in public view;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(d)(ii): has available utilities comparable to the normal industry practice for an entity of that type; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(d)(iii): has a current valid business license or permit under applicable local ordinances, state law, and federal law to conduct business on the premise upon which the sign is located;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(e): whether the advertisement is located on the site of any auxiliary facility that is not essential to, or customarily used in, the ordinary course of business for the activities, services, events, persons, or products being advertised; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-508(7)(f): whether the sign or advertisement is located on property that is not contiguous to a property that is essential and customarily used for conducting the business of the activities, services, events, persons, or products being advertised.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-511 Violation of part -- Misdemeanor.
----------------------------------------------------------------
A person who violates any provision of this part is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-512 Appeals by attorney general.
-----------------------------------------------------------
The attorney general may take such appeals as are provided for in 23 U.S.C., Sec. 131.
