Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514 Landscape control program.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(1): As used in this section, "landscape control" means trimming or removal of seedlings, saplings, trees and vegetation along the interstate, federal aid primary highway existing as of June 1, 1991, and national highway system right-of-way to provide clear visibility of outdoor advertising.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(2)(a): The department shall establish a landscape control program as provided under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(2)(b): Except as provided in this section, a person, including an outdoor advertising sign owner or business owner may not perform or cause landscape control to be performed.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(a): An outdoor advertising sign owner or business owner may submit a request for landscape control to the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b): (3)(a) Within 60 days of the request under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b)(i): conduct a field review of the request with a representative of the sign or business owner, the department, and the Federal Highway Administration to consider the following issues listed in their order of priority:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b)(i)(A): safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b)(i)(B): protection of highway features, including right-of-way and landscaping;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b)(i)(C): aesthetics; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b)(i)(D): motorists' view of the sign or business; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(b)(ii): notify the sign or business owner what, if any, trimming, removal, restoration, banking, or other landscape control shall be allowed as decided by the department, after consultation with the Federal Highway Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(3)(c): If the sign or business owner elects to proceed, in accordance with the decision issued under this subsection, the department shall issue a permit that describes what landscape control may be allowed, assigns responsibility for costs, describes the safety measures to be observed, and attaches any explanatory plans or other information.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(4): (3) The department shall establish an appeals process within the department for landscape control decisions made under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(5): (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(5)(a): A person who performs landscape control in violation of this section is guilty of a class C misdemeanor, and is liable to the owner for treble the amount of damages sustained to the landscape.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-514(5)(b): (5)(a) Each permit issued under this section shall notify the permit holder of the penalties under Subsection

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-602(1): A railroad entity may not construct a new highway-railroad grade crossing without first obtaining written authorization from the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-602(2): (4) Subject to Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-7-602(2)(e): allocate responsibilities, including costs, for the alteration, abolition, or separation of any highway-railroad grade crossing in the state between each affected railroad entity and highway authority.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 8 - Pedestrian Safety and Facilities Act
*********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Pedestrian Safety and Facilities Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-102(1): "Construction" means the function of constructing or reconstructing a sidewalk with or without curb and gutter and includes land acquisition and engineering or inspection as defined by the rules and regulations of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-102(2): "Curb and gutter" means the area between the roadway and sidewalk designed for water runoff and providing a barrier for safety of pedestrian and vehicular traffic.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-102(3): "Participating municipality" means a city of the third, fourth, or fifth class or a town.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-102(4): "Pedestrian safety devices" means any device or method designed to foster the safety of pedestrian traffic including sidewalks, curbs, gutters, and pedestrian overpasses.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-103 Designated county and municipal sidewalks -- Construction on easements granted by transportation department.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-103(1): All sidewalks, including curbs and gutters within the unincorporated areas of a county and within nonparticipating municipalities situated within the county, are designated county sidewalks. All sidewalks within participating municipalities are designated municipal sidewalks.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-103(2): Counties and participating municipalities may construct and maintain curbs, gutters, sidewalks, and pedestrian safety devices adjacent to the traveled portion of state highways upon easements that may be granted by the department. The department shall cooperate with counties and participating municipalities to accomplish pedestrian safety construction and maintenance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-103(3): A county or municipality may construct and maintain pedestrian safety devices on state highways in compliance with rules made by the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104 Funding priorities by county and municipality officials -- Factors.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(1): A county or municipality may use a portion of their B and C road funds for pedestrian safety devices under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2): The county legislative body of the counties and the governing officials of participating municipalities may establish funding priorities relating to construction of curbs, gutters, sidewalks, or other pedestrian safety construction, with funds permitted to be expended by this part, based on factors including, but not limited to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2)(a): existing useable rights-of-way;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2)(b): vehicle-pedestrian accident experience;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2)(c): average daily vehicle traffic;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2)(d): average daily pedestrian traffic;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2)(e): average daily school age pedestrian traffic; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(2)(f): speed of vehicle traffic.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-104(3): All construction performed under this part shall be barrier free to wheelchairs at crosswalks and intersections.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-105 Pedestrian safety to be considered in highway planning.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A highway authority shall consider pedestrian safety in all highway engineering and planning where pedestrian traffic may be a significant factor on all projects within the state or any of its political subdivisions.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-106 Rules and regulations -- Cooperation with the county legislative body.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall:Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-106(1): make rules providing for uniform accounting of the funds permitted to be expended for curbs, gutters, sidewalks, and pedestrian safety devices, as provided in this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-106(2): cooperate with the county executives and county legislative bodies and the governing officials of participating municipalities in order to implement this part and make rules required by this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-107 County or city granting exemption from construction -- Not eligible to utilize funds under part.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-107(1): This part may not be construed to substitute or replace the construction of curbs, gutters, sidewalks, or pedestrian safety devices by any counties or participating municipalities.  Funds expended under this part are in addition to funds normally used by counties and participating municipalities for pedestrian safety devices and may not be used in substitution for local funding.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-107(2): If any county or participating municipalities or any of their agencies grant an exemption or deferral agreement for the construction of sidewalks, curbs, gutters, or pedestrian safety devices which are otherwise normally required, the area for which the exemption or deferral agreement applies is not be eligible to utilize funds permitted to be expended by this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-109 Safe Routes to School Program.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-109(1): As part of providing for the safety of the state transportation system, the department shall establish a program that promotes walking and bicycling to school through infrastructure improvements and noninfrastructure efforts such as safety awareness education.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-109(2): In addition to any federal funds made available to the department for the program, the department may fund the program from money made available to the department by the Legislature and as prioritized by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-109(3): The department, in consultation with the State Board of Education, may give priority consideration to a project located in an area of a school that receives funding under the Elementary and Secondary Education Act of 1965, Title I, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 6301, et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-8-109(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with


Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 9 - Motor Carrier Safety Act
*********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Motor Carrier Safety Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(a): "Commercial vehicle" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(a)(i): an interstate commercial vehicle; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(a)(ii): an intrastate commercial vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(b): "Commercial vehicle" does not include the following vehicles for purposes of this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(b)(i): equipment owned and operated by the United States Department of Defense when driven by any active duty military personnel and members of the reserves and national guard on active duty including personnel on full-time national guard duty, personnel on part-time training, and national guard military technicians and civilians who are required to wear military uniforms and are subject to the code of military justice;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(b)(ii): firefighting and emergency vehicles, operated by emergency personnel, not including commercial tow trucks;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(b)(iii): recreational vehicles that are driven solely as family or personal conveyances for noncommercial purposes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(1)(b)(iv): vehicles owned by the state or a local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2): "Interstate commercial vehicle" means a self-propelled or towed motor vehicle used on a highway in interstate commerce to transport passengers or property if the vehicle:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2)(a): has a gross vehicle weight rating or gross vehicle weight of 10,001 or more pounds, or gross combination weight rating or gross combination weight of 10,001 or more pounds, whichever is greater;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2)(b): is designed or used to transport more than eight passengers, including the driver, for compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2)(c): is designed or used to transport more than 15 passengers, including the driver, and is not used to transport passengers for compensation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2)(d)(i): is used to transport materials designated as hazardous in accordance with 49 U.S.C. Sec. 5103; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(2)(d)(ii): is required to be placarded in accordance with regulations under 49 C.F.R., Subtitle B, Chapter I, Subchapter C.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3): "Intrastate commercial vehicle" means a motor vehicle, vehicle, trailer, or semitrailer used or maintained for business, compensation, or profit to transport passengers or property on a highway only within the boundaries of this state if the commercial vehicle:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(a)(i): has a manufacturer's gross vehicle weight rating or gross vehicle weight, or gross combination weight rating or gross combination weight of 26,001 or more pounds, whichever is greater, and is operated by an individual who is 18 years old or older; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(a)(ii): has a manufacturer's gross vehicle weight rating or gross combination weight rating of 16,001 or more pounds and is operated by an individual who is under 18 years old;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(b)(i): is designed to transport more than 15 passengers, including the driver; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(b)(ii): is designed to transport more than 12 passengers, including the driver, and has a manufacturer's gross vehicle weight rating or gross combination weight rating of 13,000 or more pounds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(3)(c): is used in the transportation of hazardous materials and is required to be placarded in accordance with 49 C.F.R.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(4): "Motor carrier" means a person engaged in or transacting the business of transporting passengers, freight, merchandise, or other property by a commercial vehicle on a highway within this state and includes a tow truck business.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(5): 41-1a-102 "Owner" as pertaining to a vehicle, vessel, or outboard motor, means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(6): "Property owner" means the owner or lessee of real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(7): 41-1a-102 "State impound yard" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(8): "Tow truck" means a motor vehicle constructed, designed, altered, or equipped primarily for the purpose of towing or removing damaged, disabled, abandoned, seized, or impounded vehicles from a highway or other place by means of a crane, hoist, tow bar, tow line, dolly, tilt bed, or other means.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(9): "Tow truck motor carrier" means a motor carrier that is engaged in or transacting business for tow truck services.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(10): "Tow truck operator" means an individual that performs operations related to a tow truck service as an employee or as an independent contractor on behalf of a tow truck motor carrier.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(11): "Tow truck service" means the functions and any ancillary operations associated with recovering, removing, and towing a vehicle and its load from a highway or other place by means of a tow truck.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-102(12): "Transportation" means the actual movement of property or passengers by motor vehicle, including loading, unloading, and any ancillary service provided by the motor carrier in connection with movement by motor vehicle, which is performed by or on behalf of the motor carrier, its employees or agents, or under the authority of the motor carrier, its employees or agents, or under the apparent authority and with the knowledge of the motor carrier.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-104 Motor carriers to operate under chapter.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
A motor carrier may not operate any commercial vehicle for the transportation of persons or property on any public highway in this state except in accordance with this chapter, and rules and orders of the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201 Motor Carrier Advisory Board created -- Appointment -- Terms -- Meetings -- Per diem and expenses -- Duties.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(1): There is created within the department the Motor Carrier Advisory Board consisting of five members appointed by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(2): Each member of the board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(2)(a): represent experience and expertise in the areas of motor carrier transportation, commerce, agriculture, economics, shipping, or highway safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(2)(b): be selected at large on a nonpartisan basis; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(2)(c): have been a legal resident of the state for at least one year immediately preceding the date of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(3): (3)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(3)(a): (3)(b) Except as required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(3)(b): The department shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of board members are staggered so that approximately half of the board is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(3)(c): A member shall serve from the date of appointment until a replacement is appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(4): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the department shall appoint the replacement to serve for the remainder of the unexpired term beginning the day following the day on which the vacancy occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(5): The board shall elect its own chair and vice chair at the first regular meeting of each calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(6): The board shall meet at least twice per year or as needed when called by the chair.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(7): Any three voting members constitute a quorum for the transaction of business that comes before the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(9): The board shall advise the department and the commission on interpretation, adoption, and implementation of this chapter and other motor carrier related issues.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-201(10): The department shall provide staff support to the board.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-302(3): An agreement may allow the exchange of information for audit, reporting, and enforcement purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401 Liability of motor carriers for loss or damage to freight.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(1)(a): A motor carrier receiving property for transportation from one point in this state to another point in this state shall issue a receipt or bill of lading for the property, and shall be liable to the lawful holder of the property for any loss, damage, or injury to the property caused by the motor carrier, or by any motor carrier to which the property may be delivered or over whose line or lines the property may pass within this state when transported on a through bill of lading.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(1)(b): A contract, receipt, rule, regulation, or other limitation of any character whatsoever may not exempt the motor carrier from this liability.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(2): A motor carrier that receives property for transportation or any motor carrier delivering the property to the consignee shall be liable to the lawful holder of the receipt or bill of lading, or to any party entitled to recover on the property whether the receipt or bill of lading has been issued or not, for the full actual loss, damage or injury to the property caused by the motor carrier, or by any motor carrier to which the property may have been delivered or over whose line or lines the property may have passed within this state when transported on a through bill of lading.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(3): (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(3)(a): (2) The provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(3)(b): Any limitation of liability is unlawful and void if the provisions respecting liability for full actual loss, damage, or injury notwithstanding any limitation of liability or of recovery, or any representation or agreement or release as to value to property, except livestock, received for transportation concerning which the motor carrier expressly authorizes or requires, by order of the commission, the establishment and maintenance of rates dependent upon the value declared in writing by the shipper or agreed to in writing as the released value of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-401(3)(c): The declaration or agreement shall have no other effect than to limit liability and recovery to an amount not exceeding the value so declared or agreed upon.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-402 Limitation of time for presenting claims and bringing suit.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-402(1): A motor carrier shall allow at least:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-402(1)(a): 90 days for giving notice of claims for any loss, damage, or injury to property;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-402(1)(b): four months for the filing of claims; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-402(1)(c): two years for the institution of suits.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-402(2): If the loss or injury complained of is due to delay or damage while being loaded or unloaded, or damage in transit caused by carelessness or negligence, a notice of claim or a filing of claim is not required as a condition precedent to recovery.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-403 Contribution between connecting motor carriers.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-403(1): The motor carrier paying for the loss or damage to property transported or received is entitled to recovery from the motor carrier responsible for the loss or damage, or on the motor carrier's line the loss, damage, or injury was sustained.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-403(2): The amount of the loss or damage is equal to the amount the motor carrier is required to pay to the persons entitled to the recovery.

-------------------------------------------------------
Bills of lading issued by any motor carrier for the transportation of goods within this state shall conform to this chapter, rules made under this chapter, and

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-604(10): If a tow truck motor carrier is dispatched as part of a towing rotation, the tow truck operator that responds may not respond to the location in a tow truck that is owned by a tow truck motor carrier that is different than the tow truck motor carrier that was dispatched.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-605 Exception from part.
---------------------------------------------------
This part does not apply to a person who is towing a vehicle owned by that person in a noncommercial operation.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-607 Required process before removal from towing rotation.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-607(1): Each political subdivision or state agency that establishes a towing rotation to facilitate tows initiated by the political subdivision or state agency shall establish a policy for an appeals process to hear and decide appeals from a decision to suspend or remove a tow truck motor carrier or tow truck operator from a towing rotation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-607(2): (1) In conducting an appeal as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-607(2)(a): the appeal process may be conducted by a single appeal officer or a panel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-607(2)(b): an individual hearing an appeal, whether as a single appeal officer or as part of a panel, may not be the same individual who made the decision to suspend or remove the tow truck motor carrier or tow truck operator from the towing rotation.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-701 Penalty for unlawful conduct.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-701(1): Unless otherwise specified, any person who violates a provision of this chapter or who aids or abets another person in a violation of this chapter is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-701(2): A second or subsequent conviction for a violation of this chapter or of aiding or abetting another person in a violation of this chapter is a class A misdemeanor.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-702 Existing rights of action unaffected -- Penalties cumulative.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-702(1): This chapter may not be construed to have the effect of releasing or waiving any right of action by the state, the department or any person for any right, penalty, or forfeiture which may have arisen or occurred under any law of this state before May 10, 1983, or which arises or occurs after May 10, 1983.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-702(2): All penalties accruing under this chapter are cumulative, and a suit for the recovery of one penalty is not a bar to and shall not affect the recovery of any other penalty or forfeiture, and is not a bar to any criminal prosecution against any motor carrier, or any officer, director, agent, or employee of a motor carrier, or any other corporation or person, or a bar to the exercise by the department, through the court, of its power to punish for contempt.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703 Civil penalties for violations -- Compromise.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(1): In addition to any other penalties, a motor carrier that fails or neglects to comply with any provision of the Constitution of this state, statute, or any rule or order of the department is subject to a civil penalty of not less than $500 nor more than $2,000 for each offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(2): Every violation of any provision of the constitution of this state, statute, or any rule or order of the department, is a separate and distinct offense.  Each day's continuance of the violation is a separate and distinct offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(3)(a): The civil penalty may be compromised by the department and a determination of compromise is appealable by the person alleged to have committed the violation.  In determining the amount of the penalty or the amount agreed upon in compromise, the department shall consider the:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(3)(a)(i): gravity of the violation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(3)(a)(ii): good faith of the person charged in attempting to achieve compliance after notification of the violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(3)(b): The amount of the penalty when finally determined or the amount agreed upon in compromise may be deducted from any sums owing by the state to the person charged or may be recovered in a civil action in the courts of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-703(4): In construing and enforcing the provisions of this chapter relating to penalties, the act, omission, or failure of any officer, agent, or employee of any motor carrier, acting within the scope of his official duties or employment, is deemed to be the act, omission, or failure of the motor carrier.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-704 Assignment of administrative law judge.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-704(1): The department shall assign an administrative law judge to hear contested matters.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-704(2): The administrative law judge's orders shall be reviewed by the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-9-705 Disposition of fees and civil fines.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
All fees and civil fines received and collected under this chapter shall be transmitted daily to the state treasurer and deposited in the Transportation Fund.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 10 - Aeronautics Act
*************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Aeronautics Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(1): "Acrobatics" means the intentional maneuvers of an aircraft not necessary to air navigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(a): "Advanced air mobility system" means a system that transports individuals and property using piloted and unpiloted aircraft, including electric aircraft and electric vertical takeoff and landing aircraft, in controlled or uncontrolled airspace.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b): (2)(a) "Advanced air mobility system" includes each component of a system described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b)(i): the aircraft, including payload;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b)(ii): communications equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b)(iii): navigation equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b)(iv): controllers;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b)(v): support equipment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(2)(b)(vi): remote and autonomous functions.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(3): "Aerial transit corridor" means an airspace volume defining a three-dimensional route segment with performance requirements to operate within or to cross where tactical air traffic control separation services are not provided.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(4): "Aeronautics" means transportation by aircraft, air instruction, the operation, repair, or maintenance of aircraft, and the design, operation, repair, or maintenance of airports, or other air navigation facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(5): "Aeronautics instructor" means any individual engaged in giving or offering to give instruction in aeronautics, flying, or ground subjects, either with or without:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(5)(a): compensation or other reward;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(5)(b): advertising the occupation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(5)(c): calling his facilities an air school, or any equivalent term; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(5)(d): employing or using other instructors.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(6): "Aircraft" means any contrivance now known or in the future invented, used, or designed for navigation of or flight in the air.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(7): "Air instruction" means the imparting of aeronautical information by any aviation instructor or in any air school or flying club.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(8): "Airport" means any area of land, water, or both, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(8)(a): is used or is made available for landing and takeoff;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(8)(b): provides facilities for the shelter, supply, and repair of aircraft, and handling of passengers and cargo;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(8)(c): meets the minimum requirements established by the department as to size and design, surface, marking, equipment, and operation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(8)(d): includes all areas shown as part of the airport in the current airport layout plan as approved by the Federal Aviation Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(9): "Airport authority" means a political subdivision of the state, other than a county or municipality, that is authorized by statute to operate an airport.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(10): "Airport operator" means a municipality, county, or airport authority that owns or operates a commercial airport.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a): "Airport revenue" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i): all fees, charges, rents, or other payments received by or accruing to an airport operator for any of the following reasons:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(A): revenue from air carriers, tenants, lessees, purchasers of airport properties, airport permittees making use of airport property and services, and other parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(B): revenue received from the activities of others or the transfer of rights to others relating to the airport, including revenue received:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(B)(I): for the right to conduct an activity on the airport or to use or occupy airport property;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(B)(II): for the sale, transfer, or disposition of airport real or personal property, or any interest in that property, including transfer through a condemnation proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(B)(III): for the sale of, or the sale or lease of rights in, mineral, natural, or agricultural products or water owned by the airport operator to be taken from the airport; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(B)(IV): for the right to conduct an activity on, or for the use or disposition of, real or personal property or any interest in real or personal property owned or controlled by the airport operator and used for an airport-related purpose but not located on the airport; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(i)(C): revenue received from activities conducted by the airport operator whether on or off the airport, which is directly connected to the airport operator's ownership or operation of the airport; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(a)(ii): state and local taxes on aviation fuel.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(11)(b): "Airport revenue" does not include amounts received by an airport operator as passenger facility fees pursuant to 49 U.S.C. Sec. 40117.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(12): "Air school" means any person engaged in giving, offering to give, or advertising, representing, or holding himself out as giving, with or without compensation or other reward, instruction in aeronautics, flying, or ground subjects, or in more than one of these subjects.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(13): "Airworthiness" means conformity with requirements prescribed by the Federal Aviation Administration regarding the structure or functioning of aircraft, engine, parts, or accessories.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(14): "Civil aircraft" means any aircraft other than a public aircraft.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(15): "Commercial aircraft" means aircraft used for commercial purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(16): "Commercial airport" means a landing area, landing strip, or airport that may be used for commercial operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(17): "Commercial flight operator" means a person who conducts commercial operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(18): "Commercial operations" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(18)(a): any operations of an aircraft for compensation or hire or any services performed incidental to the operation of any aircraft for which a fee is charged or compensation is received, including the servicing, maintaining, and repairing of aircraft, the rental or charter of aircraft, the operation of flight or ground schools, the operation of aircraft for the application or distribution of chemicals or other substances, and the operation of aircraft for hunting and fishing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(18)(b): the brokering or selling of any of these services; but
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(18)(c): does not include any operations of aircraft as common carriers certificated by the federal government or the services incidental to those operations.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(19): 77-16b-102 "Correctional facility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(20): "Dealer" means any person who is actively engaged in the business of flying for demonstration purposes, or selling or exchanging aircraft, and who has an established place of business.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(21): "Experimental aircraft" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(21)(a): any aircraft designated by the Federal Aviation Administration or the military as experimental and used solely for the purpose of experiments, or tests regarding the structure or functioning of aircraft, engines, or their accessories; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(21)(b): any aircraft designated by the Federal Aviation Administration as:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(21)(b)(i): being custom or amateur built; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(21)(b)(ii): used for recreational, educational, or display purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(22): "Flight" means any kind of locomotion by aircraft while in the air.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(23): "Flying club" means five or more persons who for neither profit nor reward own, lease, or use one or more aircraft for the purpose of instruction, pleasure, or both.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(24): "Glider" means an aircraft heavier than air, similar to an airplane, but without a power plant.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(25): "Mechanic" means a person who constructs, repairs, adjusts, inspects, or overhauls aircraft, engines, or accessories.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(26): "Parachute jumper" means any person who has passed the required test for jumping with a parachute from an aircraft, and has passed an examination showing that he possesses the required physical and mental qualifications for the jumping.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(27): "Parachute rigger" means any person who has passed the required test for packing, repairing, and maintaining parachutes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(28): "Passenger aircraft" means aircraft used for transporting persons, in addition to the pilot or crew, with or without their necessary personal belongings.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(29): "Person" means any individual, corporation, limited liability company, or association of individuals.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(30): "Pilot" means any person who operates the controls of an aircraft while in-flight.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(31): "Primary glider" means any glider that has a gliding angle of less than 10 to one.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(32): "Public aircraft" means an aircraft used exclusively in the service of any government or of any political subdivision, including the government of the United States, of the District of Columbia, and of any state, territory, or insular possession of the United States, but not including any government-owned aircraft engaged in carrying persons or goods for commercial purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(33): "Reckless flying" means the operation or piloting of any aircraft recklessly, or in a manner as to endanger the property, life, or body of any person, due regard being given to the prevailing weather conditions, field conditions, and to the territory being flown over.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(34): "Registration number" means the number assigned by the Federal Aviation Administration to any aircraft, whether or not the number includes a letter or letters.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(35): "Secondary glider" means any glider that has a gliding angle between 10 to one and 16 to one, inclusive.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(36): "Soaring glider" means any glider that has a gliding angle of more than 16 to one.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(37): "Unmanned aircraft" means an aircraft that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(37)(a): capable of sustaining flight; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(37)(b): operated with no possible direct human intervention from on or within the aircraft.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38): "Unmanned aircraft system" means the entire system used to operate an unmanned aircraft, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38)(a): the unmanned aircraft, including payload;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38)(b): communications equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38)(c): navigation equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38)(d): controllers;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38)(e): support equipment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(38)(f): autopilot functionality.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(39): "Unmanned aircraft system traffic management" means a traffic management ecosystem for uncontrolled operations, including unmanned aircraft systems, that is separate from, but complementary to, the Federal Aviation Administration's air traffic management  system.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-102(40): "Vertiport" means an area of land, or a structure, used or intended to be used for electric, hydrogen, and hybrid vertical aircraft landings and takeoffs, including associated buildings and facilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103 Rulemaking requirement.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(1)(a): governing the establishment, location, and use of air navigation facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(1)(b): regulating the use, licensing, and supervision of all airports and vertiports in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(1)(c): establishing minimum standards with which all air navigation facilities, flying clubs, aircraft, gliders, pilots, and airports must comply; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(1)(d): safeguarding from accident and protecting the safety of persons operating or using aircraft and persons and property on the ground.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(2): The rules may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(2)(a): require that any device or accessory that forms part of any aircraft or its equipment be certified as complying with this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(2)(b): limit the use of any device or accessory as necessary for safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(2)(c): develop and promote aeronautics within this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(3)(a): To avoid the danger of accident incident to confusion arising from conflicting rules governing aeronautics, the rules shall conform as nearly as possible with federal legislation, rules, regulations, and orders on aeronautics.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(3)(b): The rules may not be inconsistent with paramount federal legislation, rules, regulations, and orders on the subject.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(4): The department may not require any pilot, aircraft, or mechanic who has procured a license under the Civil Aeronautics Authority of the United States to obtain a license from this state, other than required by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(5): The department may not make rules that conflict with the regulations of:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(5)(a): the Civil Aeronautics Authority; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(5)(b): other federal agencies authorized to regulate the particular activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-103(6): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The department shall comply with the procedures and requirements of


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104 Investigations and hearings -- Powers.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(1): The department may conduct investigations, inquiries, and hearings concerning matters covered by this chapter and accidents or injuries incident to the operation of aircraft occurring within this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(2): The department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(2)(a): administer oaths and affirmations;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(2)(b): certify to all official acts;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(2)(c): issue subpoenas;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(2)(d): compel the attendance and testimony of witnesses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(2)(e): compel the production of papers, books, and documents.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(3)(a): If any person fails to comply with any subpoena or order issued by the department, the department may petition any district court in this state to order compliance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(3)(b): The district court may order the person to comply with the requirements of the subpoena or order of the department, or to give evidence upon the matter in question.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-104(3)(c): Any failure to obey the order of the court may be punished by the court as contempt.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-105 Reports of investigations or hearings -- Restrictions on use -- Employees of department not required to testify.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-105(1): The reports of investigations or hearings, or any part of them, may not be admitted in evidence or used for any purpose in any suit, action, or proceeding growing out of any matter referred to in the investigations or hearings, or in any report of them, except in case of criminal or other proceedings instituted by or on behalf of the department under this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-105(2): An employee of the department may not be required to testify to any fact ascertained in or information gained by reason of his official capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-105(3): The employees of the department may not be required to testify as expert witnesses in any suit, action, or proceeding involving any aircraft or any navigation facility.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106 Enforcement of chapter -- Fees for services by department.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(1)(a): The department and every county and municipal officer required to enforce state laws shall enforce and assist in the enforcement of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(1)(b): The department may enforce this chapter by injunction in the district courts of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(1)(c): Other departments and political subdivisions of this state may cooperate with the department in the development of aeronautics within this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(2)(a): Unless otherwise provided by statute, the department may adopt a schedule of fees assessed for services provided by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(2)(b): Each fee shall be reasonable and fair, and shall reflect the cost of the service provided.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(2)(c): Each fee established in this manner shall be submitted to and approved by the Legislature as part of the department's annual appropriations request.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-106(2)(d): The department may not charge or collect any fee proposed in this manner without approval by the Legislature.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall conduct adjudicative proceedings in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-108 Payment of expenses of administration.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
The department shall pay the expenses of the administration of this part out of the special funds set up by the state treasurer for that purpose.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-109 Certificate of registration of aircraft required -- Exceptions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-109(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-109(1)(a): A person may not operate, pilot, or navigate, or cause or authorize to be operated, piloted, or navigated within this state any civil aircraft domiciled in this state unless the aircraft has a current certificate of registration issued by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-109(1)(b): (1)(a) The restriction described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-109(2): (1) Aircraft centrally assessed by the State Tax Commission are exempt from the state registration requirement under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-110 Aircraft registration information requirements -- Registration fee -- Administration -- Partial year registration.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-110(1): All applications for aircraft registration shall contain:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-113 Pilot's certificate of competency required -- Exceptions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-113(1): A person may not pilot within this state any civil aircraft unless that person is the holder of a currently effective pilot's certificate of competency issued by the government of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-113(2): This restriction does not apply to any person operating any aircraft licensed by a foreign country with which the United States has a reciprocal agreement covering the operation of the licensed aircraft.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-114 Mechanic's certificate of competency.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-114(1): Mechanics will be rated as airframe or powerplant mechanics.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-114(2): A person may hold a plurality of certificate of competency, including both classes of mechanic's certificate of competency or a pilot's and mechanic's certificate of competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-114(3): The certificate shall be a currently effective certificate of competency issued by the government of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-114(4): This restriction does not apply to mechanics employed by the United States government.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-115 Certificate carried subject to inspection -- Burden of proving validity of certificate in criminal proceedings.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-115(1): The certificate of license or permit required of a pilot or a student shall be kept in the personal possession of a licensee or permittee operating an aircraft within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-115(2): The certificate of license required for an aircraft shall be carried in the aircraft at all times and shall be conspicuously posted in clear view of passengers.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-115(3): The certificate of pilot's license, student's permit, or aircraft license shall be presented for inspection upon the demand of any peace officer of this state, any authorized official or employee of the department, or any official, manager, or person in charge of any airport in this state upon which it shall land, or upon the reasonable request of any other person.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-115(4): In any criminal prosecution under this title, a defendant who relies upon a license or permit of any kind has the burden of proving that the defendant is properly licensed or is the possessor of a proper license or permit.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-115(5): The fact of nonissuance of a license or permit may be evidenced by a certificate signed by the official having power of issuance, or his deputy, under seal of office, stating that a diligent search in the office records has been made and that from the records it appears that no license or permit was issued.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116 Restrictions on use of lands or waters of another.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116(1)(a): The landing or taking off of aircraft on or from the lands or waters of another without consent is unlawful, except in the case of a forced landing.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116(1)(b): For damages caused by a takeoff or landing, the owner, lessee of the aircraft, operator, or any of them is liable.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116(2)(a): A student pilot may not land on any area without the knowledge of the operator, instructor, or school from which the student is flying.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-116(2)(b): The use of private landing fields must not impose a hazard upon the person or property of others.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117 Aircraft landing permits -- Eligible aircraft -- Special licenses -- Rules -- Proof of insurance -- Bonds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(1)(a): The county executive of any county may issue a permit authorizing an aircraft to land on or take off from designated county roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(1)(b): The county executive of any county may issue a permit to an aircraft operated:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(1)(b)(i): as an air ambulance;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(1)(b)(ii): as a pesticide applicator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(1)(b)(iii): by or under contract with a public utility and used in connection with inspection, maintenance, installation, operation, construction, or repair of property owned or operated by the public utility.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(2): The county executive of any county may issue a permit under this section to other aircraft under rules made by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(3)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(3)(a)(i): an aircraft permitted by a county executive to land on a county road; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(3)(a)(ii): a pilot permitted to operate an aircraft licensed under this subsection from a county road.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(3)(b): The rules made under this subsection shall include provisions for the safety of the flying and motoring public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(5): 31A-22-1300 Before obtaining a permit or license under this section, the applicant shall file with the county executive and the department proof of public liability insurance coverage that meets the requirements described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-117(6): In addition to the insurance required under this section, either the county executive or the department may require the posting of a bond to indemnify the county or department against liability resulting from issuing the permit or license under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118 Reason for department order to be stated -- Closing airports -- Notice -- Right of inspection.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(1): If the department rejects an application for permission to operate or establish an airport, or issues any order under this chapter that requires or prohibits certain actions, its order shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(1)(a): contain the reasons for the rejection or order; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(1)(b): state the requirements to be met before approval will be given or the order changed.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(2): The department may order the closing of any airport until its requirements have been fulfilled.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(3)(a): An airport not meeting the standards required by the department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(3)(a)(i): be given notice of its noncompliance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(3)(a)(ii): have 10 days from the receipt of that notice to respond to the department with a plan and schedule for compliance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(3)(b): If the airport fails to respond within the required time, the department may revoke the airport license and close the airport.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-118(4): The department and any state, county, or municipal officer charged with the duty of enforcing this chapter may inspect and examine at reasonable hours any premises, buildings, or other structures where regulated airports are operated.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-119 Judicial review.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-119(1): Any person against whom an order has been entered may obtain judicial review.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-119(2): Venue for judicial review of informal adjudicative proceedings is in the district court of the county in which the order was made or the county in which property affected by the order is located.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-120 Violations -- Penalty.
------------------------------------------------------
A person who fails to comply with the requirements of or violates any provision of this part is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-121 Severability clause.
----------------------------------------------------
If any provision of this part or its application to any person or circumstances is held invalid, this invalidity may not affect other provisions or applications of the part which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application and to this end the provisions of this part are declared to be severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-122 Construction of chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
This chapter shall be so interpreted and construed as to effectuate its general purpose to make uniform the law of those states which enact it.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-123 Sovereignty in space above land and water in state.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Sovereignty in the space above the lands and waters of this state is declared to rest in the state, except where granted to and assumed by the United States pursuant to a constitutional grant from the people of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-124 Report of death or serious injury to person or property.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If in the operation of civil aircraft death or serious injury to person or to property results, a report shall be made in accordance with federal aviation regulations.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-125 Report of injury to aircraft or property.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
All accidents in the operation of civil aircraft which cause injury to aircraft or property shall be reported in accordance with federal aviation regulations.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-126 Marking buildings to aid navigation.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-126(1): The department may cooperate with the officials of all state institutions for the purpose of marking one building within their group as an aid to aerial navigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-126(2): The marking is subject to the approval of the department and shall comply with the requirements of the United States civil aeronautics authority for air marking.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-127 Tampering with aircraft forbidden.
------------------------------------------------------------------
It shall be unlawful for any person, without express or implied authority of the owner, to operate, climb upon, enter, manipulate the controls or accessories of, set in motion, remove parts or contents of, or otherwise tamper with any civil aircraft within this state, or knowingly cause or permit the same to be done.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-128 Tampering with airport or equipment forbidden.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person may not interfere or tamper with any airport, landing field, or airway, or the equipment thereof.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129 Expenditures for Civil Air Patrol.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129(1): The department may expend state aeronautics funds for the Utah wing of the Civil Air Patrol to be used to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129(1)(a): purchase aviation facilities, training, supplies, and equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129(1)(b): defray maintenance and rental costs of hangar facilities and aircraft;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129(1)(c): purchase maintenance supplies and equipment for the communications network of the Civil Air Patrol; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129(1)(d): provide administrative costs approved by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-129(2): The expenditures may not exceed in any fiscal year the amount appropriated to the Utah wing of the Civil Air Patrol by the Legislature.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-130 Approval of expenditures for Civil Air Patrol.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An expenditure of state funds for the civil air patrol may not be made unless a purchase order is first approved by the director of aeronautics under guidelines established by the department and unless the funds are specifically used as required in this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-131 Tax-exempt status of Civil Air Patrol equipment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Equipment, aircraft and vehicles owned by the civil air patrol and used for the emergency service needs of the state of Utah are given tax-exempt status.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133 Marking of meteorological evaluation towers.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(a): "Meteorological evaluation tower" means a permanent or temporary tower used for meteorological evaluation that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(a)(i): is supported by guy wires and ground anchors; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(a)(ii): has accessory facilities on which an antenna, sensor, camera, meteorological instrument, or other meteorological monitoring equipment is mounted.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(b): "Meteorological evaluation tower" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(b)(i): a tower registered with the Federal Communications Commission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(b)(ii): a tower that is primarily used to support telecommunications equipment, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(b)(ii)(A): a microwave relay facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(1)(b)(ii)(B): a tower erected for the purpose of providing commercial mobile radio service or commercial mobile data service, as those terms are defined in 47 C.F.R. Sec. 20.3.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(2): (3) Except as required by federal law, rule, or regulation, a meteorological evaluation tower shall be marked as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(2)(a): over 50 feet in height;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(2)(b): located outside of an incorporated city or town; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(2)(c): on land that is primarily rural, undeveloped, or used for agricultural purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3)(a): A meteorological evaluation tower shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3)(a)(i): be painted in equal alternating bands of aviation orange and white, beginning with orange at the top and bottom of the tower, to be visible in clear air during daylight hours from a distance of at least two thousand feet;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3)(a)(ii): have a high-visibility safety sleeve at least seven feet long on each guy wire, extending from the anchor point along each guy wire attached to the anchor point;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3)(a)(iii): have a spherical marker attached to the top third of each of the highest guy wires; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3)(a)(iv): have a flashing light at the top of the tower that, when flashing, is visible during nighttime from a distance of at least two thousand feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(3)(b): (3)(a) The owner of a meteorological evaluation tower shall replace the markings described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-133(4): The owner of a meteorological evaluation tower erected before May 5, 2021, shall meet the requirements of this section before May 5, 2022.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-201 Powers of department -- Acceptance of property.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The department, a county, or municipal legislative body may accept contributions of money or real or personal property for the purpose of establishing, developing, operating, or maintaining airports under this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202 Cooperation with counties, municipalities, and federal government -- Expenditures by department.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202(1): The department may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202(1)(a): cooperate with counties and municipalities in developing and constructing airports;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202(1)(b): make agreements on behalf of the state with any county or municipality regarding the financial participation, construction, and operation of any airports;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202(1)(c): cooperate with the federal government in establishing airports; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202(1)(d): accept from the United States of America, money to be matched with the funds of the state and funds appropriated by any county or municipality in developing and constructing airports under the Uniform Airports Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-202(2): The department may expend not to exceed 10% of its annual appropriation from the Aeronautics Restricted Account upon any one project under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203 Department and counties, municipalities, and airport authorities authorized to acquire and regulate airports.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203(1): The department and municipalities, counties, and airport authorities may acquire, establish, construct, expand, own, lease, control, equip, improve, maintain, operate, regulate, and police airports for the use of aircraft and may use for these purposes any available property that is owned or controlled by the department or by a municipality, county, or airport authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203(2): A county may not exercise the authority conferred in this section outside of its geographical limits except  jointly with an adjoining county.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5 Advisory boards of airports and extraterritorial airports.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(1): For purposes of this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(1)(a): "Airport owner" means the municipality, county, or airport authority that owns one or more airports.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(1)(b): "Extraterritorial airport" means an airport, including the airport facilities, real estate, or other assets related to the operation of an airport, outside the municipality or county and within the boundary of a different municipality or county.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(2)(a): If an airport owner that owns an international airport also owns one or more extraterritorial airports, the airport owner shall create and maintain an advisory board as described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(2)(b): The advisory board shall advise and consult the airport owner according to the process set forth in ordinance, rule, or regulation of the airport owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3): (2); (3)(a)(i)(A); (3)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3)(a): (2); (3)(a)(i)(A); (3)(a)(i) An advisory board described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3)(a)(i): (3)(a)(i)(A) one individual from each municipality or county in which an extraterritorial airport is located, appointed:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3)(a)(i)(A): according to an ordinance or policy in place in each municipality or county for appointing individuals to a board, if any; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3)(a)(i)(B): (3)(a)(i)(A) if no ordinance or policy described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3)(a)(ii): (3)(a)(i) as many individuals as necessary, appointed by the chief executive officer of the airport owner, with advice and consent from the legislative body of the airport owner, when added to the individuals appointed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-203.5(3)(b): The airport owner shall ensure that members of the advisory board have the following qualifications:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205 Acquisition of property -- Condemnation.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205(1): Private property needed by the department or a county, municipality, or airport authority for an airport or landing field or for the expansion of an airport or landing field may be acquired by grant, purchase, lease, or other means if the department or the political subdivision is able to agree with the owners of the property on the terms of acquisition.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205(2): If no agreement can be reached, the private property may be obtained by condemnation in the manner provided for the state or a political subdivision to acquire real property for public purposes.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205.5 Abandoned aircraft on airport property -- Seizure and disposal.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205.5(1)(a)(ii): is in a wrecked, inoperative, derelict, or partially dismantled condition; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205.5(1)(a)(iii): is not in the process of actively being repaired.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205.5(1)(b): "Abandoned aircraft" does not include an aircraft:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205.5(1)(b)(iii): for which evidence is shown indicating repairs are in process, including:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-205.5(1)(b)(iii)(B): a statement from a mechanic making the repairs.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-206 Payment by appropriation or sale of bonds.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
The purchase price or award for real property acquired, in accordance with the provisions of this part, for an airport or landing field may be paid for by appropriation of money available for the property or wholly or partly from the proceeds of the sale of bonds of the county, municipality, or other political subdivision, as the legislative body of the political subdivision shall determine, subject to the adoption of a proposition at a regular or special election, if the adoption of a proposition is a prerequisite to the issuance of bonds of the political subdivision for public purposes generally.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207 Powers of department and political subdivisions over airports -- Security unit.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1): The department, and counties, municipalities, or other political subdivisions of this state that have established or may establish airports or that acquire, lease, or set apart real property for those purposes, may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1)(a): construct, equip, improve, maintain, and operate the airports or may vest the authority for their construction, equipment, improvement, maintenance, and operation in an officer of the department or in an officer, board, or body of the political subdivision;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1)(b): adopt rules, establish charges, fees, and tolls for the use of airports and landing fields, fix penalties for the violation of the rules, and establish liens to enforce payment of the charges, fees, and tolls, subject to approval by the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1)(c): lease the airports to private parties for operation for a term not exceeding 50 years, as long as the public is not deprived of its rightful, equal, and uniform use of the facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1)(d): lease or assign space, area, improvements, equipment, buildings, and facilities on the airports to private parties for operation for a term not exceeding 50 years;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1)(e): lease or assign real property comprising all or any part of the airports to private parties for the construction and operation of hangars, shop buildings, or office buildings for a term not exceeding 50 years, if the projected construction cost of the hangar, shop building, or office building is $100,000 or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(1)(f): establish, maintain, operate, and staff a security unit for the purpose of enforcing state and local laws at any airport that is subject to federal airport security regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(2): (1) The department or political subdivision shall pay the construction, equipment, improvement, maintenance, and operations expenses of any airport established by them under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3): (1)(f); Title 53, Chapter 13, Peace Officer Classifications; (1)(f)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(a): (1)(f); Title 53, Chapter 13, Peace Officer Classifications If the department or political subdivision establishes a security unit under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(b): A security unit appointed by the department or political subdivision is exempt from civil service regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(c): (1)(f) If the department or political subdivision establishes a security unit under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(c)(i): may allow peace officers or other workers to assist with airport operations and vehicle and traffic flow; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(c)(ii): may not allow peace officers or other workers to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(c)(ii)(A): unreasonably impede or obstruct traffic;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(c)(ii)(B): create unsafe traffic situations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-207(3)(c)(ii)(C): intimidate vehicle drivers or airport passengers.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-208 Providing for levying of taxes.
---------------------------------------------------------------
The local public authorities having power to appropriate money within the counties, municipalities, or other public subdivisions of this state for the purpose of acquiring, establishing, developing, operating, maintaining, or controlling airports  under the provisions of this part, are authorized to appropriate and cause to be raised by taxation or otherwise in such political subdivisions money sufficient to carry out therein the provisions of this part, also to use for such purpose or purposes money derived from the airports.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-209 Acquisition of air rights -- Condemnation.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-209(1): To provide unobstructed air space for the landing and taking off of aircraft using airports acquired or maintained under this chapter, the department and a county, municipality, or airport authority may acquire the air rights over private property necessary to insure safe approaches to the landing areas of the airports.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-209(2): 72-10-205 The air rights may be acquired by grant, purchase, lease, or condemnation in the same manner provided under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-210 Easements for marks or lights -- Condemnation.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-210(1): The department and a county, municipality, or airport authority may acquire the right or easement for a term of years or perpetually to place and maintain suitable marks for the daytime, and to place, operate, and maintain suitable lights for the nighttime marking of buildings or other structures or obstructions for the safe operation of aircraft using airports and landing fields acquired or maintained under this chapter.
