Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-211 Police regulations.
---------------------------------------------------
The department and a county, municipality, or airport authority acquiring, establishing, developing, operating, maintaining, or controlling airports outside the geographical limits of the subdivisions, under this chapter may amend and enforce police regulations for the airports.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-212 General provisions of law applicable in condemnation proceedings, issuing bonds, and levying taxes.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
It is the intent and purpose of this part that all provisions herein relating to the issuance of bonds and the levying of taxes for airport purposes and the condemnation for airports and airport facilities shall be construed in accordance with general provisions of the law of this state governing the right and procedure of municipalities to condemn property, issue bonds, and levy taxes.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-213 Severability clause.
----------------------------------------------------
If any provision of this part or its application is held invalid, this invalidity does not affect provisions or applications of the part which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this part are declared to be severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-214 Construction of part.
-----------------------------------------------------
This part shall be so interpreted and construed as to effectuate the general purpose of those states which enact it.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-215 Restrictions on use of airport revenue to finance a fixed guideway.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An airport operator may not use airport revenue to contribute to the cost of constructing, equipping, maintaining, or operating any portion of a fixed guideway as defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301(1): "Airport" means any area of land or water which is used, or intended for use for the landing and taking-off of aircraft, and any appurtenant areas which are used, or intended for use, for aircraft buildings or other airport facilities or rights of way, together with all airport buildings and facilities located on them.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301(2): "Air navigation facility" means any facility -- other than one owned and operated by the United States -- used in, available for use in, or designed for use in aid of air navigation, including any structures, mechanisms, lights, beacons, markers, communicating systems, or other instrumentalities, or devices used or useful as an aid, or constituting an advantage or convenience, to the safe taking-off, navigation, and landing of aircraft, or the safe and efficient operation or maintenance of an airport, and any combination of any or all of the facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301(3): "Airport hazard" means any structure, object of natural growth, or use of land which obstructs the air space required for the flight of aircraft in landing or taking-off at an airport or is otherwise hazardous to the landing or taking-off of aircraft.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301(4): "Municipality" means any county, city, town, or political subdivision of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301(5): "Person" means any individual, firm, partnership, corporation, company, association, joint stock association, or body politic and includes any trustee, receiver, assignee, or other similar representation thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-301(6): "Public agency" means the United States government or any of its agencies, a state or its agencies, a municipality or other political subdivision, or a tax-supported organization.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-302 Purpose and policy of part.
-----------------------------------------------------------
It is declared that the purpose of this part is to further the public interest in aeronautical progress:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-302(1): by authorizing public agencies of this state to accept, channel, and disburse federal, state, and other funds for the planning, acquisition, construction, maintenance, operation, and regulation of airports and air navigation facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-302(2): by granting to a state agency the powers and imposing upon it the duties that the state may obtain the full benefit of financial assistance made available by the federal government, as well as assistance from other sources;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-302(3): by providing authority that may be exercised by a public agency independently or jointly with other public agencies, and enabling two or more cities, towns, counties, and other political subdivisions jointly to establish, acquire, develop, and operate an airport or airports for their joint or common use.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-303 Submission of requests for aid -- Approval by department -- Receipt and disbursement of funds.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-303(1): The state, a county, municipality, or airport authority may not submit to any federal agency or department of the United States any requests for aid under any act of congress that provides funds for airports or commercial airport construction, development, expansion, or improvements, unless the project and the requests for aid have been first approved by the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-303(2): The state, a county, municipality, or airport authority may not directly accept, receive, receipt for, or disburse any funds granted by the United States under the act, but it shall designate the department as its agent and in its behalf to accept, receive, receipt for, and disburse the funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-303(3): The state, a county, municipality, or airport authority shall enter into an agreement with the department, prescribing the terms and conditions of the agency in accordance with federal laws, rules, and regulations and applicable laws of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-303(4): Money paid by the United States government shall be retained by the state or paid to a county, municipality, or airport authority under terms and conditions imposed by the United States government in making the grant.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304 Powers and duties of department.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(1): The department may make available its engineering and other technical services, with or without charge, to the state, a county, municipality, or airport authority or person desiring them in connection with the planning, acquisition, construction, improvement, maintenance, or operation of airports or air navigation facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(2)(a): The department may render financial assistance by grant, loan, or both, to any county, municipality, or airport authority, in the planning, acquisition, construction, improvement, maintenance, or operation of an airport owned or controlled, or to be owned or controlled by the county, municipality, or airport authority, out of appropriations made by the Legislature for these purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(2)(b): Financial assistance may be furnished in connection with federal or other financial aid for the same purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(3)(a): The department may use the facilities and services of other state agencies and of the counties and municipalities to the utmost extent possible.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(3)(b): The state agencies, counties, and municipalities shall make available their facilities and services.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-304(4): All powers granted to any county, municipality, or airport authority by this  chapter may be exercised jointly with any county, municipality, or airport authority, and jointly with any state agency or the United States if the laws of the other state or of the United States permit  the joint exercise.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-305 Mutual assistance -- Gifts, leases, and loans.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-305(1): If any public agency determines that the public interest and the interest of the public agency will be served by assisting any other public agency in exercising the powers and authority granted by this part, the public agency may furnish assistance by gift of real or personal property or money or lease or loan with or without charge or interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-305(2): In appropriating the property or money and providing for the assistance by taxation, the issuance of bonds, or other means, the public agency may exercise all of its powers as though used for its own direct purposes as provided in this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-306 Contractual powers of public agencies.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
A public agency may enter into any contracts necessary to the execution of the powers granted it, and for the purposes provided by this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-307 Powers of governing bodies.
-----------------------------------------------------------
The governing body of any public agency having power to appropriate and raise money is authorized to appropriate, and to raise by taxation or otherwise, sufficient money to carry out the provisions and purposes of this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-308 Construction of part.
-----------------------------------------------------
This part shall be so interpreted and construed as to make uniform so far as possible the laws and regulations of this state and other states and of the government of the United States having to do with the subject of public airports.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-309 Severability clause.
----------------------------------------------------
If any provision of this part or its application to any person or circumstance shall be held invalid, this invalidity does not affect the provisions or applications of this part which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this part are declared to be severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(1): "Airport" means any publicly used area of land or water that is used, or intended to be used, for the landing and take-off of aircraft and utilized or to be utilized in the interest of the public for these purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(2): "Airport hazard" means any structure, tree, object of natural growth, or use of land that potentially obstructs or otherwise impacts the safe and efficient utilization of the navigable airspace required for the flight of aircraft in landing or take-off at an airport.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(3): "Airport influence area" means land located within 5,000 feet of an airport runway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(4): "Airport overlay zone" means a secondary zoning district designed to protect the public health, safety, and welfare near an airport that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(4)(a): applies land use regulation in addition to the primary zoning district land use regulation of property used as an airport and property within an airport influence area;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(4)(b): may extend beyond the airport influence area;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(4)(c): ensures airport utility as a public asset;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(4)(d): protects property owner land values near an airport through compatible land use regulations as recommended by the Federal Aviation Administration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(4)(e): protects aircraft occupant safety through protection of navigable airspace.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(5): "Avigation easement" means an easement permitting unimpeded aircraft flights over property subject to the easement and includes the right:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(5)(a): to create or increase noise or other effects that may result from the lawful operation of aircraft; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(5)(b): to prohibit or remove any obstruction to such overflight.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(6): 10-9a-103; 17-27a-103 "Land use regulation" means the same as that term is defined in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(7): "Political subdivision" means any municipality, city, town, or county.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(8): "Structure" means any object constructed or installed by man, including buildings, towers, smokestacks, and overhead transmission lines.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-401(9): "Tree" means any object of natural growth.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402 Declaration with respect to airport hazards.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Legislature finds that:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(1): an airport hazard endangers the lives and property of users of the airport and of occupants of land in its vicinity;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(2): an obstruction of the type that reduces the size of the area available for the landing, taking-off, and maneuvering of aircraft tends to destroy or impair the utility of the airport and the public investment in the airport;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(3): the creation or establishment of an airport hazard is a public nuisance and an injury to the community served by the airport in question;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(4): it is necessary in the interest of the public health, public safety, and general welfare that the creation or establishment of airport hazards be prevented;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(5): this should be accomplished, to the extent legally possible, by exercise of the police power, without compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(6): both the prevention of the creation or establishment of airport hazards and the elimination, removal, alteration, mitigation, or marking and lighting of existing airport hazards are public purposes for which political subdivisions may raise and expend public funds and acquire land or property interests in land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-402(7): the establishment of an airport overlay zone best prevents the creation or establishment of an airport hazard, and promotes the public health, safety, and general welfare.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403 Airport zoning regulations.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(1): Title 10, Chapter 9a, Municipal Land Use, Development, and Management Act; Title 17, Chapter 27a, County Land Use, Development, and Management Act In order to prevent the creation or establishment of airport hazards, each political subdivision located within an airport influence area, shall adopt, administer, and enforce land use regulations for the airport influence area, including an airport overlay zone, under the police power and in the manner and upon the conditions prescribed:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(1)(a): in this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(1)(b): Title 10, Chapter 9a, Municipal Land Use, Development, and Management Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(1)(c): Title 17, Chapter 27a, County Land Use, Development, and Management Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2)(a): Each political subdivision located within an airport influence area shall notify a person building on or developing land in an airport influence area, in writing, of aircraft overflights and associated noise.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2)(b): To promote the safe and efficient operation of the airport, a political subdivision located within an airport influence area:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2)(b)(i): shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2)(b)(i)(A): adopt an airport overlay zone conforming to the requirements of this chapter and 14 C.F.R.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2)(b)(i)(B): require any proposed development within an airport influence area to conform with 14 C.F.R.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(2)(b)(ii): may, as a condition to granting a building permit, subdivision plat, or a requested zoning change within an airport influence area, require a person building or developing land to grant or sell to the airport owner, at appraised fair market value, an avigation easement.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(3): If a political subdivision located within an airport influence area fails to adopt an airport overlay zone by December 31, 2024, then the following requirements shall apply in an airport influence area:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(3)(a): each political subdivision located within an airport influence area shall notify a person building on or developing land within an airport influence area, in writing, of aircraft overflights and associated noise;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(3)(b): as a condition to granting a building permit, subdivision plat, or a requested zoning change within an airport influence area, require the person building or developing land to grant or sell to the airport owner, at appraised fair market value, an avigation easement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-403(3)(c): require a person building or developing land within an airport influence area conform to the requirements of this chapter and 14 C.F.R.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-404 Zoning ordinances -- Governing law in event of conflict.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
In the event of conflict between any airport land use regulations adopted under this part and any other regulations applicable to the same area, whether the conflict be with respect to the height of structures or trees, the use of land, or any other matter, the airport overlay zone requirement shall govern and prevail.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-413 Purchase or condemnation of air rights or navigation easements.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A political subdivision owning the airport, whether or not the airport is located within the territorial limits of the political subdivision, or a political subdivision that is served by the airport may acquire, by purchase, grant, or condemnation in the manner provided by the law under which political subdivisions are authorized to acquire real property for public purposes, an air right, an avigation easement, or other estate or interest in the property or nonconforming structure or use in question if:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-413(1): it is desired to remove, lower, or otherwise terminate a nonconforming structure or use;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-413(2): the approach protection necessary cannot, because of constitutional limitations, be provided by airport land use regulations under this part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-413(3): it appears advisable that the necessary approach protection be provided by acquisition of property rights rather than by airport zoning regulations.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-415 Severability clause.
----------------------------------------------------
If any provision of this part or its application to any person or circumstances is held invalid, this invalidity does not affect the provisions or applications of the part which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this part are declared to be severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501 Flying under the influence of alcohol, drugs, or with specified or unsafe blood alcohol concentration -- Calculations of blood or breath alcohol -- Criminal punishment -- Arrest without warrant.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(1)(a): A person may not operate or be in actual physical control of an aircraft within this state if the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(1)(a)(i): has sufficient alcohol in his body that a subsequent chemical test shows that the person has a blood or breath alcohol concentration of .04 grams or greater at the time of the test;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(1)(a)(ii): is under the influence of alcohol, any drug, or the combined influence of alcohol and any drug to a degree that renders the person incapable of safely operating an aircraft; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(1)(a)(iii): has a blood or breath alcohol concentration of .04 grams or greater at the time of operation or actual physical control.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(1)(b): The fact that a person charged with violating this section is or has been legally entitled to use alcohol or a drug is not a defense against any charge of violating this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(2): 41-6a-502(1) Calculations of blood or breath alcohol concentration under this section shall be made in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(3): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(3)(a): (1) A person convicted of a violation of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(3)(a)(i): class B misdemeanor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(3)(a)(ii): class A misdemeanor if the person has also inflicted bodily injury upon another as a proximate result of having operated the aircraft in a negligent manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(3)(b): In this section, the standard of negligence is that of simple negligence, the failure to exercise that degree of care that an ordinarily reasonable and prudent person exercises under like or similar circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(4): A peace officer may, without a warrant, arrest a person for a violation of this section when the officer has probable cause to believe:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(4)(a): the violation has occurred, although not in the officer's presence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-501(4)(b): the violation was committed by that person.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(1): 10-2-301 "City" means a municipality of the first class, as defined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(1)(a): is authorized by statute to operate an airport; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(1)(b): operates an airport with greater than 10 million annual passengers.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(2): 53-10-103 "Division" means the Criminal Investigation and Technical Services Division of the Department of Public Safety, established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(3): "Ground transportation service" means transporting passengers for hire or as a courtesy in connection with a business over public streets pursuant to a license with the city.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4): 17B-2a-802
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(a): "Ground transportation service provider" means a driver who provides ground transportation service where the pickup or drop-off of a passenger occurs at an airport under a city's authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b): 17B-2a-802 "Ground transportation service provider" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b)(i): a taxicab driver;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b)(ii): a limousine or luxury car driver;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b)(iii): 17B-2a-802 a bus or minibus driver, except a driver of a transit vehicle, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b)(iv): a courtesy vehicle or hotel vehicle driver;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b)(v): a special transportation vehicle driver who transports persons with a disability; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-601(4)(b)(vi): a van driver.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-604 Written notice to ground transportation service provider whose access to airport is denied or terminated -- Right to respond and seek review.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-604(1): If a city denies or terminates the right of a ground transportation service provider to provide ground transportation service to an airport because of information obtained through a criminal background check under this part, the city shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-604(1)(a): notify the ground transportation service provider in writing of the reasons for the denial or termination; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-604(1)(b): give the ground transportation service provider an opportunity to respond to the reasons and to seek review of the denial or termination through administrative procedures established by the city.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-604(2): If a ground transportation service provider is denied access to provide ground transportation service to an airport, the denial shall not impact the right of another ground transportation service provider who provides ground transportation service for the same business.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701 Preemption of local ordinance -- Business licensing.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(1): As used in this section, "advanced air mobility business" means a business that operates an unmanned aircraft system or an advanced air mobility system for a commercial purpose that is required to obtain a certificate pursuant to 14 C.F.R.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(2): A political subdivision of the state, or an entity within a political subdivision of the state, may not enact a law, ordinance, or rule governing the private use of an unmanned aircraft or the private use of an advanced air mobility system, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(2)(a): authorized by this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(2)(b): the political subdivision or entity is an airport operator that enacts the law, rule, or ordinance to govern:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(2)(b)(i): the operation of an unmanned aircraft or an advanced air mobility system within the geographic boundaries of the airport over which the airport operator has authority; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(2)(b)(ii): the takeoff or landing of an unmanned aircraft or an aircraft operated as part of an advanced air mobility system at the airport over which the airport operator has authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(3)(a): Subject to the provisions of this chapter, a political subdivision may require an advanced air mobility business to obtain a business license if the advanced air mobility business does not hold a current business license in good standing from another political subdivision in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(3)(b): A political subdivision may only charge a licensing fee to an advanced air mobility business in an amount that reimburses the political subdivision for the actual cost of processing the business license.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(4): (3)(a); (3) A political subdivision may not require an advanced air mobility business to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(4)(a): (3)(a) obtain a separate business license beyond the initial business license described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(4)(b): (3) pay a fee other than the fee for the initial business license described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(4)(c): pay a fee for each employee the advanced air mobility business employs.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(5): A political subdivision shall provide a reasonable accommodation to an advanced air mobility business with regard to any regulation or restriction on the size of the business.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(6): A political subdivision shall recognize as valid within the political subdivision the business license of an advanced air mobility business obtained in another political subdivision within the state, if the business license is current and in good standing.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(7): (7)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(7)(a): A political subdivision may not create a monopoly by entering into an agreement to grant or permit an exclusive right to one or more vertiport owners as the only vertiport owners or operators within the boundary of the political subdivision.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(7)(b): (7)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(8): (7) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-701(9): This chapter supersedes any law, ordinance, or rule enacted by a political subdivision of the state before July 1, 2022.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-702 Applicability.
----------------------------------------------
This chapter does not apply to a person or business entity:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-702(1): using an unmanned aircraft for legitimate educational or business purposes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-702(2): operating the unmanned aircraft system in a manner consistent with applicable Federal Aviation Administration rules, exemptions, or other authorizations.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part, "weapon" means:Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(1): 76-10-501 a firearm as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2): an object that in the manner of the object's use or intended use is capable of causing death, bodily injury, or damage to property, as determined according to the following factors:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2)(a): the location and circumstances in which the object is used or possessed;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2)(b): the primary purpose for which the object is made;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2)(c): the character of the damage, if any, the object is likely to cause;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2)(d): the manner in which the object is used;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2)(e): whether the manner in which the object is used or possessed constitutes a potential imminent threat to public safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-901(2)(f): the lawful purposes for which the object may be used.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002 Safe operation of unmanned aircraft.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(1): An individual who operates an unmanned aircraft system to fly an unmanned aircraft for recreational purposes shall comply with this section or 14 C.F.R. Sec. 101, Subpart E.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2): (2)(a)(i) An individual operating an unmanned aircraft shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(a): maintain visual line of sight of the unmanned aircraft in order to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(a)(i): know the location of the unmanned aircraft;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(a)(ii): determine the attitude, altitude, and direction of flight;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(a)(iii): observe the airspace for other air traffic or hazards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(a)(iv): determine that the unmanned aircraft does not endanger the life or property of another person;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(b): (2)(a)(i) ensure that the ability described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(b)(i): the operator of the unmanned aircraft; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(2)(b)(ii): a visual observer.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(3): An individual may not operate an unmanned aircraft in Class B, Class C, or Class D airspace or within the lateral boundaries of the surface area of Class E airspace designated for an airport unless the operator of the unmanned aircraft has prior authorization from air traffic control.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(4): An individual may not operate an unmanned aircraft in a manner that interferes with operations and traffic patterns at any airport, heliport, or seaplane base.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(5): An individual may not operate an unmanned aircraft system:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(5)(a): from a public transit rail platform or station; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(5)(b)(i): under a height of 50 feet within a public transit fixed guideway right-of-way; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(5)(b)(ii): directly above any overhead electric lines used to power a public transit rail vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(6): An individual may not operate an unmanned aircraft in violation of a notice to airmen described in 14 C.F.R. Sec. 107.47.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(7): An individual may not operate an unmanned aircraft at an altitude that is higher than 400 feet above ground level unless the unmanned aircraft:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(7)(a): is flown within a 400-foot radius of a structure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(7)(b): does not fly higher than 400 feet above the structure's immediate uppermost limit.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(8): (8)(d)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(8)(a): An individual who violates this section is liable for any damages that may result from the violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(8)(b): A law enforcement officer shall issue a written warning to an individual who violates this section who has not previously received a written warning for a violation of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(8)(c): (8)(d) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-10-1002(8)(d): An individual who violates this section is guilty of a class B misdemeanor for each conviction of a violation of this section after the individual is convicted of an infraction or a misdemeanor for a previous violation of this section.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 11 - Passenger Ropeway Systems Act
***************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the " Passenger Ropeway Systems Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(1): "Aerial lift" means a ropeway on which passengers are transported in cabins or on chairs.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(2): "Aerial tramway" means a ropeway on which passengers are transported in cable supported carriers and are not in contact with the ground or snow surface and that reciprocates between terminals.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(3): "Area" means the geographic area, terrain, and ski slopes served by a passenger ropeway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(4): 72-11-202 "Committee" means the Passenger Ropeway Safety Committee created by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(5): "Conveyor" means a device used to transport skiers and snowboarders standing on a flexible moving element or belt.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(6): "Detachable grip lift" means a monocable or bicable ropeway system on which carriers circulate around the system alternately attaching to and detaching from a moving haul rope.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(7): "Funicular" means a ropeway on which carriers are supported and guided by a guideway and that is propelled by means of a haul rope system and that is operated as a single or double reversible system.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(8): "Industry" means the passenger ropeway business activities of any person in the state who owns, manages, or directs the operation of a passenger ropeway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(9): "Operator" means a person, including any political subdivision or instrumentality of the political subdivision, who owns, manages, or directs the operation of a passenger ropeway.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(a): "Passenger ropeway"  means a device, excluding an elevator, used to transport passengers along a level, inclined or declined path by means of a haul rope or other flexible elements that is driven by a power unit that remains essentially at a single location.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b): Passenger ropeways include the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b)(i): an aerial tramway;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b)(ii): an aerial lift, including a detachable grip lift and chair lift;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b)(iii): a conveyor;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b)(iv): a funicular;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b)(v): a surface lift, including a J-bar, T-bar, or platter pull; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(10)(b)(vi): a  rope tow, including a wire rope and fiber rope tow.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11): (11)(d)(i) "Private residence passenger ropeway" means a passenger ropeway that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(a): is installed at a private residence;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(b): is not accessible to the general public;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(c): is not used for commercial purposes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(d): (11)(d)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(d)(i): is owned by one single owner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(d)(ii): (11)(d)(i) the owner described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(d)(ii)(A): a unit or homeowner's association; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(11)(d)(ii)(B): a planned unit development or a planned residential unit development organization or entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(12): "Rope tow" means a ropeway on which passengers remain in contact with the ground or snow surface and are pulled in one direction only by a towing device attached to a circulating wire rope.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-102(13): "Surface lift" means a ropeway on which passengers remain in contact with the ground or snow surface and are pulled by a towing device attached to a circulating overhead wire rope, and includes a J-bar, T-bar, or platter pull.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-103 Authority of Passenger Ropeway Safety Committee -- Location of system.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-103(1): The committee is authorized to acquire, construct, reconstruct, improve or extend, maintain and operate, either directly or through others by contract, lease, concession or otherwise, a passenger ropeway system for the transportation of persons and property between a point or points in the:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-103(1)(a): Wasatch Mountain State Park; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-103(1)(b): Uintah and Wasatch National Forests in the upper parts of Big Cottonwood, Little Cottonwood and American Fork Canyons in Salt Lake, Utah and Wasatch Counties.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-103(2): The committee may acquire by purchase, contract, lease, permit, donation or otherwise, and to construct, maintain and operate, either directly or through others, by contract, lease, concession or otherwise, all property, rights of way, approach roads, parking and other areas, structures, facilities and services for the convenience and recreation of patrons of the transportation system and visitors to the Wasatch Mountain State Park.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-103(3): Any contract, lease, concession, or other arrangement may be entered into in a manner and upon the terms and conditions as the committee may consider advisable.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-104 Laws applicable to construction contracts and contractor's bonds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-104(1): Construction contracts entered into by the committee under the authority of this chapter shall be governed solely by this chapter, except that they are subject to the approval of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-104(2): Title 14, Chapter 1, Public Contracts The provisions of


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-105 Authority of committee to accept grants and assistance.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-105(1): The committee is authorized to co-operate and contract with and accept grants or other assistance from any other agency of the state of Utah and from any department, bureau, agency, instrumentality, office or officer of the United States and from the trustees or administrators of any fund established in the interest of conservation or recreation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-105(2): The grants or other assistance may be used for the acquisition, construction, maintenance, development, and operation of any of the areas, facilities, activities, or services at any time under, or intended to be brought under, the jurisdiction or control of the committee, expressly including those contemplated by the provisions of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-106 Revenue bonds authorized.
---------------------------------------------------------
To raise funds for the acquisition, financing, construction, reconstruction, improvement, or extension of any of those purposes, projects, and facilities, the committee is authorized to issue revenue bonds in amounts bearing a rate or rates of interest not exceeding 9% per annum, with maturities, in a form and on terms and conditions as it, with the approval of the director of the Division of Finance, considers necessary or convenient.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-107 Payment of interest and principal of revenue bonds -- Agreements authorized.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The committee may provide by resolution at a duly called regular or special meeting for the payment of the interest and principal of any and all revenue bonds as may be issued from time to time, and for that purpose may enter into agreements with other parties and may execute documents in a form and substance and on terms and conditions as it, with the approval of the director of the Division of Finance, may from time to time determine.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-108 Revenue bonds not debt or obligation of state or committee.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-108(1): In any and all revenue bonds issued hereunder and in the resolution or resolutions authorizing them, and in the agreements or documents entered into and executed in connection therewith, neither the payment of the principal or interest of any bond nor the obligation of any resolution, agreement, or document shall constitute a debt, liability, or obligation of the state or the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-108(2): Payments are to be paid solely from the revenues received from the operation of the proposed passenger ropeway transportation system, visitor care and accommodations, and all services in connection with the Wasatch Mountain State Park, as in the proceedings authorizing the issuance of the bonds, shall be pledged to the payment thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-108(3): All bonds issued under this chapter by the committee shall contain a recital on their face that neither the payment of the principal or any part thereof, nor any interest thereon, constitute a debt, liability, or obligation of the state or the committee.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-109 Revenues from operation to be pledged to payment of bonds and used for costs of operation and maintenance.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-109(1): Any resolution or trust indenture authorizing the issuance of the revenue bonds shall provide that all toll rates and charges and fees imposed for the use of all transportation, visitor care and accommodations, recreational and other facilities and all services, the revenues of which are pledged to the payment of revenue bonds authorized hereunder, shall be at all times fixed in the amounts as will yield sufficient revenues to pay principal of and interest on the bonds, to maintain the necessary reserves in connection therewith and to pay the annual cost of operation and maintenance of any of the facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-109(2): The committee may in the resolution or trust indenture pledge to the payment of the principal of and interest on the revenue bonds all or part of the revenues arising from the operation of all transportation, visitor care and accommodations, recreational and other facilities, and all services operated by the commission in connection with the Wasatch Mountain State Park, whether or not acquired with the proceeds of the revenue bonds, after there shall have been paid from the revenues the annual costs of operation and maintenance of all the facilities, including necessary costs of insurance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-109(3): The committee may also in the resolution or trust indenture reserve the right to issue bonds on a parity with the bonds authorized by the resolution or indenture under the terms and conditions as may be provided therein.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-109(4): After and subject to the payment of annual operating and maintenance expenses and insurance costs, the bond redemption and interest payments, including reserves therefor, shall constitute a first lien on all the rates, tolls and charges, and other revenues received from the use and operation of the project or projects for the acquisition and construction of which the revenue bonds were issued, and of any other revenue received from the operation of facilities in connection with the Wasatch Mountain State Park that may be pledged by the committee as security for the payment of the revenue bonds and interest for this project or projects.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-110 Bonds -- Negotiability -- Tax exemption except corporate franchise tax.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
All bonds issued under the provisions of this chapter are negotiable instruments except when registered in the name of a registered owner and all the bonds, and the interest or income therefrom, are exempt from all taxation in the state, except for the corporate franchise tax.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-111 Sale of bonds.
----------------------------------------------
The committee, with the approval of the director of the Division of Finance, may fix the terms and conditions for the sale or other disposition of any authorized issuance of bonds under this chapter and may sell any of the bonds at less than the par or face value, but no bond may be sold at a price below the par or face value of the bond which would result in a sale price yielding to the purchaser an average of more than 9% per annum, payable semiannually according to standard tables of bond values.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-112 Powers and authority of committee.
------------------------------------------------------------------
The committee, its officers, employees, and agents are authorized to carry out the necessary procedures to implement the acquisition and development of a passenger ropeway system together with the property, appliances, facilities, rights of way and easements necessary or useful in connection with it and to do anything not inconsistent with law which they consider necessary or convenient to carry out the provisions of this chapter, whether or not the authority is expressly granted in this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-113 Refunding of bonds authorized.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to the approval of the director of the Division of Finance, the committee is authorized to refund any revenue bonds that may become due or that may be called with the consent of the holder or holders whenever refunding may be considered necessary or desirable.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201 Passenger ropeways -- Purpose and scope.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(1): 72-11-210 In order to safeguard the life, health, property, and welfare of citizens while using passenger ropeways, it is the policy of the state to:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(1)(a): protect citizens and visitors from unnecessary mechanical hazards in the design, construction, and operation of passenger ropeways, but not from the hazards inherent in the sports of mountaineering, skiing, snowboarding, mountain biking, and hiking, or from the hazards of the area served by passenger ropeways, all of which hazards are assumed by the  sportsman; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(1)(b): 72-11-210 require periodic inspections of passenger ropeways to ensure that each passenger ropeway meets "The United States of America Standard Institute Safety Code for Aerial Passenger Tramways," or an equivalent standard established by rule under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(2): (2)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(2)(a): (2)(b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(2)(a)(i): register all passenger ropeways in the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(2)(a)(ii): establish reasonable standards of design, construction, and operational practices; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(2)(a)(iii): make inspections as necessary to implement this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-201(2)(b): The committee has no jurisdiction over the construction, modification, registration, or inspection of a private residence passenger ropeway.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202 Passenger ropeways -- Creation of Passenger Ropeway Safety Committee within Department of Transportation -- Members.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(1): There is created within the Department of Transportation a Passenger Ropeway Safety Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(2): The committee is comprised of six appointive members and one ex officio member who shall be appointed by the executive director of the Department of Transportation.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(3): The appointive members shall be appointed by the governor from persons representing the following interests:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(3)(a): two members to represent the industry;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(3)(b): two members to represent the public at large;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(3)(c): one member who is a licensed engineer in Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(3)(d): one member to represent the United States Forest Service.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(4): (4)(b); (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(4)(a): (4)(b) Except as required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(4)(b): (4)(a) Notwithstanding the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(4)(c): The governor may not consider or seek to discover the political affiliation of a person when considering the person for appointment or reappointment to the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(5): The governor, in making the appointments, shall request and consider recommendations made to him by:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(5)(a): the membership of the particular interest from which the appointments are to be made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-202(5)(b): the Department of Transportation.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------
The committee shall comply with the procedures and requirements of

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-204 Vacancies -- Expenses -- Reimbursement -- Use of facilities of Department of Transportation -- Functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-204(1): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-204(2): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-204(3): Reimbursement shall be made from fees collected by the committee for services rendered by the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-204(4): The Department of Transportation shall supply the committee with office accommodation, space, equipment, and secretarial assistance the executive director considers adequate for the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-204(5): In addition to the functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities granted to the committee under this chapter, the committee shall assume and have all of the functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities of the Division of Outdoor Recreation in relation to passenger ropeway systems pursuant to that chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205 Passenger ropeways -- Registration of ropeways.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205(1): (2); (4) Except as provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205(2): The initial application for registration of a passenger ropeway permits the operator to operate the passenger ropeway until final action on the application is taken by the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205(3): If an operator files an application to renew registration of a passenger ropeway, then the operator may continue the operation of the passenger ropeway under the existing registration until the committee takes final action on the pending application and has:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205(3)(a): issued a certificate to the operator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205(3)(b): given written notice to the operator that the passenger ropeway has not qualified for certification.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-205(4): A private residence passenger ropeway may be operated in this state without fulfilling the registration requirements of this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210 Passenger ropeways -- Additional powers and duties of committee.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The committee may:Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (1)(a)(i) in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(1)(a): (1)(a)(i) public safety in the design, construction, and operation of passenger ropeways that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(1)(a)(i): adopt the American National Standard for Passenger Ropeways;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(1)(a)(ii): (1)(a)(i) modify the standard under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(1)(a)(iii): establish an equivalent standard; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(1)(b): the annual registration date;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(2): hold hearings and take evidence in all matters relating to the exercise and performance of the powers and duties vested in the committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(3): subpoena witnesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(4): administer oaths;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(7): cause the prosecution and enjoinder of all persons violating the provisions of this chapter and incur the necessary expenses;

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-210(9): employ, within the funds available, and prescribe the duties of a secretary and other personnel as the  committee considers necessary.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-211 Passenger ropeways -- Inspection.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-211(1): The committee may order inspections of the design, construction, operation, and maintenance of passenger ropeways as the committee may reasonably require.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-211(2): If, as the result of an inspection, it is found that a violation of the committee's rules exists, or a condition in passenger ropeway construction, operation, or maintenance exists that endangers the safety of the public, an immediate report shall be made to the operator whose passenger ropeway has received the inspection and to the committee for appropriate investigation and order.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-211(3): A private residence passenger ropeway is not subject to the inspection requirements under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-212 Passenger ropeways -- Violations -- Order of committee.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-212(1): If, after investigation, the committee finds that a violation of this chapter or any of its rules exists, or that there is a condition in passenger ropeway construction, operation, or maintenance that endangers the safety of the public, it shall immediately issue its written order setting forth its findings, the corrective action to be taken, and setting a reasonable time for compliance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-212(2): The order shall be served upon the operator involved in the violation personally or by registered mail at the committee's election.  Return shall be made as provided in the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-213 Passenger ropeways -- Failure to comply with order -- Suspension -- Injunction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-213(1): If any operator fails to comply with a legal order or rule of the committee, the committee may:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-213(1)(a): suspend the registration of the affected passenger ropeway until the operator complies; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-213(1)(b): bring injunctive proceedings in the district court of the judicial district in which the affected passenger ropeway is located to compel compliance.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-213(2): In these proceedings the committee is not required to post bond.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-214 Passenger ropeways -- Not common carriers or public utilities -- Cooperative agreement with United States Forest Service.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-214(1): Passenger ropeways are not common carriers or public utilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-214(2): To avoid duplicate effort by authorities having jurisdiction over passenger ropeways on National Forest System land in the state, the committee may enter into a cooperative agreement with the United States Forest Service to establish reasonable standards for design, construction, maintenance, operational practices, and inspection.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-214(3): Upon application for registration of a passenger tramway, the operator shall pay to the committee a reasonable inspector's fee, plus a surcharge, that would have been charged had the inspection been made by the committee and its inspectors.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-215 Passenger ropeways -- Use in dangerous manner unlawful.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person who rides or uses a passenger ropeway may not do so in a manner that may endanger the life and safety of another person or cause damage to passenger ropeway equipment.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-11-216 Passenger ropeways -- Violation of act a misdemeanor.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person who violates Section

Utah Code Annotated - Title 72 - Chapter 12 - Travel Reduction Act
******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Travel Reduction Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102 Legislative findings and policy.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102(1): The Legislature finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102(1)(a): increasingly heavy commuting burdens on Utah's freeways and major transportation arteries are gradually aggravating driving conditions for all Utah motorists;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102(1)(b): single-occupant driving is the predominant mode of transportation used by commuters in Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102(1)(c): single-occupant driving represents the most costly and most excessive use of dwindling petroleum reserves; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102(1)(d): rapidly increasing energy costs represent an ever-growing burden on commuters' work-related expenses.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-102(2): The policy of this state is to support and encourage transportation modes and ride-sharing programs that reduce the number of vehicle miles traveled, thereby reducing gasoline consumption and protecting the environment.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(1): "Car-pool" means a mode of transportation in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(1)(a): six or fewer persons, including the driver, ride together in a motor vehicle;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(1)(b): that transportation is incidental to another purpose of the driver; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(1)(c): the vehicle manufacturer's design capacity of any one seat is not exceeded.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2): "Van-pool" means a nonprofit mode of prearranged commuter transportation of a relatively fixed group of seven to 15 persons, including the driver, between home and work, or termini near home and work, in a vehicle the group occupancy of which does not exceed the vehicle manufacturer's design capacity and that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(a): is owned or leased and operated by an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(a)(i): who owns only one van-pool vehicle;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(a)(ii): whose provision of transportation is incidental to another purpose of the operator;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(a)(iii): who does not  transport people as a business; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(a)(iv): who accepts money from riders in the  vehicle, if at all, only to recover some or all expenses directly related to the transportation, including fuel, maintenance, insurance, and depreciation;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(b): is owned or leased by a nonprofit employee organization and used to transport employees between home and work, or termini near home and work to provide incentives to employees to make the commute by a mode other than single occupant motor vehicle, the operating, administration, and reasonable depreciation costs of which are paid, if at all, by the persons using the vehicles; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(2)(c): is owned or leased by an employer, a public agency, or a public transit district, either alone or in cooperation with others to provide incentives to employees to make the  commute by a mode other than single occupant motor vehicle, the driver and passengers of which are employees and fees charged, if at all, for which are nonprofit and only to recover operating, maintenance, administration, and reasonable depreciation costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-103(3): "Ride-sharing arrangement" means either a car-pool, van-pool, or both.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-104 Ride-sharing arrangements -- Exemption from specified laws and rules.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The following laws and rules do not apply to ride-sharing arrangements:Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-104(1): laws and rules containing insurance requirements that are specifically applicable to motor carriers or commercial vehicles;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-104(2): laws imposing a higher standard of care on drivers or owners of motor carriers or commercial vehicles than that imposed on drivers or owners of other motor vehicles;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-104(3): laws and rules with equipment requirements and special accident reporting requirements that are specifically applicable to motor carriers or commercial vehicles; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-104(4): laws imposing a tax on fuel purchased in other states by motor carriers or road user taxes on commercial buses.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-105 Worker compensation inapplicable to injuries in ride-sharing.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Section

Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-106 Employer's liability for ride-sharing injuries.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-106(1): An employer is not liable for injuries to passengers or other persons or both resulting from the operation or use of a motor vehicle not owned, leased, or contracted for by the employer in a ride-sharing arrangement.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-106(2): An employer is not liable for injuries to passengers or other persons or both on account of the employer having provided information or incentives or otherwise having encouraged employees to participate in ride-sharing arrangements.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-107 Benefits of ride-sharing driver not taxable income.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Money and other benefits, other than salary, received by a driver in a ride-sharing arrangement does not constitute income for the purpose of computing gross income under

Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-108 Local taxation and licensing.
-------------------------------------------------------------
A county or municipality may not impose a tax on, or require a license for, a ride-sharing arrangement.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-109 Wage and hour regulations unaffected by ride-sharing.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The fact that an employee participates in any kind of ride-sharing arrangement does not affect the application of any laws requiring payment of a minimum wage or overtime pay or otherwise regulating the hours a person may work.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-110 Vehicles used and drivers excluded from definitions for regulatory purposes.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-110(1): Title 41, Chapter 1a, Motor Vehicle Act; Title 41, Chapter 6a, Traffic Code A motor vehicle used in a ride-sharing arrangement is not a bus or commercial vehicle under:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-110(1)(a): Title 41, Chapter 1a, Motor Vehicle Act
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-110(1)(b): Title 41, Chapter 6a, Traffic Code
Utah Code Annotated § 72-12-110(2): Title 53, Chapter 3, Uniform Driver License Act The driver of a vehicle used in a ride-sharing arrangement is not a chauffeur and he is not transporting persons for compensation under the driver licensing provisions of

***********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Amusement Ride Safety Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(1): 72-16-204 "Account" means the Amusement Ride Safety Restricted Account created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(2)(a): "Amusement park" means a permanent indoor or outdoor facility or park where one or more amusement rides are available for use by the general public.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(2)(b): "Amusement park" does not include a traveling show, carnival, or public fairground.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3): 72-11-102
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(a): "Amusement ride" means a device or combination of devices or elements that carries or conveys one or more riders along, around, or over a fixed or restricted route or course or allows the riders to steer or guide the device within an established area for the purpose of giving the riders amusement, pleasure, thrills, or excitement.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b): 72-11-102 "Amusement ride" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(i): a coin-operated ride that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(i)(A): is manually, mechanically, or electrically operated;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(i)(B): is customarily placed in a public location; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(i)(C): does not normally require the supervision or services of an operator;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(ii): nonmechanized playground equipment, including a swing, seesaw, stationary spring-mounted animal feature, rider-propelled merry-go-round, climber, playground slide, trampoline, or physical fitness device;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(iii): an inflatable device;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(iv): a water-based recreational attraction where complete or partial immersion is intended, including a water slide, wave pool, or water park;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(v): a challenge, exercise, or obstacle course;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(vi): 72-11-102 a passenger ropeway as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(vii): a device or attraction that involves one or more live animals;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(viii): a tractor ride or wagon ride;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(ix): motion seats in a movie theater for which the manufacturer does not require a restraint; or
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(3)(b)(x): a zip line.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(4): 72-16-201 "Committee" means the Utah Amusement Ride Safety Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(5): 72-16-202 "Director" means the director of the committee, hired under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(6): "Mobile amusement ride" means an amusement ride that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(6)(a): designed or adapted to be moved from one location to another;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(6)(b): not fixed at a single location; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(6)(c): relocated at least once each calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(7): "Operator" means the individual who controls the starting, stopping, or speed of an amusement ride.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(8): "Owner-operator" means the person who has control over and responsibility for the maintenance, setup, and operation of an amusement ride.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(9): "Permanent amusement ride" means an amusement ride that is not a mobile amusement ride.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(10): "Qualified safety inspector" means an individual who holds a valid qualified safety inspector certification.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(11): 72-16-303 "Qualified safety inspector certification" means a certification issued by the director under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(12): "Reportable serious injury" means an injury to a rider that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(12)(a): occurs when there is a failure or malfunction of an amusement ride; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(12)(b): results in death, dismemberment, permanent disfigurement, permanent loss of the use of a body organ, member, function, or system, or a compound fracture.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13): 72-16-304; 72-16-304 "Safety inspection certification" means a written document that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13)(a): 72-16-304; 72-16-304 is signed by a qualified safety inspector certifying that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13)(a)(i): 72-16-304 the qualified safety inspector performed an in-person inspection of an amusement ride to check compliance with the safety standards described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13)(a)(ii): 72-16-304 at the time the qualified safety inspector performed the in-person inspection, the amusement ride:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13)(a)(ii)(A): was set up for use by the general public; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13)(a)(ii)(B): 72-16-304 satisfied the safety standards described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(13)(b): includes the date on which the qualified safety inspector performed the in-person inspection.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(14): "Serious injury" means an injury to a rider that:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(14)(a): occurs when there is a failure or malfunction of an amusement ride; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-102(14)(b): requires immediate admission to a hospital and overnight hospitalization and observation by a licensed physician.

Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-204 Amusement Ride Safety Restricted Account.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-204(1): There is created in the General Fund a restricted account known as the "Amusement Ride Safety Restricted Account."
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-204(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-204(2)(a): The account is funded from:

Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305 Insurance required.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(1): An owner-operator of an amusement ride shall carry liability insurance coverage in at least the following amounts:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(1)(a): $1,000,000 for bodily injury per occurrence;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(1)(b): $250,000 for property damage per occurrence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(1)(c): $3,000,000 annual aggregate limit.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(2): An owner-operator of an amusement ride located in an amusement park that employs more than 1,000 individuals in a calendar year shall carry liability insurance coverage in at least the following amounts:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(2)(a): $5,000,000 for bodily injury per occurrence;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(2)(b): $1,000,000 for property damage per occurrence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-305(2)(c): $10,000,000 annual aggregate limit.


Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306 Reporting and shutdown for certain injuries.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(a): An owner-operator shall report each known reportable serious injury to the director within eight hours after the owner-operator learns of the reportable serious injury.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b): (1)(a) An owner-operator shall include the following information in a report described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b)(i): the owner-operator's name and contact information;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b)(ii): the location of the amusement ride at the time the reportable serious injury occurred;
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b)(iii): a description of:
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b)(iii)(A): the amusement ride; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b)(iii)(B): the nature of the reportable serious injury; and
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(1)(b)(iv): any other information required by rule made under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(2): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(2)(a): (1) In addition to the requirement described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 72-16-306(2)(b): After a reportable serious injury, the owner-operator may not operate the mobile amusement ride until the owner-operator receives written authorization from the director or the director's designee as required by rule made in accordance with this chapter.
